Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Definition of Fatwa and Its Three Types
Definition and threefold classification of fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define fatwa according to its technical usage and distinguish its three types, identifying the scope of each.

Core Idea
Fatwa is an answer to any religious question — not only fiqh, but also creed and hadith.

This lesson addresses the fundamental definition of fatwa in Islamic jurisprudence, particularly within the Hanafi tradition. The author, Mufti Muhammad Taqi Usmani, begins with a stern warning about the gravity of issuing fatwas, then provides a nuanced definition that expands beyond mere legal rulings. He classifies fatwa into three hierarchical types, beginning with legislative fatwa from the Quran and Sunnah. Understanding this classification is crucial for recognizing the authority and scope of different fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Parse the hadith warning about fatwa
Identify the hadith cited at the beginning: 'The most daring of you in giving fatwa is the most daring of you to the Fire.' Consider what this implies about the responsibility of a mufti.
The hadith, though weak in chain, is widely accepted for its meaning.
2
Identify the definition and why 'religious' is used instead of 'legal'
The author defines fatwa as 'the answer to a religious question.' He chooses 'religious' (diniyya) over 'legal' (shar'iyya) because a mufti's scope includes creed, hadith interpretation, and other religious sciences.
3
List the three types of fatwa and their distinguishing features
The three types are: legislative fatwa (from the Lawgiver), juristic fatwa (from scholars' ijtihad), and particular fatwa (specific to a case). Note the hierarchy.
4
Examine the legislative fatwa examples from the Quran
The author cites verses where Allah uses 'yuftikum' (He gives a ruling) in response to questions about women, kalalah, and new moons. These become general law.
These verses illustrate that the highest form of fatwa is from the Quran itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أصول الإفتاء
الفتوى وخطورتها
من أحاديثه الشريفة، كما ورد في قوله عليه السلام: "أَجْرَوْكُمْ عَلَى الْفُتْيَا أَجْرَؤُكُمْ عَلَى النَّارِ " (۱) فمعنى الكلمة في اصطلاح اليوم : "الجواب عن مسئلة دينية. " وإنّما اخترنا لفظ "الدينية " ، دونَ "الشرعية " لأن المفتي لا يُجيب عن الأحكام الشرعيّة العملية فحسب، بل ربما يُجيب عن مسائل دينية اعتقادية، وعن معنى الأحاديث، وكيفية إسنادها وما إلى ذلك من المسائل التي تتعلق بالدين وعلومه.
ثمّ إنّ كلمة الفتوى والإفتاء أطلق فى كلام القوم على معانٍ ثلاثة يُمكن أن نقسمها على ثلاثة أقسام الفتوى التشريعية، والفتوى الفقهية، والفتوى الجزئية.
الفتوى التشريعية
أمّا الفتوى التشريعيّة، فهى التى صدرت من الشارع، إما بوحي متلو في القرآن الكريم أو بوحى غير متلو فى سنة النبي الكريم صلى الله عليه وسلّم فى الجواب عن سؤال، أو لبيان نازلةٍ فى عهد النبي الكريم صلى الله عليه وسلّم، فأصبحت شرعاً عاما. وذلك مثل قوله تعالى المذكور فيما سبق: وَيَسْتَفْتُونَكَ فِي النِّسَاءِ قُلِ اللَّهُ يُفْتِيكُمْ فِيهِنَّ [النساء : ۱۲۷] وقوله تعالى: يَسْتَفْتُونَكَ قُلِ اللَّهُ يُفْتِيكُمْ فِي الْكَلَلَةِ ) [النساء : ١٧٦] وقوله تعالى:  يَسْتَلُونَكَ عَنِ الْأَهِلَّةِ قُلْ هِيَ مَوَاقِيتُ لِلنَّاسِ وَالْحَقِّ ﴾ [البقرة : ۱۸۹]
(1) أخرجه الدارمي (۱:۱۷۹) عن عبيدالله ابن أبي جعفر مرسلا، وأخرجه سعيد بن منصور في باب قول عمر في الجد من سننه (١٦٤)، برقم (٥٦) عن سعيد بن المسيب مرسلا بلفظ : "أجرؤكم على قسم الجد أجرؤكم على النار " ورمز له بالصحة في الجامع الصغير وفيض القدير للمناوى ١:١٥٨، ومراسيل سعيد بن المسيب مقبولة باتفاق أهل العلم
Principles of Issuing Fatwas: The Fatwa and its Gravity. From his noble hadith, as reported in his saying, peace be upon him: 'The most daring of you in giving fatwa is the most daring of you to the Fire.' So the meaning of the word in today's terminology is: 'The answer to a religious question.' We chose the word 'religious' instead of 'legal' because the mufti does not only answer practical legal rulings, but may also answer matters of creedal belief, the meaning of hadith, their chains of transmission, and other matters related to religion and its sciences. Then, the term fatwa and ifta' has been used by scholars in three meanings that can be divided into three types: legislative fatwa, juristic fatwa, and particular fatwa. Legislative Fatwa: As for legislative fatwa, it is that which emanated from the Lawgiver, either through recited revelation in the Noble Quran or through non-recited revelation in the Sunnah of the Noble Prophet, peace be upon him, in answer to a question or to clarify an event during the era of the Noble Prophet, peace be upon him, thus becoming a general law. Such as the saying of Allah mentioned previously: 'And they ask you for a ruling concerning women. Say, Allah gives you a ruling concerning them...' [4:127], and His saying: 'They ask you for a ruling. Say, Allah gives you a ruling concerning al-kalalah...' [4:176], and His saying: 'They ask you about the new moons. Say, They are measurements of time for the people and for Hajj.' [2:189].
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage opens the discussion on the principles of ifta (issuing fatwas) by firstly emphasizing its gravity through a hadith: the more one dares to give fatwas, the more one dares toward the Fire. This is a stern warning against carelessness in fatwa. The author then defines fatwa in contemporary usage as 'the answer to a religious question.' He deliberately uses 'religious' (diniyya) rather than 'legal' (shar'iyya) because a mufti's scope is broader than practical legal rulings; it includes creed, hadith interpretation, and other religious sciences. The passage then introduces a threefold classification of fatwa: (1) legislative (tashri'iyya) – directly from the Lawgiver (Quran or Sunnah), which becomes binding law; (2) juristic (fiqhiyya); and (3) particular (juz'iyya). Only legislative fatwa is elaborated here with Quranic examples demonstrating that Allah Himself uses the verb 'yuftikum' (He gives you a ruling) in response to questions. This classification helps students understand that not all fatwas are equal in authority. Legislative fatwa is the highest source, while juristic and particular fatwas derive from it.

Key Terms
الفتوى (al-fatwa): An answer to a religious question, encompassing legal, creedal, and other religious matters.
الفتوى التشريعية (al-fatwa al-tashri'iyya): Fatwa directly from the Lawgiver (Quran or Sunnah) that becomes general law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author use the word 'دينية' (religious) instead of 'شرعية' (legal) in defining fatwa?
A) Because fatwa only deals with religious rituals, not legal transactions.
B) Because fatwa covers not only practical legal rulings but also creed and other religious topics.
C) Because 'شرعية' is a broader term that includes non-religious matters.
D) Because the author follows the Shafi'i school where fatwa is limited to legal rulings.

Key Takeaway
Fatwa is a broad religious answer, not limited to fiqh, and its highest form is legislative from Quran and Sunnah.

Distinguishing Fatwa from Qada: Scope and Binding Force
Two preserved points from a list of four differences between fatwa and qada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two preserved differences between fatwa and qada and apply them to determine which institution (mufti or qadi) handles a given scenario.

Core Idea
Fatwa is broader in scope but non-binding; qada is narrower but enforceable.

A common confusion among students is equating fatwa with qada. In this lesson, we examine two key distinctions preserved from a classical list of four. Understanding these will sharpen your ability to assign the correct legal function to each institution and appreciate the mufti's role as a non-binding advisor covering all areas of sharia, including creed and worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the function of a mufti versus a qadi
The passage states that the mufti's job is to give a ruling on a hypothetical scenario without verifying the actual facts, whereas the qadi must investigate and enforce.
The first two missing points likely addressed this factual investigation difference.
2
Analyze the third difference: scope of legal categories
Fatwa applies to all five ahkam (wajib, haram, mubah, nadb, karaha) and to validity/invalidity. Qada only applies to binding categories (wajib, haram) and not to non-binding ones like nadb (recommended) or karaha tanzihiyya (disliked).
Because qada involves compulsion, it cannot enforce merely recommended or discouraged acts.
3
Analyze the fourth difference: subject matter
Fatwa covers beliefs (aqida) and acts of worship (ibadat) directly. Qada touches these only incidentally, for example when a dispute involves a creedal matter.
A mufti may be asked about the validity of a prayer or a point of faith; a judge only deals with such matters if they are part of a litigated case.
4
Apply the distinctions to a concrete scenario
Given a scenario, decide whether it falls under fatwa or qada based on the categories and subject matter.
For example: a person asks whether a certain transaction is recommended – that's a fatwa matter. If two parties dispute over a debt, that's qada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وظيفته أن يُحقِّق صحته فى نفس الأمر بطلب البينة وغيرها. ولذلك يقول المفتى: "الحكم فى الصورة المسئول عنها كذا." ولا يلزم منه أن تكونَ الصورة المسئول عنها موافقة للواقع في نفس الأمر.
الثالث: الفتوى تجرى فيما يترتب عليه الوجوب أو الحرمة أو الإباحة أو النُّدب أو الكراهة، أو الصحة أو البطلان أما القضاء، فلا يجرى فيما يترتب عليه الندب أو الكراهة التنزيهيّة، لأنّ الندب والكراهة حث على الفعل أو الترك من غير إلزام، والقضاء إجبار والزام.
الرابع: أن الفتوى لا تقتصر على الأحكام الفقهية، بل تتعلق بالعقائد والعبادات أيضاً، والقضاء لا يتعلّق بالعقائد والعبادات إلا عن طريق التبعية.
Its function is to verify its correctness in reality by requesting evidence and other means. Therefore, the mufti says: 'The ruling in the questioned scenario is such-and-such.' And it does not necessarily follow that the questioned scenario corresponds to reality. Third: Fatwa applies to what entails obligation, prohibition, permissibility, recommendation, or dislike, or validity or invalidity. As for qada, it does not apply to what entails recommendation or disliked (tanzihi) [acts], because recommendation and dislike encourage action or abstention without compulsion, while qada is compulsion and obligation. Fourth: Fatwa is not limited to legal rulings, but also pertains to beliefs and acts of worship, whereas qada does not pertain to beliefs and acts of worship except incidentally.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage enumerates key differences between fatwa and qada (judicial verdict). Although the first two points are missing, the preserved third and fourth points are instructive. The mufti's job is to give a ruling on a hypothetical scenario without investigating the actual facts (that is the qadi's job). The third point: fatwa covers all five legal categories (wajib, haram, etc.) including non-binding ones like recommendation (nadb) and dislike (karaha tanzihiyya). Qada, however, only deals with binding rulings (such as obligation and prohibition) because a judge enforces decisions. The fourth point: fatwa extends to matters of creed and worship (e.g., explaining aqida or how to pray), while qada only touches these incidentally (e.g., when a dispute involves a creedal matter). This distinction helps a student understand that the mufti's role is broader in scope but less authoritative in enforcement than the qadi's.

Key Terms
الفتوى (al-fatwa): A non-binding legal opinion on a hypothetical scenario, covering all five categories and beliefs/worship.
القضاء (al-qada): A binding judicial verdict that resolves disputes and enforces rulings, limited to enforceable matters.
النُّدب (an-nadb): Recommended act (mustahabb) – one of the five legal categories; non-binding.
الكراهة التنزيهيّة (al-karāha at-tanzīhiyya): Disliked but not prohibited (makruh tanzihi) – non-binding category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a correct difference between fatwa and qada?
A) Fatwa applies only to binding rulings, while qada applies to all five categories.
B) Fatwa covers beliefs and worship directly, while qada does so only incidentally.
C) Qada is non-binding, while fatwa is binding.
D) Both fatwa and qada require the same factual investigation.

Key Takeaway
Fatwa is broader in scope (covering all legal categories and matters of creed and worship) but non-binding, while qada is narrower (binding categories only) but enforceable through compulsion.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Permissibility of Hypothetical Fatwas
Defends permissibility of hypothetical fatwas with hadith and reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on issuing fatwas for hypothetical events and apply the key proofs from the hadith and reasoning of al-Khatib.

Core Idea
It is permissible for a mufti to discuss hypothetical events because the Prophet's cautionary reason no longer applies after Shariah's completion.

This passage addresses a foundational rule in mufti conduct: may a mufti issue fatwas on events that have not yet occurred? Some early scholars, like Imam Malik, discouraged this out of scrupulousness. However, the later Hanafi position, supported by al-Bayhaqi, al-Halimi, and al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, permits it, especially for educational purposes. In this lesson, you will examine the two scholarly approaches, the key hadith proofs, and the operative rule for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scholarly approaches
Distinguish the early Salaf who disliked hypotheticals from later jurists who permitted them for teaching and ijtihad.
The early Salaf's view is based on tawaru' (scrupulousness), not a categorical prohibition.
2
Analyze the prophetic proofs
Examine the hadiths of Rafi' ibn Khadij (slaughtering with reeds) and the man about oppressive rulers; note how the Prophet answered hypothetical questions without disapproval.
These hadiths show the Prophet engaging with future-oriented questions.
3
Understand the reasoning for permissibility
Al-Khatib argues that the Prophet's earlier dislike was out of compassion, fearing questions could lead to hardship by causing prohibitions. After the Shariah's completion, this concern no longer exists.
The reasoning hinges on the change in context: the Prophet was the legislator; after him, no new prohibitions can be introduced by questioning.
4
Apply the rule to mufti practice
Recognize that discussing hypotheticals is allowed for educational and guidance purposes, and for compiling fiqh, as long as it is not presented as binding action unless the event actually occurs.
Al-Halimi restricts this to the mutafaqqihah (students of ijtihad), for training purposes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأخرج عن مالك ، قال : " أدركت هذه البلدة وإنهم ليكرهون هذا الإكثار الذي فيه اليوم، يريد المسائل (1) الفقهاء الذين أفتوا فى المسائل التى لم تقع، وحجتهم
أما القسم الثانى من العلماء هم الذين نَصَبوا أنفسهم لبيان الأحكام الفقهية وتدوينها بما يُيَسِّرُ لمن جاء بعدهم الوقوف عليها عند الحاجة، فتكلموا في المسائل المحتملة التي لم تقع بعد وحمَلُوا ماذكرنا من آثار الصحابة والتابعين على التورّع والاحتياط. فقال البيهقى رحمه الله تعالى يعد نقل هذه (۲) الآثار: وبلغنى عن أبي عبد الله الحليمي رحمه الله أنه أباح ذلك للمتفقهة الذين غرض العالم من جوابهم تنبيههم وإرشادهم إلى طريق النظر والإرشاد، لا ليعملوا " ثمّ قال الإمام البيهقى: " وعلى هذا الوجهِ  َوضعَ الفقهاء مسائل المجتهدات، وأجروا بآراءهم فيها لما في ذلك من إرشاد (۳) ۹۹ المتفقهة، وتنبيههم على كيفية الاجتهاد. وقال الخطيب بعد رواية آثار الصحابة والتابعين: " فهذا ما تعلّق به مَن مَنَع من الكلام فى الحوادثِ قبل نزولها ، ونحن نجيب عنه بمشيئة الله وعونه : أما كراهة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المسائل، فإنما كان ذلك إشفاقاً على أمته ورأفة بها ، وتحتناً عليها، وتخوفاً أن يُحرم الله عند سؤال سائل أمراً كان مباحاً قبل سؤاله عنه ، فيكون السؤال سبباً فى حظر ما كان للأمة منفعة فى إباحته ، فتدخل بذلك المشقة عليهم والإضرار بهم. وهذا المعنى قد ارتفع بموتِ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، واستقرت أحكام الشريعة ، فلا حاظر ولا مبيح بعده. " ثم استدل الخطيب رحمه الله تعالى على جواز السؤال عما لم يكُن بحديث رافع بن خدیج رضى الله تعالى عنه قال : قلت : "يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ، إِنَّا نَخَافُ أَنْ نَلْقَى العَدُو غَدًا ، وَلَيْسَ مَعَنَا مُدَى ، فَنَدْبَحُ بِالْقَصَبِ؟ فَقَالَ رَسُوْلَ اللهِ صَلَّى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ : "مَا أَنْهَرَ الدَّمَ وَذَكَرْتَ عَلَيْهِ اسْمَ اللَّهِ فَكُلْ، مَا خَلَاَ السِنَّ وَالظُّفْرَ." فلم يعب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مسألة رافع عمّا لم ينزل به ، لأنه قال: غدا ولم يقل له: لِمَ سألت عن شيء لم يكن بعد. وكذلك استدل الخطيب بحديث يزيد بن سلمة ، عن أبيه أنَّ رَجُلاً قَامَ إِلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، فَقَالَ : يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ! أَرَأَيْتَ لَوْ كَانَ عَلَيْنَا أُمَرَاءُ يَسْأَلُونَا الْحَقَّ وَيَمْنَعُونَا حَقَّنَا ، فَتُقَاتِلُهُمْ؟ فَقَامَ الْأَشْعَثُ بْنُ قَيْسٍ ، فَقَالَ : تَسْأَلُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَنْ أَمْرٍ لَمْ يَحْدِثُ بَعْد؟ فَقَالَ: لَأَسْأَلُنَّهُ حَتَّى يَمْنَعَنِي ، فَقَالَ : يَا رَسُوْلَ اللهِ! أَرَأَيْتَ لَوْ كَانَ عَلَيْنَا أُمَرَاءُ يَسْأَلُونَا الْحَقَّ وَيَمْنَعُونَا أَنْقَاتِلُهُمْ ؟ قَالَ : "لا! عَلَيْكُمْ مَا حُمِّلْتُمْ وَعَلَيْهِمْ مَا حُمِّلُوا (۱) قال الخطيب رحمه الله تعالى: "فلم يمنع رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلّم هذا الرجل من مسألته ، ولا أنكرها عليه ، بل أجابه عنها من غير كراهة، وفي الآثار نظائر
And it is narrated from Malik that he said: 'I came upon this city, and they indeed dislike this abundance which is present today, meaning the issues [of] the jurists who issued fatwas on matters that had not occurred.' Their proof: As for the second group of scholars, those who dedicated themselves to explaining fiqh rulings and compiling them in a way that facilitates for those after them to refer to them when needed, they spoke about potential matters that had not yet occurred and interpreted what we mentioned of the effects of the Companions and Followers as scrupulousness and caution. Al-Bayhaqi, may Allah have mercy on him, said after narrating these effects: 'It reached me from Abu Abdullah al-Halimi, may Allah have mercy on him, that he permitted that for the students of fiqh, for whom the purpose of the scholar's answer is to alert them and guide them to the path of reflection and guidance, not for them to act upon it.' Then Imam al-Bayhaqi said: 'And in this way, the jurists laid down the issues of ijtihad, and they used their opinions in them because of what is in that of guidance for the students of fiqh and alerting them to the method of ijtihad.' And al-Khatib said, after narrating the effects of the Companions and Followers: 'This is what those who forbade speaking about events before their occurrence adhere to. And we will answer it, by the will and assistance of Allah: As for the dislike of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, of questions, that was only out of compassion for his Ummah and mercy upon them, and out of fear that Allah would prohibit something that was permissible before it was asked about, such that the question would become the cause of prohibition of something in whose permissibility there was benefit for the Ummah, thus hardship and harm would enter upon them. And this meaning has been lifted with the death of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and the rulings of the Shariah have become settled; there is no prohibitor nor permitter after him.' Then al-Khatib, may Allah have mercy on him, used as evidence for the permissibility of asking about what has not been, the hadith of Rafi' ibn Khadij, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: 'I said: O Messenger of Allah, we fear that we will meet the enemy tomorrow, and we do not have knives with us, so can we slaughter with reeds? The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: Whatever makes the blood flow and you mention the name of Allah over it, eat, except teeth and nails.' So the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, did not disapprove of Rafi''s question about something that had not befallen him, because he said 'tomorrow' and did not say to him: 'Why did you ask about something that has not yet happened?' And similarly, al-Khatib used as evidence the hadith of Yazid ibn Salamah, from his father, that a man stood before the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, what do you think if there are rulers over us who ask us for what is rightfully theirs and deny us our right, should we fight them?' Then al-Ash'ath ibn Qays stood and said: 'Do you ask the Messenger of Allah about something that has not yet happened?' He said: 'I will ask him until he prevents me.' So he said: 'O Messenger of Allah, what do you think if there are rulers over us who ask us for what is rightfully theirs and deny us our right, should we fight them?' He said: 'No! You have what you are charged with, and they have what they are charged with.' Al-Khatib, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'So the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, did not prevent this man from his question, nor did he disapprove of it, but rather answered him without dislike. And there are similar examples in the reports.'
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage addresses a methodological rule in ifta: whether a mufti may issue fatwas on hypothetical events that have not yet occurred. The text presents two scholarly approaches: (1) the early Salaf, including Imam Malik, who disliked dealing with hypothetical questions, and (2) later jurists who compiled fiqh and discussed potential issues. The Hanafi position aligns with the second group, as the text goes on to defend this view. The defense relies on arguments from al-Bayhaqi, al-Halimi, and al-Khatib al-Baghdadi. Al-Halimi permits it for students of fiqh as a teaching tool, not for action. Al-Bayhaqi confirms that jurists set down hypothetical ijtihad issues for guidance. Al-Khatib addresses the hadith evidence: the Prophet's dislike of questions was due to fear of causing hardship, but after his death, the Shariah is complete, so no such fear remains. He then cites hadiths where the Prophet answered questions about future hypothetical situations (Rafi' ibn Khadij about slaughtering with reeds, and the man about oppressive rulers), showing that the Prophet did not condemn such questions. The passage thus establishes the rasm rule: it is permissible for a mufti to discuss and issue fatwas on hypothetical events, especially for educational purposes, provided he does not present them as binding for action unless they occur.

Key Terms
المسائل التي لم تقع (al-masa'il allati lam taqa'): Hypothetical legal issues that have not yet occurred in reality.
التورّع والاحتياط (al-tawaru' wa al-ihtiyat): Scrupulousness and caution, used to explain why early scholars avoided hypotheticals.
المتفقهة (al-mutafaqqihah): Students of fiqh learning the methodology of ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in this passage, why is it permissible to issue fatwas on hypothetical events that have not occurred?
A) Because the Prophet explicitly permitted such questions.
B) Because the reason for the Prophet's dislike (fear of causing hardship) no longer exists after the completion of the Shariah.
C) Because the early Salaf changed their opinion after the Prophet's death.
D) Because hypothetical questions are always necessary for the Ummah.

Key Takeaway
It is permissible for a mufti to discuss hypothetical events for educational and guidance purposes because the Prophet's cautionary reason has ceased with the completion of Shariah.

Defense of Ahl al-Ra'y and Imam Abu Hanifa
Explains the term Ahl al-Ra'y and defends Abu Hanifa against critics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi definition of Ahl al-Ra'y to distinguish between general and technical usage and evaluate the legitimacy of Abu Hanifa's ijtihad in fatwa.

Core Idea
Ahl al-Ra'y is not a pejorative; every mujtahid uses ra'y, and Abu Hanifa's departures from hadith are rewarded ijtihad, not obstinacy.

The term 'Ahl al-Ra'y' has been used historically to label the Hanafi school, sometimes with negative connotations. This passage clarifies that the term applies broadly to all mujtahids, but technically denotes the Kufan school. It then defends Abu Hanifa against the charge of opposing hadith arbitrarily, emphasizing that his ijtihad is based on clear proofs and carries reward even if mistaken.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two uses of 'Ahl al-Ra'y'
Notice that the author distinguishes between a general sense (all mujtahids use ra'y) and a technical sense (specifically the Iraqi, Kufan school).
This distinction is crucial to avoid misusing the term.
2
Recognize the criticism against Abu Hanifa
The passage notes that some early scholars criticized Abu Hanifa for departing from the apparent meaning of certain hadiths.
This criticism is the context for the defense.
3
Summarize the author's defense arguments
The author provides multiple arguments: Abu Hanifa did not oppose out of obstinacy but based on clear proofs; a mujtahid is rewarded even if wrong; critics are either envious or ignorant; and Imam Ahmad praised him.
List each argument mentally for comprehension.
4
Assess the authority of the defense
Note the citation of Imam Ahmad's praise, which adds weight to the defense, and the author's own declaration of Abu Hanifa's innocence.
This shows the defense is grounded in established scholarly opinion.
5
Link to fatwa practice
Understand that this defense underpins the validity of Hanafi fatwas: even when they depart from apparent hadith, they are legitimate ijtihad.
A mufti can rely on this principle when issuing fatwas.

Know that the term 'people of opinion' (Ahl al-Ra'y), in terms of attribution to them, includes everyone who uses opinion in legal rulings, thus it includes all scholars of Islam, because every mujtahid cannot do without consideration and opinion in his ijtihad, even if only in verifying the effective cause and refining it, about the correctness of which there is no dispute. As for its technical meaning, it was, in the usage of the early generations, a title for the people of Iraq, and they are the people of Kufa: Abu Hanifa and those who followed him. Then he mentioned some aspects in which the Hanafis left the apparent meaning of some hadiths, and the criticism leveled by some scholars against him because of that. Then he said: 'The criticism against him from the early imams increased, to the point that they went to extremes, and the soul does not delight in mentioning it. But Allah refused except to protect him from what they said, and to declare him innocent of what they attributed to him. The summary of the matter is: He definitely did not oppose the Sunnah out of obstinacy; rather, he opposed in what he opposed out of ijtihad due to clear proofs and manifest valid evidence. His arguments are present among people, and rarely do his opponents get justice from them. If he errs, he has one reward; if he is correct, he has two rewards. Those who criticize him are either envious or ignorant of the positions of ijtihad. The latest confirmed report from Imam Ahmad (may Allah be pleased with him) is his good speech about him and praise of him. Abu al-Ward from our companions mentioned it in the book 'Usul al-Din.' And Allah, the Exalted, knows best what is correct.'

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the Hanafi school's methodology. The author first clarifies that 'Ahl al-Ra'y' as a general term applies to all mujtahids, but historically it became a specific title for the Iraqi school led by Abu Hanifa. He then addresses the criticism that Hanafis sometimes departed from the apparent meaning of hadiths, explaining that this was not out of stubbornness but based on valid ijtihad. He defends Abu Hanifa by stating that his arguments are clear, and that his critics are either envious or ignorant. He cites Imam Ahmad's eventual praise of Abu Hanifa as evidence of his integrity. This lesson emphasizes that disagreement with some hadiths is a legitimate form of ijtihad, and the mujtahid is rewarded even if mistaken.

Key Terms
أهل الرأي (Ahl al-Ra'y): Technically, the Hanafi school of Iraq; generally, any mujtahid using opinion
أصحاب الرأي (Ashab al-Ra'y): Synonym for Ahl al-Ra'y

The Obligation of Taqlid of a Specific Madhhab
Historical and legal analysis of taqlid obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why taqlid of one of the four madhhabs is obligatory for a non-mujtahid and identify the historical conditions that made it so.

Core Idea
Taqlid of a specific madhhab became obligatory only when the capacity for ijtihad diminished and only the four madhhabs remained reliably transmitted.

In the early centuries, communities had mujtahids, so taqlid of a specific madhhab was not required. Over time, as the ability for independent ijtihad dwindled, the Ummah found itself reliant on the four codified madhhabs. This lesson traces that historical shift and establishes the contemporary obligation for non-mujtahids to adhere to one of these four schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the historical change
The passage states that in the first two centuries, scholars were not united on taqlid of one specific madhhab. After the second century, tamadhdhub (adopting a specific madhhab) became widespread and eventually obligatory.
This is not a change in Shari'ah but a change in circumstances affecting obligation.
2
Understand the principle of original obligation
The original obligation is the existence of mujtahids who derive rulings from detailed proofs. The prerequisite of that obligation is obligatory – so if multiple ways to fulfill it exist, any suffices; if only one remains, that one becomes obligatory.
This is a usul principle: ما لا يتم الواجب إلا به فهو واجب.
3
Apply the principle to taqlid
When ijtihad was widespread, following any mujtahid was sufficient. When only the four madhhabs were systematically preserved and transmitted mutawatir, following them became the only viable path, hence obligatory.
The passage emphasizes that other madhhabs were not compiled comprehensively.
4
Recognize the uniqueness of the four madhhabs
The four madhhabs were codified, verified by many students, and attributed to their founders with certainty. This did not happen for other imams or companions.
Imam al-Nawawi explains that companions did not have time to codify their rulings.
5
Conclude the ruling
Therefore, for a non-mujtahid today, it is wajib (obligatory) to follow one of the four madhhabs and not to follow any other madhhab or personal opinion.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school and agreed upon by the later scholars.

Source Text

Principles of Issuing Fatwa: The Methods of Fatwa among the Predecessors. In the first and second centuries [AH], they were not united upon taqlid of one specific madhhab. After the second century, adopting a specific madhhab of individual mujtahids appeared among them, and few did not rely on the madhhab of a specific mujtahid. This was the obligatory (wajib) at that time. If you say: How can one thing be non-obligatory at one time and obligatory at another, even though the Shari'ah is one? I say: The original obligation is that there be in the Ummah those who know the subsidiary rulings from their detailed proofs. The people of truth are agreed upon that, and the prerequisite of the obligatory is obligatory. So if there are multiple paths to the obligatory, it is obligatory to attain one of those paths without specification. And if only one path becomes specific, then that specific path becomes obligatory... Upon this, one should analogize that the obligation of taqlid of a specific imam follows; it may be obligatory and may not be obligatory. (1) He said elsewhere: "Indeed these four codified and verified madhhabs, the Ummah - or those among it considered reliable - have agreed upon the permissibility of taqlid of them until this day of ours. In that are benefits that are not hidden, especially in these days when aspirations have become very short, souls have drunk in desires, and every person with an opinion has been impressed with his own opinion. Despite the fact that mujtahid jurists were abundant in every Muslim region, it was the will of Allah that their madhhabs were not comprehensively codified as the madhhabs of the four jurists were codified, and their attribution to them became mutawatir, and their students who studied them and examined them thoroughly and derived subsidiary rulings from them multiplied, and such was not attained for other madhhabs." Sheikh Waliullah al-Dahlawi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (1) al-Insaf fi Bayan Asbab al-Ikhtilaf p. 68-70 (2) (2) Hujjat Allah al-Baligha vol. 1 p. 442, chapter on the narrative of people before the fourth century and after it. "And in summary, adopting a specific madhhab of the mujtahids is a secret that Allah instilled in the scholars and united them upon, whether they feel it or not." (1) 99 From here the scholars said: It is obligatory for the non-mujtahid to follow one of these four madhhabs, and not to follow a madhhab besides them. Imam al-Nawawi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: "It is not permissible for him to adopt the madhhab of any of the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) or others among the early generations, even though they were more knowledgeable and higher in rank than those after them, because they were not free to devote themselves to codifying knowledge and compiling its principles and branches, so none of them has a refined, verified, and established madhhab. Rather, that was undertaken by those who came after them from the imams who drew from the madhhabs of the Companions and Followers, who undertook to prepare rulings for events before their occurrence, and rose to clarify their principles and branches, like Malik and Abu Hanifah and others." (2) 99 (3) Al-Munawi related from al-Hafiz al-Dhahabi (may Allah have mercy on them) that he said: "It is obligatory upon us to believe that the four imams, and al-Sufyanayn, al-Awza'i, Dawud al-Zahiri, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, and all the imams are upon guidance, and no attention is paid to those who speak against them, including..." (1) al-Insaf p.73 (2) al-Majmu' Sharh al-Muhadhdhab, introduction, chapter on the manners of the mustafti - (1/55) (3) Imam Dawud al-Zahiri: He is Dawud ibn Ali ibn Khalaf al-Isbahani, Abu Sulayman, nicknamed al-Zahiri: one of the mujtahid imams in Islam, to whom the Zahiri sect is attributed, named so for taking the apparent meaning of the Book and Sunnah and refraining from interpretation, opinion, and analogy. Dawud was the first to declare this view. He was born in Kufa in 201 AH. He was originally from Isfahan, from the people of Qashan a town near Isfahan. Then he resided in Baghdad, and the leadership of knowledge there ended with him. He died in Baghdad in 270 AH. (Summarized from al-A'lam 2/333, and see al-Fihrist by Ibn al-Nadim p. 272 for details on his works.)
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is a methodological discussion on the history and obligation of taqlid. It begins by describing the first two Islamic centuries, during which scholars were not united on following one specific madhhab. After the second century, adopting a specific madhhab became common and eventually obligatory. The author (Shah Waliullah Dehlawi, as quoted) clarifies that the original obligation is that there be mujtahids in the community. When no single path to ijtihad exists for everyone, it suffices to follow any valid path. However, when only one path remains reliable, it becomes obligatory. The passage then explains why only the four madhhabs (Hanafi, Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) are suitable for taqlid: their teachings were comprehensively compiled, mutawatir in transmission, and thoroughly studied by many scholars, unlike other madhhabs. Imam al-Nawawi is cited to emphasize that one cannot follow a Companion's madhhab because they did not systematically compile their rulings. The passage concludes with a quote from al-Dhahabi affirming the guidance of all imams but implying the primacy of the four. This establishes the rasm (rule) that a non-mujtahid must follow one of the four recognized madhhabs.

Key Terms
تَمَذْهَب (tamadhhub): The act of adopting a specific madhhab (school of law) of a mujtahid imam.
تَقْلِيد (taqlid): Following the legal opinion of a mujtahid without knowing the detailed evidence.
مُجْتَهِد (mujtahid): One who has the capability to derive rulings from the primary sources independently.
غَيْر مُجْتَهِد (ghayr mujtahid): One who does not meet the conditions for ijtihad and must follow a mujtahid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because Companions were less knowledgeable than later imams.
B) Because Companions did not codify their rulings systematically, so they lack a refined, verified madhhab.
C) Because the Companions forbade taqlid of themselves.
D) Because there is no transmission of their rulings at all.

Key Takeaway
A non-mujtahid must follow one of the four codified madhhabs, as they alone are systematically preserved and verified by the Ummah.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Obligation to Follow One of the Four Madhahib for Non-Mujtahids
Explains the necessity of taqlid of the four madhahib and prohibition of following non-codified madhahib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the ruling regarding taqlid for non-mujtahids and explain why following non-codified madhahib (like those of the Sahaba) is prohibited.

Core Idea
A non-mujtahid must follow a codified madhhab; following the Sahaba directly is not permitted.

This lesson addresses a fundamental principle in Hanafi ifta: the obligation for non-mujtahids to adhere to one of the four established Sunni schools. The passage argues that, although the Companions were superior in knowledge, their rulings were not systematically compiled and refined, making their individual opinions unsuitable for direct taqlid. Instead, the later imams (Abu Hanifa, Malik, etc.) undertook the task of codifying and verifying Islamic law, producing structured madhahib that are reliable for the masses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Main Ruling
Locate the central ruling: it is obligatory (wajib) for a non-mujtahid to follow one of the four madhahib and prohibited to follow any other madhhab.
The text states 'يجب لغير المجتهد أن يقلد أحد هذه المذاهب الأربعة'.
2
Understand the Prohibition of Following Non-Codified Madhahib
The passage explicitly forbids adopting the madhhab of a Sahabi or any early imam whose rulings were not codified. Look for Imam al-Nawawi's explanation.
Key phrase: 'ليس له التمذهب بمذهب أحد من أئمة الصحابة'.
3
Analyze the Rationale (Codification vs. Non-Codification)
The Companions did not systematically record their legal principles and branches. Later imams refined and corrected the rulings, creating a muharrar (refined) and muqarrar (settled) madhhab.
The text contrasts 'لم يتفرغوا لتدوين العلم' with 'قام بذلك من جاء بعدهم'.
4
Examine the Supporting Evidence
The passage cites several authorities: al-Nawawi, al-Dhahabi, al-Razi (who reports ijma'), and al-Dahlawi. Identify their arguments and note the consensus claim.
Al-Razi: 'نقل الإمام الرازي إجماع المحققين على منع العوام من تقليد أعيان الصحابة'.
5
Apply the Rule to a Geographic Context
Shah Waliullah al-Dahlawi gives an example: in India or Transoxiana where only Hanafi scholars exist, one must follow the Hanafi madhhab and cannot leave it. This illustrates the practical operation of the rule.
This shows that the obligation is not abstract but depends on availability and necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و بالجملة، فالتَّمَذهب للمجتهدين سر ألهمه الله تعالى العلماء و جَمَعهم عليه من حيث يشعرون أولا يشعرون . ومن هنا قال العلماء: إنّه يجب لغير المجتهد أن يُقلّد أحد هذه المذاهب الأربعة، وأن لا يُقلّد مذهباً سواها. قال الإمام النووي رحمه الله تعالى: " وليس له التمذهب بمذهب أحدٍ من أئمّةِ الصحابة رضى الله عنهم وغيرهم من الأولين، وإن كانوا أعلم وأعلى درجة ممّن بعدهم، لأنهم لم يتفرغوا لتدوين العلم وضبط أصوله وفروعه فليس لأحدٍ منهم مذهب مهذب محرّر مقرر. وإنما قام بذلك من جاء بعدهم من الأئمة الناحلين لمذاهب الصحابة والتابعين القائمين بتمهيد أحكام الوقائع قبل وقوعها، الناهضين بإيضاح أصولها وفروعها، كمالك وأبي حنيفة وغيرهما." ونقل المُناوى عن الحافظ الذهبي رحمهما الله تعالى أنه قال: "ويجب علينا أن نعتقد أنّ الأئمة الأربعة والسفيانين والأوزاعي وداود الظاهري وإسحاق بن راهويه وسائر الأئمة على هدى، ولا التفات لمن تكلم فيهم بما هم بريئون منه، والصحيح وفاقاً للجمهور أنّ المُصيب في الفروع واحد، والله تعالى فيما حكم عليه أمارة، وأن المجتهد كُلف بإصابته، وأن مُخطِئه لا يأثم، بل يؤجر. فمن أصاب فله أجران، ومن أخطأ فأجر. نعم! إن قصر المجتهد أثم اتفاقاً، وعلى غير المجتهد أن يقلد مذهباً معيناً ... لكن لا يجوز تقليد الصحابة وكذا التابعين، كما قاله إمام الحرمين من كل من لم يدوّن مذهبه فيمتنع تقليد غير الأربعة في القضاء والافتاء. لأن المذاهب الأربعة انتشرت وتحرّرت حتى ظهر تقييد مطلقها وتخصيص عامها، بخلاف غيرهم لانقراض أتباعهم. وقد نقل الإمام الرازي رحمه الله تعالى إجماع المحققين على منع العوام من تقليد أعيان الصحابة وأكابرهم. وقال الشيخ ولى الله الدهلوی رحمه الله تعالى في موضع آخر. " إعلم أنّ في الأخذ بهذه المذاهب الأربعةِ مصلحة عظيمة، وفي الإعراض عنها كلها مفسدة كبيرة، ونحن نبيّن ذلك بوجوه... وقال في موضع آخر: "فإذا كان إنسان جاهل في بلاد الهند أو في بلاد ما وراء النهر، وليس هناك عالم شافعي ولا مالكي ولا حنبلي، ولاكتاب من كتب هذه المذاهب، وجب عليه أن يقلّد لمذهب أبي حنيفة، ويحرم عليه أن يخرج من مذهبه، لأنه حينئذ يَخْلَعُ رِبْقَة الشريعة، ويبقى سُدى مُهملاً، بخلاف ما إذا كان في الحرمين، فإنه متيسر له هناك معرفة جميع المذاهب، ولا يكفيه أن يأخذ بالظن من غير ثقة، ولا أن يأخذ من ألسنة العوام، ولا أن يأخذ من كتاب غير مشهور، كما ذكر كل ذلك في النّهر الفائق شرح كنز الدقائق.
In short, adherence to a madhhab for the mujtahids is a secret that Allah the Exalted inspired into the scholars and brought them together upon it, whether they feel it or not. From here, the scholars have said: It is obligatory for a non-mujtahid to follow one of these four madhahib, and not to follow any madhhab besides them. Imam al-Nawawi, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'It is not permissible for him to adopt the madhhab of any of the imams among the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, nor of others from the early generations, even though they were more knowledgeable and of a higher rank than those after them, because they did not devote themselves to codifying knowledge and recording its principles and branches. So none of them has a refined, corrected, and determined madhhab. Rather, that was undertaken by those who came after them from the imams who extracted from the madhahib of the Companions and Followers, and who were responsible for preparing the rulings of events before they occurred, and who arose to clarify their principles and branches, such as Malik, Abu Hanifah, and others.' And al-Munawi narrated from al-Hafiz al-Dhahabi, may Allah have mercy on them both, that he said: 'We must believe that the four imams, and Sufyan al-Thawri, al-Awza'i, Dawud al-Zahiri, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, and the rest of the imams are upon guidance, and no attention is paid to those who speak about them with what they are innocent of. The correct view, in agreement with the majority, is that the one who is correct in subsidiary matters is one, and Allah the Exalted has established an indicator for what He has ruled; and that the mujtahid is required to be correct, and the one who errs does not sin but rather is rewarded. So whoever is correct receives two rewards, and whoever errs receives one reward. Indeed! If the mujtahid is negligent, he sins by agreement. And the non-mujtahid must follow a specific madhhab... but it is not permissible to follow the Companions, nor likewise the Followers, as stated by the Imam of the Two Sanctuaries (al-Juwayni) regarding anyone whose madhhab was not recorded. Thus, following other than the four in judgment and issuing fatwa is prohibited, because the four madhahib have spread and become refined so that the restriction of their absolute statements and the specification of their general statements have become apparent, unlike others due to the extinction of their followers. Imam al-Razi, may Allah have mercy on him, transmitted the consensus of the verifying scholars on prohibiting the common people from following the prominent Companions and their great ones. And Shaykh Waliyyullah al-Dahlawi, may Allah have mercy on him, said elsewhere: 'Know that in adhering to these four madhahib there is a great benefit, and in turning away from all of them there is a great corruption, and we will explain that with various aspects...' And he said elsewhere: 'If a person is ignorant in the land of India or in the land beyond the river (Transoxiana), and there is no Shafi'i, Maliki, or Hanbali scholar there, nor any books of these madhahib, then he must follow the madhhab of Abu Hanifah, and it is forbidden for him to leave his madhhab, because in that case he would remove the bond of Sharia, and remain aimless and neglected, contrary to the situation if he is in the Two Sanctuaries (Mecca and Medina), for there it is easy for him to gain knowledge of all the madhahib. However, it is not sufficient for him to act upon conjecture from an unreliable source, nor to take from the tongues of common people, nor to take from an obscure book, as all this is mentioned in al-Nahr al-Fa'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq.'
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage opens with a statement that the adherence (tamadhhab) of the mujtahids to one of the established schools is a secret that Allah inspired in the scholars, bringing them together even if they are unaware of it. From this principle, the scholars derive the ruling that it is obligatory for a non-mujtahid to follow one of the four established madhahib and not to follow any madhhab beyond them. The passage then quotes Imam al-Nawawi explaining why one cannot follow the companions: because they did not dedicate themselves to codifying their knowledge and recording the principles and branches of their madhhab. Thus, there is no fully refined, verified, and determined madhhab from them. The task was carried out by later imams who extracted from the companions and followers and prepared rulings for events before they occurred. Al-Nawawi also cites al-Munawi and al-Dhahabi stating that we must believe that the four imams and others like Sufyan al-Thawri, al-Awza'i, Dawud al-Zahiri, and others are all on guidance. The correct view is that the mujtahid who errs is not sinful, but rather rewarded, and the one who is correct has two rewards. However, if the mujtahid is negligent, he is sinful by consensus. The non-mujtahid must follow a specific madhhab. It is not allowed to follow the companions or their followers because their madhhab was not recorded. Imam al-Razi transmitted the consensus of the verifying scholars on prohibiting the laypeople from following the notable companions. Finally, Shah Waliullah al-Dehlawi emphasizes the great benefit in adhering to the four madhahib and the great harm in turning away from them entirely. He gives a ruling for someone in India or Transoxiana who does not have scholars from other madhahib: they must follow the Hanafi madhhab and it is forbidden to leave it, because that would remove the bond of sharia. This differs from someone in the Haramayn who has access to all madhahib. However, even there, one cannot act on mere conjecture from unreliable sources.

Key Terms
تمذهب (tamadhhab): Adherence to a specific madhhab (school of law) as a consistent methodology.
تقليد (taqlid): Following the ruling of a mujtahid without demanding evidence.
المذاهب الأربعة (al-madhahib al-arba'ah): The four established Sunni schools: Hanafi, Maliki, Shafi'i, and Hanbali.
محرر (muharrar): Refined and corrected (i.e., the rulings have been thoroughly checked and established).
مقرر (muqarrar): Determined and settled (i.e., the principles and branches are firmly established).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Sahaba were not mujtahids.
B) Because the Sahaba did not codify their madhhab into a systematic school.
C) Because the Sahaba allowed following others.
D) Because the later imams are more knowledgeable than the Sahaba.

Key Takeaway
It is wajib for a non-mujtahid to follow one of the four codified madhahib, and it is not permissible to follow the uncodified opinions of the Companions.

The Instrumental Nature of Taqlid
Quoting Imam Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi on the instrumental nature of taqlid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Imam Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi's view that taqlid is not inherently obligatory but is a means to prevent disorder, and apply this understanding to contemporary fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Taqlid is not a command; it is a tool for religious order.

Many Muslims assume that following a specific madhhab is a religious duty. However, Imam Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi offers a more nuanced perspective: taqlid is not an end in itself but a practical measure to avoid chaos and ensure consistency in applying Islamic law. This distinction is crucial for muftis who must understand the scope and purpose of madhhab adherence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central claim
Read the quote carefully and note that al-Tahanawi explicitly denies that taqlid is fard or wajib in itself. Look for the phrasing 'لَسْنَا نَعْتَقِدُ أَنَّ التَّقْلِيدَ الشَّخْصِيَّ فَرْضٌ أَوْ وَاجِبٌ فِي نَفْسِهِ'.
The negation is emphatic and deliberate.
2
Recognize the justification
Identify why taqlid is recommended: it organizes religious affairs (ينتظم به أمور الدين) and prevents chaos (فَوْضَوِيّة). This is an instrumental, not intrinsic, justification.
The key Arabic terms: انتظام (order) and فوضوية (chaos).
3
Understand the practical implication for a mufti
A mufti should not present taqlid as a strict religious obligation. Instead, he should explain its role as a means for preserving consistency and preventing arbitrary rulings. This affects how fatwas are given, especially to laypersons.
This aligns with the principle that necessities are measured by their purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مناهج الفتوى في السلف

"إن تقليد مذهب معين ليس حكماً شرعيا فى نفسه، ولكنه فتوى أصدرت لتنتظم به أمور الدين."
قال الإمام الشيخ أشرف على التهانوى رحمه الله تعالى في بعض مواعظه: "ہم تقلید شخصی کو فی نفسہ فرض یا واجب نہیں کہتے، بلکہ یوں کہتے ہیں کہ شخصی میں دین کا انتظام ہوتا ہے اور ترک تقلید میں بے انتظامی ہوتی ہے۔"
"فنحن لا نعتقد أنّ التقليد الشخصى فرض أو واجب في نفسه، بل نقول إن التقليد الشخصى ينتظم به أمور الدين، وفي ترك التقليد فَوْضَوِيّة"
Methodologies of Fatwa among the Predecessors: "Indeed, following a specific madhhab is not in itself a legal ruling, but rather a fatwa that was issued so that matters of religion become organized." Imam Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi said in some of his exhortations: "We do not say that individual taqlid is in itself obligatory or required, but rather we say that through individual taqlid, religious affairs become organized, and abandoning taqlid leads to disorder." "So we do not believe that individual taqlid is obligatory or required in itself, but rather we say that through individual taqlid, religious affairs become organized, and in abandoning taqlid there is chaos."
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage presents a key principle in the methodology of issuing fatwas: the status of taqlid (following a specific madhhab). The author quotes Imam Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi, a leading Hanafi scholar from the Indian subcontinent, to clarify that adherence to a particular madhhab is not an inherent religious obligation (fard or wajib). Instead, it is a practical measure (a 'fatwa' issued) to bring order to religious practice. The quote emphasizes the utilitarian purpose: taqlid prevents chaos (fawdawiyyah) by providing a structured framework for deriving and applying Islamic law. The passage underscores the difference between intrinsic obligation and instrumental necessity. This is crucial for a mufti to understand: while taqlid is not commanded in itself, it is indispensable for maintaining consistency and preventing arbitrary rulings.

Key Terms
التقليد الشخصى (al-taqlid al-shakhsi): Following a specific madhhab (school of law) in all rulings, as opposed to non-commitment or eclectic selection.
فَوْضَوِيّة (fawḍawiyyah): Chaos, disorder; the state of lacking a systematic approach in religious practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is a divine command explicitly mentioned in the Quran.
B) It is necessary to avoid chaos and maintain order in religious affairs.
C) It is the only way to attain salvation.
D) It is a fundamental article of faith.

Key Takeaway
Taqlid is an instrumental necessity for maintaining order in religious practice, not an intrinsic religious obligation.

Non-Personal Taqlid for the Secure Scholar
Ruling on non-personal taqlid for a secure scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which non-personal taqlid is permissible for a scholar and apply the fatwa hierarchy to evaluate its permissibility.

Core Idea
A scholar safe from desire and public disturbance may adopt the strongest evidence from any madhhab.

This lesson addresses a key question in Hanafi ifta: when is it allowed for a scholar to depart from his own madhhab's preferred view? The passage from Shaykh Rashid Ahmad al-Kankohi clarifies that non-personal taqlid is not absolutely prohibited; it is conditionally permissible for those who are secure from fitna. Understanding this ruling helps muftis balance adherence to the madhhab with the search for the strongest evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the overall hukm on non-personal taqlid for a scholar as given in the passage.
The ruling is that it is permissible under conditions.
2
Extract the conditions
List the two conditions that must be met for permissibility: security from following desire and no public disturbance.
These conditions prevent the evils that the fuqaha sought to avoid.
3
Understand the rationale
Explain why the fuqaha prohibited non-personal taqlid for laymen but allowed it for scholars under these conditions.
The prohibition was to prevent fitna, which is more likely among laymen.
4
Apply the fatwa hierarchy
Determine the mufta bihi position and cite the authority level (fatawa mutakhkhirin).
The ruling is from later Hanafi scholars; it is operative when conditions are met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن لوازم هذا القول أنه حيث وقع الأمن من اتباع الهوى، فلابأس بالأخذ بما هو أرجح دليلاً لعالم أهل للنظر في الأدلة. قال الإمام الفقيه الشيخ رشيد أحمد الكنكوهى " رحمه الله تعالى: "اسی واسطے تقلید غیر شخصی کو فقہاء نے کتابوں میں منع لکھا ہے، مگر جو عالم غیر شخصی کے سبب مبتلا ان مفاسد مذکورہ کا نہ ہو، اور نہ اسکے سبب سے عوام میں ہیجان ہو، اسکو تقلید غیر شخصی اب بھی جائز ہو گی۔ "إن الفقهاء منعوا العامّة من التقليد غير الشخصى (وهو أن يُقلّد مذهباً في مسألة وغيره في مسألة أخرى بسبب هذه المفاسد). ولكن العالم الذى يأمن من هذه المفاسد، فإنّه يجوز له التقليد غير الشخصي اليوم أيضاً، بشرط أن لا يُحدِث بذلك بلبلةً واضطراباً فى العامة.
And from the necessities of this statement is that wherever there is safety from following desire, there is no harm in a scholar competent in examining evidence adopting what is stronger in proof. Imam al-Faqih al-Shaykh Rashid Ahmad al-Kankohi said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'For this reason, the fuqaha have prohibited non-personal taqlid in the books, but a scholar who, due to non-personal taqlid, does not fall into the mentioned evils, and there is no disturbance among the common people because of it, then non-personal taqlid is still permissible for him.' 'Indeed the fuqaha have prohibited the common people from non-personal taqlid (which is to follow one madhhab in one issue and another madhhab in another issue because of these evils). But the scholar who is secure from these evils, then non-personal taqlid is permissible for him today as well, on the condition that he does not thereby cause confusion and disturbance among the common people.'
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling (hukm) on the permissibility of non-personal taqlid (taqlid ghair shakhsi) for a scholar. It begins by establishing a general principle: where the fear of following personal desire is absent, a scholar qualified to weigh evidence may adopt the preponderant view (arjah) even if it is not the preferred view of his own madhhab. Then the author cites Shaykh Rashid Ahmad al-Kankohi, who explains that the prohibition of non-personal taqlid recorded by the fuqaha was primarily directed at the common people to prevent the evils of picking and choosing (tatabbu' al-rukhas) and public confusion. However, a scholar who is immune from these evils—i.e., he does not follow desire, and his action does not cause uproar among the laity—may still engage in non-personal taqlid. The ruling is conditional: it requires both personal integrity (freedom from following desire) and social stability (no public disturbance). This is a nuanced fatwa methodology that balances adherence to the madhhab with the search for the strongest evidence.

Key Terms
التقليد غير الشخصي (al-taqlid ghair al-shakhsi): Following a different madhhab in each issue rather than sticking to one specific madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition is non-personal taqlid (taqlid ghair shakhsi) permissible for a scholar?
A) When he finds the other madhhab's evidence stronger
B) When he is secure from following desire and does not cause public disturbance
C) When he is a layperson
D) When he is a scholar of any sort

Key Takeaway
Non-personal taqlid is permissible for a qualified scholar who is safe from desire and does not create public disturbance.

When a Madhhab Ruling Contradicts Clear Texts: Balancing Truth and Unity
Ruling on leaving the madhhab when proven wrong, with Tahanawi's balanced approach.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi mufti rule for handling contradictions between a relied-upon ruling and clear Quran/Sunnah, balancing public interest (maslahah) and scholarly authority (taqlid).

Core Idea
A mufti must abandon a madhhab ruling if it clearly contradicts Quran/Sunnah, but if abandoning it causes public division, he may stick with the weaker view to preserve unity.

This lesson examines a delicate point in Hanafi fatwa methodology: what should a mufti do when he becomes certain that his madhhab's ruling on a matter directly opposes a clear Quranic verse or authentic hadith? Shaykh Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi provides a nuanced answer that balances the duty to follow truth with the responsibility to maintain community harmony. We will dissect his reasoning and the evidence he cites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
The passage begins by stating that if it is established that an Imam's ruling contradicts the Book and Sunnah, it is obligatory upon every believer to leave it. Record this as the baseline duty: truth over taqlid when contradiction is proven.
This is the position of many Hanafi scholars, including Imam Abu Hanifa's own statement.
2
Recognize the Practical Problem
The author immediately raises a crucial question: how can the common people verify such a contradiction? This shows that the duty to leave a ruling depends on knowledge, which laypersons generally lack. Only qualified scholars can make this determination.
This prevents laypeople from cherry-picking rulings without proper ijtihad.
3
Apply Tahanawi's Balanced Approach
Shaykh al-Tahanawi provides a structured framework: (a) Taqlid is valid because the mujtahid is seen as a channel for divine law, not as a legislator. (b) If a scholar (or a layman via a trustworthy scholar) becomes certain that the stronger (preponderant) view lies elsewhere, he must check if there is still a valid legal proof for the current (weaker) madhhab position. (c) If such a proof exists, and if abandoning the weaker view would cause public turmoil (fitna), then the preferable course is to act on the weaker (madhhab) view to preserve Muslim unity.
The key condition is that the weaker view must have some basis; it cannot be a baseless opinion.
4
Understand the Evidence
The passage cites a hadith from Aisha (radi Allahu anha) as proof for preferring unity. Although the hadith is cut off in our text, its placement indicates that preventing division among Muslims is a recognized maqsad (objective) of Shariah that can take precedence over acting on a stronger proof when weaker proofs exist.
The full hadith likely relates to avoiding fitna or maintaining community cohesion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في موضع آخر: "الغرض بعد ثبوت اس امر کے کہ یہ مسئلہ اپنے امام کا خلاف کتاب وسنت کے ہے، ترک کرنا ہر مومن کو لازم ہے، اور کوئی بعد وضوح اس امر کے اس کا منکر نہیں، مگر عوام کو یہ تحقیق ہی نہیں رہو سکتا ہے۔ (1) موجب " والحاصل أنّه إذا ثبت أنّ هذه المسئلة من إمامنا يُخالف الكتاب والسنة، لزم كل مؤمن أن يتركها ولا أحد ينكره بعد وضوح ذلك. ولكن كيف يمكن للعامة أن يحققوا هذا الأمر؟ " وفصل شيخ مشايخنا الإمام أشرف على التهانوي رحمه الله تعالى هذه المسئلة باعتدال واتزان بالغ فلابأس بإيراد كلامه بلفظه متبوعاً بترجمته العربية: " جس طرح تقلید کا انکار قابل ملامت ہے، اسی طرح اس میں غلو و جمود بھی مذمت ہے۔ اور تعیین طریق حق کے لئے) اوپر ثابت ہو چکا ہے کہ تقلید مجتہد کی اس کو شارع و بانی احکام سمجھ کر نہیں کی جاتی، بلکہ اسکو مین احکام اور موضح شرائع و مظہر مراد الله ور سول اعتقاد کرکے کی جاتی ہے۔ پس جب تک کوئی امر منافی اور رافع اس اعتقاد کا نہ پایا جاویگا ،اس وقت تک تقلید کی جائیگی، اور جس مسئلے میں کسی عالم وسیع النظر، ذکی الفہم، منصف مزاج کو اپنی تحقیق سے ، یا کسی عامی کو ایسے عالم سے، بشر طیکہ منتقی بھی ہو ، بشارتِ قلب معلوم ہو جاوے کہ اس مسئلے میں راج دوسری جانب ہے ، تو دیکھنا چاہئے کہ اس مرجوح جانب میں بھی دلیل شرعی سے عمل کی گنجائش ہے یا نہیں ؟ اگر گنجائش ہو ، تو ایسے موقع پر جہاں احتمال فتنہ و تشویش عوام کا ہو، مسلمانوں کو تفریق کلمہ سے بچانے کیلئے اولیٰ یہی ہے کہ اس مرجوح جانب پر عمل کرے۔ دلیل اس کی یہ حدیثیں ہیں۔۔۔۔۔ حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ عنہا سے روایت ہے کہ مجھ سے ارشاد فرمایا رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے کہ " تم کو "
And he said in another place: 'The purpose after the establishment that this issue is contrary to the Book and Sunnah from our imam, it is obligatory upon every believer to leave it, and no one denies it after the clarity of this matter, but the common people cannot verify this. So the conclusion is that if it is established that this issue from our imam contradicts the Book and Sunnah, it is obligatory upon every believer to leave it and no one denies it after the clarity of that. But how can the common people verify this matter?' And the shaykh of our shaykhs, Imam Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi, may Allah have mercy on him, detailed this issue with moderation and perfect balance, so there is no harm in quoting his words verbatim followed by its Arabic translation: 'Just as rejecting taqlid is blameworthy, likewise extremism and rigidity in it are also blameworthy. And for determining the correct way, it has been established above that taqlid of a mujtahid is not done by considering him as the legislator and founder of rulings, but rather by believing him as a medium for rulings, an explainer of laws, and a manifestation of the will of Allah and His Messenger. So as long as nothing contradictory and removing this belief is found, taqlid will be performed. And in a matter where a scholar of wide vision, sharp intellect, and fair disposition – by his own research, or a layman from such a scholar, provided he is a follower (muntahi) – obtains a clear hearted feeling that the preponderant side in this matter is the other, then one should see whether there is room for acting by a legal proof in the preponderant side as well. If there is room, then in a situation where there is a risk of turmoil and disturbance among the common people, for the sake of protecting the Muslims from division, the preferable course is to act on the preponderant side. The proof for this is the following hadith: From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to me: "You must..."'
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage discusses a critical nuance of fatwa methodology: when a scholar discovers that his imam's (mujtahid's) ruling is contrary to clear Quran and Sunnah, it becomes obligatory for every believer to leave that ruling. However, the common people cannot personally verify such contradictions. The author then quotes Shaykh Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi, who provides a refined framework: taqlid is not about deifying the mujtahid but about seeing him as a channel for understanding divine law. Therefore, as long as the belief in the mujtahid's authority remains intact, taqlid continues. But if a capable scholar (or a layman guided by such a scholar) becomes certain that the preponderant view lies elsewhere, he should check whether there is still scope to act on the previously followed (weaker) view according to some evidence. If there is such scope, and if abandoning it would cause public turmoil and division among Muslims, then the preferable course is to stick with the weaker view to preserve unity. This shows that fatwa rulings are not merely based on textual strength but also on maqasid al-shariah and public interest. The hadith from Aisha (incomplete in the text) serves as evidence for preferring harmony.

Key Terms
تقلید (taqlid): Following the ruling of a mujtahid without demanding proof, with the belief that he is a medium for understanding divine law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Shaykh Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi's discussion, what is the preferable course when a scholar finds the preponderant view is against his madhhab but there is still room for action on the weaker view, and public turmoil is likely?
A) Publicly announce the stronger view to spread truth
B) Act on the stronger view to uphold the truth
C) Act on the weaker view to preserve unity among Muslims
D) Remain silent and do not express any view

Key Takeaway
A mufti must balance following the strongest proof with preventing community division, and may continue with a weaker ruling if it has a basis and abandoning it would cause fitna.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
When Following the Weaker View is Preferred
Expands the mufti's rule on preferring weaker views to prevent fitna

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Imam al-Thanawi's rule that a muqallid may follow the weaker view if it has shari'i scope and there is fear of fitna, and distinguish this from the obligation to follow clear nass when the weaker view lacks such scope.

Core Idea
If the weaker view is valid and following the stronger view causes fitna, the weaker view is preferred.

What should a muqallid do when he learns that his imam's ruling contradicts a clear text? Some think he must immediately abandon his madhhab. Others insist on blind taqlid. Imam Ashraf Ali al-Thanawi provides a balanced methodology, explaining that the answer depends on whether the weaker view has shari'i scope and the potential for fitna. This lesson unpacks his analysis through two key hadith examples.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basis of taqlid
Taqlid means following a mujtahid as an interpreter, not a legislator. As long as no contradiction to this belief arises, taqlid continues.
2
Identify the scenario
When a muqallid learns (through a reliable scholar or his own research) that the rajih (preponderant) view is opposite his imam's view, he must assess the marjuh (weaker) view.
3
Check condition 1: shari'i scope
Does the marjuh view have any shari'i evidence, even if weak? If not, it cannot be acted upon, and the nass must be followed.
4
Check condition 2: fear of fitna
If the marjuh view has scope and there is likelihood of confusion or disunity among the community, it is preferable (awla) to act on the marjuh view to maintain unity.
This is based on the principle of 'دَرْءُ الْمَفَاسِدِ مُقَدَّمٌ عَلَى جَلْبِ الْمَصَالِحِ'
5
Apply the hadith examples
The Prophet chose not to rebuild the Kaaba on Ibrahim's foundation despite it being stronger, because the new Muslims would be confused. Similarly, Ibn Mas'ood prayed four rak'ats in travel to avoid dissent, though he preferred shortening.
Both actions assumed the weaker view was still permissible.

Source Text
