وقال في موضع آخر: "الغرض بعد ثبوت اس امر کے کہ یہ مسئلہ اپنے امام کا خلاف کتاب وسنت کے ہے، ترک کرنا ہر مومن کو لازم ہے، اور کوئی بعد وضوح اس امر کے اس کا منکر نہیں، مگر عوام کو یہ تحقیق ہی رہو سکتا ہے۔" والحاصل أنّه إذا ثبت أنّ هذه المسئلة من إمامنا يُخالف الكتاب والسنة، لزم كل مؤمن أن يتركها ولا أحد ينكره بعد وضوح ذلك. ولكن كيف يمكن للعامة أن يحققوا هذا الأمر؟ وفصل شيخ مشايخنا الإمام أشرف على التهانوي رحمه الله تعالى هذه المسئلة باعتدال واتزان بالغ فلابأس بإيراد كلامه بلفظه متبوعاً بترجمته العربية: "جس طرح تقلید کا انکار قابل ملامت ہے، اسی طرح اس میں غلو و جمود بھی مذمت ہے۔ اور تعیین طریق حق کے لئے) اوپر ثابت ہو چکا ہے کہ تقلید مجتہد کی اس کو شارع و بانی احکام سمجھ کر نہیں کی جاتی، بلکہ اسکو مین احکام اور موضح شرائع و مظہر مراد الله ور سول اعتقاد کرکے کی جاتی ہے۔ پس جب تک کوئی امر منافی اور رافع اس اعتقاد کا نہ پایا جاویگا ،اس وقت تک تقلید کی جائیگی، اور جس مسئلے میں کسی عالم وسیع النظر، ذکی الفہم، منصف مزاج کو اپنی تحقیق سے ، یا کسی عامی کو ایسے عالم سے، بشر طیکہ منتقی بھی ہو ، بشارتِ قلب معلوم ہو جاوے کہ اس مسئلے میں راج دوسری جانب ہے ، تو دیکھنا چاہئے کہ اس مرجوح جانب میں بھی دلیل شرعی سے عمل کی گنجائش ہے یا نہیں ؟ اگر گنجائش ہو ، تو ایسے موقع پر جہاں احتمال فتنہ و تشویش عوام کا ہو، مسلمانوں کو تفریق کلمہ سے بچانے کیلئے اولیٰ یہی ہے کہ اس مرجوح جانب پر عمل کرے۔ دلیل اس کی یہ حدیثیں ہیں۔۔۔۔۔ حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ عنہا سے روایت ہے کہ مجھ سے ارشاد فرمایا رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے کہ " تم کو معلوم نہیں کہ تمہاری قوم یعنی قریش نے جب کعبہ بنایا ہے، تو بنیادِ ابراہیمی سے کمی کردی ہے۔" میں نے عرض کیا " یا رسول اللہ ! پھر آپ اسی بنیاد پر تعمیر کرادیجئے۔ " فرمایا کہ اگر قریش کا زمانہ کفر سے قریب نہ ہوتا تو میں ایسا ہی کرتا۔" روایت کیا اسکو بخاری و مسلم نے ترمذی اور نسائی اور مالک نے۔ ف : یعنی لوگوں میں خوامخواہ تشویش پھیل جاوے گی کہ دیکھو! کعبہ گرا دیا، اسلئے اس میں دست اندازی نہیں کرتا۔ دیکھئے ! باوجودیکہ جانب راج یہی تھی کہ قواعد ابراہیمی پر تعمیر کر دیا جاتا، مگر چونکہ دوسری جانب بھی یعنی نا تمام رہنے دینا بھی، شرعاً جائز تھی، گو مرجوح تھی، آپ نے بخوف فتنہ و تشویش اسی جانب مرجوح کو اختیار فرمایا۔۔۔ (نیز) حضرت ابن مسعودؓ سے روایت ہے کہ انہوں نے (سفر میں) فرض چار رکعت پڑھی، کسی نے پوچھا کہ "تم نے حضرت عثمان پر (قصر نہ کرنے میں) اعتراض کیا تھا، پھر خود چار پڑھی؟" آپ نے جواب دیا کہ خلاف کرنا موجب شر ہے۔۔۔ اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ باوجودیکہ ابن مسعود (رضی اللہ عنہ) کے نزدیک جانب راجح سفر میں قصر کرتا ہے، مگر صرف شر اور خلاف سے بچنے کے لئے اتمام فرمالیا جو جانب مرجوح تھی، مگر معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اسکو بھی جائز سمجھتے تھے۔ بہر حال ! ان حدیثوں سے اس کی تائید ہو گئی کہ اگر جانب مرجوح بھی جائز ہو تو اسی کو اختیار کرنا اولیٰ ہے۔ اور اگر اس جانب مرجوح میں گنجائش عمل نہیں، بلکہ ترک واجب یا ارتکاب امر ناجائز لازم آتا ہے، اور بجز قیاس کے اس پر کوئی دلیل نہیں پائی جاتی، اور جانب راج میں حدیث صحیح صریح موجود ہے، اُس وقت بلا تر دو حدیث پر عمل کرنا واجب ہوگا، اور اس مسئلے میں کسی طرح تقلید جائز نہ ہوگی، کیونکہ اصل دین قرآن و حدیث ہے، اور تقلید سے یہی مقصود ہے کہ قرآن و حدیث پر سہولت وسلامتی سے عمل ہو، جب دونوں میں موافقت نہ رہی ، قرآن و حدیث پر عمل ہوگا۔ ایسی حالت میں بھی اسی پر جمے رہنا یہی تقلید ہے جسکی مذمت قرآن
And he said in another place: "The purpose after it is established that this issue is contrary to the Book and Sunnah from one's Imam, its abandonment is incumbent upon every believer, and no one denies it after the clarity of this matter. However, the common people can hardly verify this." The conclusion: if it is established that this issue from our Imam contradicts the Book and Sunnah, every believer must abandon it and no one denies that after its clarity. But how can the common people verify this matter? And the shaykh of our shaykhs, Imam Ashraf Ali al-Thanawi (may Allah have mercy on him) elaborated on this issue with great moderation and balance, so it is fine to present his words verbatim followed by its Arabic translation: "Just as rejection of taqlid is blameworthy, likewise extremism and rigidity in it are also blameworthy. And for determining the true way, it has already been proven that taqlid of a mujtahid is not done by considering him a legislator and establisher of rulings, rather it is done by believing him to be a revealer of rulings, an explainer of laws, and a manifestation of the intent of Allah and His Messenger. So as long as nothing contradictory and negating of this belief is found, taqlid will be performed. And in a matter where a broad-minded, intelligent, fair-natured scholar, from his own research, or a common person from such a scholar — provided that (the scholar) is also an expert — receives a revelation of the heart that the preponderant (rajih) is on the other side, then it should be seen whether in that preponderated (marjuh) side there is also scope for action from a shari'ah evidence or not. If there is scope, then in a situation where there is a likelihood of fitna and confusion among the common people, to protect the Muslims from disunity it is preferable to act on the preponderated side. The evidence for this are these hadiths... Narrated from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) said to me: 'Do you not know that when your people, the Quraysh, built the Kaaba, they reduced it from the foundations of Ibrahim?' I said, 'O Messenger of Allah, then why don't you rebuild it on that foundation?' He said, 'Were it not that the Quraysh's time of disbelief is near, I would have done so.' Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, and Malik narrated it. Explanation: That is, confusion would spread among the people unnecessarily that 'look! the Kaaba has been demolished', so he does not tamper with it. Observe! Even though the preponderant side was to rebuild on the foundations of Ibrahim, but since the other side — i.e., leaving it incomplete — was also permissible in shari'ah, albeit preponderated, the Prophet chose that preponderated side due to fear of fitna and confusion... Also, from Ibn Mas'ood (may Allah be pleased with him) that he prayed four rak'ats of the obligatory prayer (during travel). Someone asked: 'You objected to Uthman (regarding not shortening), yet you prayed four?' He replied: 'Dissent leads to evil.'... From this hadith it is also understood that although Ibn Mas'ood (may Allah be pleased with him) considered the preponderant side in travel to shorten, he completed the prayer (four) — which was the preponderated side — merely to avoid evil and dissent, but it appears he considered it also permissible. In any case! These hadiths support that if the preponderated side is also permissible, then it is preferable to adopt it. And if in that preponderated side there is no scope for action, rather abandoning an obligatory (wajib) or committing an impermissible action becomes necessary, and there is no evidence for it except qiyas (analogy), and on the preponderant side there is an explicit authentic hadith, then at that time acting upon the hadith without hesitation is obligatory, and in that issue taqlid is not permissible in any way, because the foundation of the religion is the Quran and hadith, and the purpose of taqlid is to act upon the Quran and hadith with ease and safety; when they do not agree, action will be upon the Quran and hadith. Even in such a state, remaining firm on that is itself taqlid, which the Quran censures.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage addresses the methodology of fatwa when a muqallid (follower of a madhhab) discovers that his imam's ruling on a particular issue contradicts clear Quranic verses or authentic hadith. The author begins by stating that if such a contradiction is established, every believer must abandon that ruling. However, the difficulty lies in how a common person can verify this. He then presents the detailed analysis of Imam Ashraf Ali al-Thanawi. Al-Thanawi explains that taqlid is based on the belief that the mujtahid is not a legislator but an interpreter of the Shari'ah. As long as nothing contradicts this belief, taqlid continues. If one comes to know — either through his own research (if he is a qualified scholar) or through a trustworthy scholar — that the preponderant view (rajih) lies elsewhere, he must look at whether the weaker view (marjuh) also has shari'i leeway (scope for action). If it does, and there is fear of fitna and disunity among Muslims, then it is actually preferable (awla) to act upon the weaker view to maintain unity. He supports this with two hadiths: the Prophet's decision not to rebuild the Kaaba on Ibrahim's foundation because it would cause confusion among the newly-reverted Quraysh, and Ibn Mas'ood's act of praying four rak'ats instead of shortening to avoid dissent, even though he considered shortening the preponderant view. The condition is that the weaker view must be genuinely valid in the Shari'ah. On the other hand, if the weaker view entails abandoning a wajib or committing something impermissible, and its only evidence is qiyas while the stronger view has an explicit authentic hadith, then it becomes obligatory to follow the hadith, and taqlid of that weaker view is not allowed. The author concludes that in such a case, following the clear text is itself the true taqlid, and remaining rigidly on the weaker view despite clear contrary evidence is the blameworthy taqlid censured in the Quran.

Key Terms
تقلید (taqlīd): Following a mujtahid by accepting his ruling as a valid interpretation of Shari'ah, not as legislation.
جانب راجح (jānib rājiḥ): The preponderant side/view based on stronger evidence.
جانب مرجوح (jānib marjūḥ): The weaker side/view that still has some shari'i validity.
گنجائش عمل (gunjāʾish ʿamal): Scope for action in Shari'ah; the view must be within the bounds of permissible rulings.
فتنہ و تشویش (fitnah wa tashwīsh): Tribulation and confusion among the community that may arise from acting on a stronger but controversial view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Ashraf Ali al-Thanawi's analysis, if a muqallid discovers that his imam's ruling is marjuh (weaker) and the stronger view has clear shari'i evidence, what is the condition for continuing to act on the marjuh side?
A) The marjuh side must also have some shari'i scope (gunjāʾish ʿamal) and there is fear of fitna/dissension.
B) The marjuh side must be preferred by the majority of scholars.
C) The muqallid must personally verify the evidence through ijtihad.
D) The marjuh side must be a concession (rukhsah) in the madhhab.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid's taqlid is not absolute; when the weaker view has shari'i scope and following the stronger view would cause fitna, acting on the weaker view is preferable to maintain unity, but if the weaker view is invalid, the stronger evidence must be followed.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Principle: Choosing the Weaker Opinion to Prevent Discord
Explains the rule of preferring marjuh to avoid fitna

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that if a weaker opinion is legally permissible and openly following the stronger opinion would cause fitna, it is better to act upon the weaker opinion.

Core Idea
Avoiding fitna can override a stronger opinion if the weaker alternative is permissible.

This lesson introduces a key principle in usul al-iftaa: a mufti may sometimes choose a weaker (marjuh) opinion over the stronger (rajih) one when doing otherwise would cause social discord or confusion. This is not arbitrary; it rests on the condition that the weaker opinion is legally permissible. The Prophet's own action regarding the Ka'bah and Ibn Mas'ud's practice during travel serve as precedents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opinions
Determine which opinion is considered stronger (rajih) and which is weaker (marjuh) in the given issue. The stronger is the one with greater evidentiary support.
In the Ka'bah example, rebuilding on Ibrahim's foundations was rajih; leaving it as is was marjuh.
2
Check permissibility of the weaker opinion
Verify that the weaker opinion is legally permissible (ja'iz) and does not require abandoning an obligation (wajib) or committing a prohibition (haram).
If it leads to haram or abandoning wajib, the exception applies (see next lesson).
3
Assess the risk of fitna
Evaluate whether openly adopting the stronger opinion would cause fitna, confusion, or division among the Muslim community, especially the general public (awamm).
Fitna includes social unrest, weakening of unity, or misunderstanding.
4
Apply the principle
If the weaker opinion is permissible and fitna is feared, it is better (awla) to act upon the weaker opinion to preserve harmony.
This is a precedent-based rule, not a license to disregard stronger evidence.
5
Recognize the limit
Be aware that this principle has an exception: if the weaker opinion violates a clear text or necessitates haram/wajib abandonment, the stronger must be followed. This will be covered in the next lesson.
The exception safeguards the primacy of textual evidence.

مناهج الفتوى فى السلف
البتہ جو شخص عقائد یا اجماعیات میں مخالفت کرے، یا سلف صالحین کو بُرا کہے ، وہ اہل سنت والجماعت سے خارج ہے، کیونکہ اہل سنت و جماعت وہ ہیں جو عقائد میں صحابہ رضی اللہ عنہم کے طریقے پر ہوں، اور یہ امور اُن کے عقائد کے خلاف ہیں، لہذا ایسا شخص اہل سنت سے خارج اور اہل بدعت و ہوئی میں داخل ہے۔ اسی طرح جو شخص تقلید میں غلو کرے کہ قرآن و حدیث کو رد کرنے لگے، ان دونوں قسم کے شخصوں سے حتی الامکان اجتناب و احتراز لازم جھیں، اور مجادلہ متعارفہ سے بھی اعراض کریں ۔ " (۱)
ترجمته: "كما أن إنكار التقليد موجب للملامة، فإن الغلو والجمود فيه موجب للمذمة أيضاً. وقد تقدم أنّ المجتهد لا يقلد لتعيين الحق باعتقاد أنّه شارع ومُنْشِى للأحكام، وإنّما يُقلد باعتقادِ أَنه مُبيِّن للأحكام وموضح للشرائع ومُظْهِرُ المُراد الله تعالى والرسول صلى الله عليه وسلّم. ولذا، فإن التقليد إنّما يُعمل به إذا لم يظهر أمرٌ يُنافى ذلك الاعتقاد أو يرفعه. فإن تبيّن لعالم واسع النظر ذكى الفهم منصف الطبع بتحقيقه، أو لعامي بواسطة مثل ذلك العالم بشهادة قلبه بشرط أن يكون متقيا، أن الراجح في هذه المسئلة جانب آخر، فلينظر هل هناك احتمال لجواز العمل بالجانب المرجوح على أساس دليل شرعى ( ولوكان مرجوحاً) أم لا؟ فإن كان هناك سعة، ويُخشى فى إظهار الخلاف من فتنة وتشويش للعوام، فالأولى في مثل هذه الحالة العمل بالجانب المرجوح وقايةً لعامة المسلمين من تفريق الكلمة. ويدلُّ على ذلك ما رَوَتْه عائشة رضى الله تعالى عنها قالت: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلّم: "أَلَمْ تَرَى أَنَّ قَوْمَكَ حِيْنَ بَنَوُا الكَعْبَةَ اقْتَصَرُوا عَنْ قَوَاعِدِ إِبْرَاهِيْمَ. " فَقُلْتُ: يَارَسُولَ اللَّهِ ! الاَتَرُدُّهَا عَلَى قَوَاعِدِ إِبْرَاهِيْمَ؟
فَقَالَ: "لَوْلا حِدثَانُ قَوْمِكِ بِالْكُفْرِ لَفَعَلْتُ " أخرجه الستة إلا أباداود. (۱) فبالرغم من أن بناء الكعبة على قواعد إبراهيم عليه السلام كان راجحاً، فإنّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلّم اختار الجانب المرجوح خشية الفتنة والتشويش، لأن هذا الجانب المرجوح كان جائزاً شرعاً، وإن كان مرجوحاً... وكذلك عن ابن مسعود رضى الله تعالى عنه أنه صلى أربعاً، يعنى في السفر) فقيل له: عبت على عثمان، ثمّ صليت أربعاً؟ فقال: "الخلاف شر " أخرجه أبوداود).
فبالرغم من أن الراجح عند ابن مسعود رضى الله تعالى عنه كان هو القصر فى السفر، فإنّه أتم الصلوة تجنباً عن الخلاف والشر، والظاهر أنه كان يرى جواز ذلك أيضاً. فتأيّد بذلك ماذكرنا أنه إن كان الجانب المرجوح جائزاً، فاختياره أولى تجبُّباً عن الفتنة والتشويش. أما إن كان الجانب المرجوح لا يحتمل الجواز، بل يستوجب ترك واجب أو ارتکاب محظور، وليس له دليل سوى القياس، ويوجد حديث صحيح صريح في الجانب الراجح، فيجب العمل بالحديث من غير تردد ولا يجوز التقليد في هذه الحالة أصلاً، لأنّ أصل الدين هو القرآن الكريم والسنة، وليس المقصود من التقليد إلا العمل بهما بسهولة وسلامة. فلما انْتَفَت الموافقة بينهما
Principles of Issuing Fatwa
Page 74
Methodologies of Fatwa Among the Salaf
But whoever opposes in matters of creed or consensus, or speaks ill of the pious predecessors, he is outside Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, because Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah are those who follow the way of the Companions in creed, and these matters are contrary to their beliefs. Therefore, such a person is excluded from Ahl al-Sunnah and enters into the people of innovation and desires. Similarly, whoever exagerrates in taqlid such that he begins to reject the Qur'an and Hadith, it is necessary to avoid and keep away from both types of persons as much as possible, and also to abstain from conventional debate." (1)
Its translation: "Just as denial of taqlid is blameworthy, so too exagerration and rigidity in it are also blameworthy. It has already been mentioned that the mujtahid does not taqlid to determine the truth with the belief that he is a legislator and originator of rulings, but rather he does taqlid with the belief that he is an explainer of rulings, a clarifier of the laws, and a revealer of the intent of Allah and the Messenger. Therefore, taqlid is only acted upon if nothing appears that contradicts that belief or removes it. So if it becomes clear to a broad-minded, intelligent, fair-natured scholar through his research, or to a common person through the mediation of such a scholar with the testimony of his heart, provided that he is pious, that the stronger (rajih) in this issue is another side, then let him consider: is there a possibility of acting upon the weaker (marjuh) side based on a shar'i evidence (even if it is weaker) or not? If there is leeway, and it is feared that revealing the difference would cause fitna and confusion for the common people, then in such a situation acting upon the weaker side is better, as a safeguard for the common Muslims against division. This is supported by what 'A'ishah reported: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Do you not see that when your people built the Ka'bah, they shortened it from the foundations of Ibrahim?' She said: 'O Messenger of Allah! Will you not return it to the foundations of Ibrahim?' He said: 'Were it not that your people are recent in disbelief, I would have done so.' Recorded by the six except Abu Dawud. So despite that building the Ka'bah upon the foundations of Ibrahim was stronger, the Messenger chose the weaker side for fear of fitna and confusion, because this weaker side was permissible legally, even though it was weaker. Similarly, from Ibn Mas'ud that he prayed four (i.e., during travel). It was said to him: You criticized 'Uthman, and then you prayed four? He said: 'Difference (khilaf) is evil.' Recorded by Abu Dawud. So despite that the stronger opinion according to Ibn Mas'ud was to shorten during travel, he completed the prayer to avoid difference and evil, and apparently he considered that also permissible. So this supports what we mentioned: if the weaker side is permissible, then choosing it is better to avoid fitna and confusion. But if the weaker side does not admit permissibility, rather necessitates abandoning an obligatory act or committing a prohibited act, and it has no evidence except qiyas, while there exists an explicit authentic hadith on the stronger side, then it is obligatory to act upon the hadith without hesitation, and taqlid is not permissible in this case at all, because the foundation of religion is the Noble Qur'an and Sunnah, and the purpose of taqlid is only to act upon them easily and safely. So when conformity is absent...
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage discusses the methodology of a mufti when faced with conflicting opinions. It begins by distinguishing between two extremes: those who completely reject taqlid and those who are rigidly fanatical in taqlid, both of which are blameworthy. The core principle is that taqlid is legitimate only as a means to understand and apply the Shari'ah, not as an end in itself. The author then presents a nuanced rule: if a mufti or a layperson realizes that the stronger (rajih) opinion actually lies contrary to the widely followed opinion, he should assess whether the weaker (marjuh) opinion is legally permissible. If it is permissible, and if openly following the stronger opinion would cause fitna (discord) or confusion among the masses, then it is better to act upon the weaker opinion to preserve unity. The author supports this with two key proofs: first, the Prophet's (peace be upon him) decision not to rebuild the Ka'bah on Ibrahim's foundations due to the recent conversion of his people, even though that was the stronger option. Second, Ibn Mas'ud's choice to pray full four rak'ahs during travel despite believing in qasr, simply to avoid conflict. However, the author adds a critical limitation: if the weaker opinion requires abandoning a wajib or committing a haram, and it is based only on qiyas while a clear authentic hadith supports the stronger side, then the stronger evidence must be followed unconditionally; taqlid of the weaker view is impermissible. This preserves the primacy of textual evidence over mere opinion. The passage thus sets out a balanced methodology for fatwa issuance that considers both evidence and social consequences.

Key Terms
تقليد (taqlid): Following a qualified mujtahid with the belief that he is explaining the Shari'ah, not legislating
راجح (rajih): The stronger opinion according to evidence, which would be followed in normal circumstances
مرجوح (marjuh): The weaker opinion, which is still legally permissible but less supported by evidence
فتنة (fitna): Discord, social disturbance, or confusion among the Muslim community

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for acting upon a weaker (marjuh) opinion to avoid fitna?
A) The weaker opinion must be based on a clear hadith.
B) The weaker opinion must be legally permissible (ja'iz).
C) The weaker opinion must be more convenient for the mufti.
D) The weaker opinion must be the majority view of the madhhab.

Key Takeaway
A mufti may prefer a weaker opinion to avoid fitna, but only if the weaker opinion is legally permissible and the stronger does not require abandoning a wajib or committing a haram.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
The Exception: When the Weaker Opinion Cannot Be Followed
Explains the exception to the rule of preferring the weaker opinion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify situations where choosing a weaker opinion is impermissible, specifically when the weaker opinion necessitates abandoning a wajib or committing a haram, and the stronger opinion is supported by an explicit authentic hadith.

Core Idea
If the weaker opinion violates a clear text, it cannot be followed, even to avoid fitna.

The previous lesson established the principle of preferring a weaker opinion to avoid fitna. However, this principle has a critical limitation. The author explicitly states that if the weaker opinion involves abandoning an obligatory act (wajib) or committing a prohibited act (haram), and it is based only on qiyas while there is an explicit authentic hadith supporting the stronger opinion, then the stronger opinion must be followed without hesitation. This lesson examines that exception and its implications for a mufti's methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the weaker opinion's content
Determine whether the weaker opinion requires abandoning a wajib or committing a haram. If it does, it is not permissible (ja'iz).
The weaker opinion must be permissible; if it entails haram, it cannot be opted for.
2
Check the basis of the weaker opinion
See if the weaker opinion is supported only by qiyas (analogy) without a strong textual basis.
Qiyas alone is weaker than an explicit text.
3
Verify the strong opinion's evidence
Confirm that the stronger opinion is based on an explicit authentic hadith (ṣaḥīḥ ṣarīḥ).
If the stronger has clear text, it takes precedence.
4
Apply the exception
If the above conditions are met, taqlid of the weaker opinion is not permissible; the stronger must be acted upon, even if it causes some fitna.
The purpose of taqlid is to follow the Qur'an and Sunnah; contradiction invalidates taqlid.
5
Understand the rationale
Preserving textual authority overrides temporary social harmony when the text is clear and the weaker opinion violates it.
Fitna from following the clear text is less harmful than abandoning the text's ruling.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to derive rulings not explicitly mentioned in the primary sources
راجح (rajih): The stronger opinion according to evidence
مرجوح (marjuh): The weaker opinion

Checkpoint
According to the exception, when is it obligatory to act upon the stronger opinion despite the potential for fitna?
A) When the weaker opinion is permitted by the majority of scholars.
B) When the weaker opinion is based on qiyas and the stronger is based on a clear hadith, and the weaker requires abandoning a wajib or doing haram.
C) Whenever the stronger opinion is more convenient for the mufti.
D) Only when the weaker opinion is based on a weak hadith.

Key Takeaway
When a weaker opinion violates a clear text by necessitating a prohibited act or abandoning an obligation, and it relies only on qiyas, the stronger text-based opinion must be followed, even if fitna is feared.

Degrees of Taqlid for the Mufti and Layperson
Explanation of the two degrees of taqlid with a historical example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two degrees of taqlid and apply the rule that a deeply learned scholar may depart from his imam's view when an explicit text contradicts it or to remove severe hardship.

Core Idea
Taqlid has degrees: the layperson adheres strictly; the advanced scholar may depart when evidence demands or hardship requires.

In this passage from 'Principles of Ifta,' Mufti Muhammad Taqi Uthmani explains that taqlid (following a madhhab) is not a single-level obligation. Through a historical anecdote about Imam al-Tahawi, we learn that even a great Hanafi scholar may occasionally differ from Abu Hanifa when strong evidence dictates. The author then formalizes two distinct degrees of taqlid, each with its own ruling. This lesson unpacks those degrees and their practical implications for both the layperson and the qualified mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the al-Tahawi anecdote
Read the story of Imam al-Tahawi and Ibn Harbawayh. Notice how al-Tahawi defends his departure from Abu Hanifa's view in one matter, emphasizing that it is not fanaticism but independent judgment. This sets the stage for the degrees of taqlid.
The anecdote illustrates that a qualified scholar may differ from his imam occasionally.
2
Extract the first degree of taqlid
Locate the passage describing the first degree: the common person or even a religious graduate who lacks the ability to compare evidences. State the ruling: such a person must commit to one madhhab and cannot reject his imam's statements based on personal opinion.
The imam's statement is treated as a proof (dalil) for them.
3
Extract the second degree of taqlid
Find the description of the deeply learned scholar. Note the conditions for departing from his imam: (1) finding an explicit text (nass) that contradicts the imam's view, after thorough research; (2) severe hardship (haraj) in the imam's madhhab that requires adopting another followed madhhab.
The scholar must have strong analytical ability and long experience in fiqh.
4
Apply the distinctions to a hypothetical scenario
Consider two persons: a recent graduate who only knows his madhhab's rulings, and a senior mufti who has studied extensively. For each, determine whether they may issue a fatwa contrary to their imam's view based on a verse they find. Use the passage's criteria.
The graduate cannot; the senior mufti may, after research and verification.

(۱) هو أحمد بن محمد بن سلامة أبو جعفر الطحاوي بفتح الطاء والحاء، نسبة إلى طحا [طحا]، قرية بصعيد مصر الأزدي. إمام جليل القدر، مشهور في الآفاق. انتهت إليه رئاسة الحنفية بمصر. كان يقرأ على خاله الإمام المزني الشافعي، فانتقل من مذهبه وتفقه على مذهب الإمام أبي حنيفة. وذكر أبو يعلى الخليلي في كتاب الإرشاد في ترجمة المزني أن محمد بن أحمد الشروطي قال للطحاوي: لم خالفت مذهب خالك؟ فقال: لأني كنت أرى خالي يديم النظر في كتب أبي حنيفة. أخذ الفقه عن أبي جعفر أحمد، ثم خرج إلى الشام فلقى بها أبا خازم عبد الحميد، قاضي القضاة بالشام، فأخذ عنه عن عيسى ابن أبان عن الإمام محمد رحمهم الله تعالى. كان إماماً في الأحاديث والأخبار، وله تصانيف جليلة معتبرة منها معاني الآثار وقد يسمى بشرح معاني الآثار، ومشكل الآثار، وأحكام القرآن والمختصر في الفقه وشرح الجامع الصغير وشرح الجامع الكبير وغيرها. توفي رحمه الله تعالى سنة ٣٢١ هـ. فالدرجة الأولى: تقليد العامي الذي ليس له معرفة بالقرآن والسنة، ولا تبحر في العلوم المنشعبة منهما، ويدخل فيهم الذين تخرجوا من المدارس والجامعات الدينية، ولم تحصل لهم ملكة يستطيعون بها المقارنة بين الآراء الفقهية في ضوء الكتاب والسنة. وحكم هؤلاء أن يلتزموا مذهب إمام معين، ولا يأخذوا إلا بأقوال إمامهم. فإن قول إمامهم دليل في حقهم، وليس لهم أن يحكموا على أقوال إمامهم بأنها معارضة للكتاب أو السنة بمجرد رأيهم، لأنه لا يتوافر لديهم ما يجب لمثل هذا الحكم.
والدرجة الثانية: تقليد عالم متبحر، وهو الذي وإن لم يبلغ درجة الاجتهاد الكلي، ولكنّه لسعة معرفته بعلوم القرآن والسنة، وتبحره في مذهب إمامه، وطول ممارسته بالفقه والفتيا لدى أساتذة مهرة، تحصل له ملكة قوية في النظر في دلائل الأحكام الفقهية، فإنّ مثل هذا العالم، وإن كان يقلد إمامه في معظم الأبواب الفقهية، ولكنه إذا وجد قولاً لإمامه معارضاً لنص صريح، ولم يجد مع طول بحثه ما يعارض ذلك النص، فإنّه يجوز له أن يترك قول إمامه من أجل ذلك النص الصريح، كما أسلفنا في عبارة الإمام الشيخ أشرف على التهانوي رحمه الله تعالى. وكذلك إذا شعر مثل هذا العالم بأن في مذهب إمامه في مسألة من المسائل حرجاً شديداً، وأن هناك حاجة عامة لدفع هذا الحرج باختيار مذهب فقهي آخر من المذاهب الأربعة المتبوعة، جاز له أن يفتي أو يعمل بقول مجتهد آخر غير إمامه، كما فعله الحنفية في مسألة
Principles of Ifta 82: Methodologies of Fatwa Among the Salaf
In some matters. And among that is what is narrated from Imam al-Tahawi, who is Hanafi in madhhab, that he said: 'Abu Ubayd ibn Harbawayh [3] used to discuss issues with me. One day I answered a question, and he said to me: "This is not the saying of Abu Hanifah." I said to him: "O judge, must I say everything that Abu Hanifah said?" He said: "I thought you were only a muqallid." I said to him: "Does anyone blindly follow except a fanatic?" He said to me: "Or stupid?" This word spread in Egypt until it became a proverb.' What al-Tahawi, may Allah have mercy on him, intended is that following a specific madhhab does not prevent a scholar like al-Tahawi from taking a saying other than that of his imam in some matters, and not out of fanaticism.

(2) Al-Qadi Abu Ubayd ibn Harbawayh... (biography) ... He died in Safar 319 AH.
(3) Mentioned by Hafiz Ibn Hajar in Raf al-Isr...

Principles of Ifta: Methodologies of Fatwa Among the Salaf
From here it becomes clear that taqlid has degrees.
The first degree: Taqlid of the common person who has no knowledge of the Quran and Sunnah, nor deep immersion in the branches of knowledge derived from them. This includes those who have graduated from religious schools and universities but have not acquired an ability to compare juristic opinions in light of the Quran and Sunnah. The ruling for these is that they commit to a specific imam’s madhhab and take only from their imam’s statements. Indeed, the statement of their imam is a proof for them, and they are not permitted to judge their imam’s statements as contradicting the Quran or Sunnah based on their own opinion, because they do not possess what is required for such a judgment.
The second degree: Taqlid of a deeply learned scholar, who, even if he has not reached the level of absolute ijtihad, due to his extensive knowledge of the sciences of the Quran and Sunnah, his deep immersion in his imam’s madhhab, and his long practice in fiqh and ifta under skilled teachers, has acquired a strong ability to examine the evidences of fiqh rulings. Such a scholar, although he follows his imam in most chapters of fiqh, if he finds a statement of his imam contradicting an explicit text, and after lengthy research he finds nothing to oppose that text, it is permissible for him to leave the statement of his imam for the sake of that explicit text, as we previously mentioned in the words of Imam Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi, may Allah have mercy on him. Similarly, if such a scholar perceives that in his imam’s madhhab on a certain issue there is severe hardship, and there is a general need to remove that hardship by choosing another fiqh madhhab among the four followed madhhabs, it is permissible for him to give fatwa or act according to the saying of another mujtahid besides his imam, as the Hanafis did in the issue of
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage from 'Principles of Ifta' discusses the different degrees of taqlid (following a madhhab). It begins with an anecdote about Imam al-Tahawi, a great Hanafi scholar, who was challenged for not always adhering to Abu Hanifa's opinion. Al-Tahawi's response shows that a scholar may occasionally depart from his imam's view when warranted, but not out of fanaticism. The author then outlines two degrees: First, the layperson or ordinary graduate who lacks the ability to compare evidences must strictly follow one madhhab and cannot reject their imam's statements based on personal judgment. Second, a deeply learned scholar who has attained a strong analytical ability may depart from his imam's opinion when faced with an explicit text that contradicts it, after thorough research, or when there is severe hardship that necessitates adopting another madhhab. This second degree is exemplified by the Hanafis in certain historical rulings.

Key Terms
تقليد (taqlid): Following the legal opinion of a mujtahid imam without knowledge of the evidence.
درجة (darajah): A level or degree, here referring to the two levels of taqlid: for the common person and for the advanced scholar.
عالم متبحر (alim mutabahhir): A deeply learned scholar who has extensive knowledge of Quran, Sunnah, and fiqh, and has acquired a strong ability to analyze evidences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for a deeply learned scholar to depart from his imam's saying?
A) He may do so whenever he personally disagrees with the imam.
B) He must find an explicit text (nass) that contradicts the imam's saying, and after thorough research finds no counter-evidence.
C) He must be an absolute mujtahid.
D) He must obtain permission from the ruling authorities.

Key Takeaway
Taqlid is not monolithic: the layperson follows strictly; the qualified scholar may depart when textual evidence or general hardship demands, but only after rigorous analysis and within the bounds of the four madhhabs.

The First Degree of Taqlid: The Layperson's Obligation
Defining the first degree of taqlid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the characteristics of the first-degree muqallid and apply the rule that they must strictly adhere to one madhhab.

Core Idea
The layperson must follow one imam; his imam's statement is his binding evidence.

This lesson focuses on the first degree of taqlid, which applies to the general public and even graduates who lack deep mastery. The author clarifies that such individuals cannot reject their imam's rulings based on personal reasoning, as they lack the capacity for comparative fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subjects of this degree
Who falls under the first degree? The layman ('ammi) including religious graduates who have not acquired the faculty for comparing juristic opinions.
2
State the ruling for them
The ruling (hukm) is that they must adhere strictly to a specific imam's madhhab and take only from his statements.
3
Understand the evidentiary value
The imam's statement is considered evidence (dalil) for them; they cannot judge it as contradicting the Book or Sunnah based on their own opinion.
4
Note the prohibition
They are prohibited from criticizing their imam's rulings without the necessary knowledge, because they lack the prerequisites for such a judgment.

مناهج الفتوى في السلف
زوجة المفقود وغيرها، وكما سيأتى إن شاء الله تعالى في موضعه، ولكن الأحوط فى هذا الزمان فى المسائل التى تعمّ بها البلوى أن لا يستبد الرجل في مثل هذه المسائل برأيه الفريد، بل يشاور غيره من العلماء، ولا يُفتى فتوى عامة إلا بعد حصول اتفاق جماعة من العلماء الراسخين. الدرجة الثالثة: تقليد مجتهد فى المذهب، وهو الذي وإن كان مقلدا لإمامه في الأصول، ولكنه حصل له نوع من الاجتهاد في الفروع أو في النوازل، و يندرج فيه أصحاب التخريج والترجيح والمجتهدون في المسائل كما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى.
والدرجة الرابعة: تقليد مجتهد مطلق، فإنّه وإن كان مستقلاً في استنباط الأحكام الشرعية من الكتاب والسنة، ولكن لا محيص له من نوع من التقليد، وهو أنّه ينظر فى أقوال السلف من الصحابة والتابعين، ويتمسك بها في شرح أحكام القرآن والسنّة، فربما لا يوجد نص صريح من الكتاب والسنة، ولكن يوجد قول من أحد الصحابة أو التابعين، فيُقدمه على رأيه الخاص وهذا كما أن أبا حنيفة رضي الله عنه كثيراً ما يأخذ بقول إبراهيم النخعي، والشافعي بقول ابن جريج، ومالكاً بقول أحد الفقهاء السبعة بالمدينة المنورة. قال العلامة ابن القيم رحمه الله تعالى فى المجتهد المطلق: "ولا ينافي اجتهاده تقليده لغيره أحياناً، فلا تجد أحداً من الأئمة إلا وهو مقلّد من هو أعلم منه في بعض الأحكام، وقد قال الشافعي رحمه الله ورضى عنه في موضع من الحج: " قلته تقليداً لعطاء. (۱)
(۱) إعلام الموقعين ٤:١٧٩ الفائدة التاسعة والعشرون: المفتون أربعة أقسام
From here it becomes clear that taqlid has degrees. Methodologies of fatwa among the Salaf. The first degree: taqlid of the layman, who has no knowledge of the Qur'an and Sunnah, nor deep immersion in the sciences derived from them. Included among them are those who have graduated from religious schools and universities, but have not acquired the faculty enabling them to compare juristic opinions in light of the Book and Sunnah. The ruling for these is that they adhere to a specific imam's madhhab and take only from their imam's statements. For their imam's statement is evidence for them, and they are not to judge their imam's statements as contradictory to the Book or Sunnah based merely on their own opinion, because they lack what is necessary for such a judgment. The second degree: taqlid of a deeply knowledgeable scholar, who, even if he has not reached the level of absolute ijtihad, yet due to his extensive knowledge of Qur'anic sciences and Sunnah, his deep immersion in his imam's madhhab, and his long practice of fiqh and fatwa under skilled teachers, acquires a strong faculty for examining the proofs of fiqh rulings. Such a scholar, although he follows his imam in most chapters of fiqh, if he finds a statement of his imam contradicting an explicit text and, despite prolonged research, finds nothing to oppose that text, it is permissible for him to leave his imam's statement for that explicit text, as we earlier quoted from Imam Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi, may Allah have mercy on him. Likewise, if such a scholar feels that in his imam's madhhab there is severe difficulty in a particular issue, and there is a general need to remove this difficulty by choosing another fiqh madhhab from the four followed madhhabs, it is permissible for him to give a fatwa or act according to the statement of another mujtahid besides his imam, as the Hanafis did in the issue of the wife of a missing person and others, and as will come, Allah willing, in its place. However, it is more cautious in this time concerning issues of widespread affliction that a man not act alone with his singular opinion in such matters, but rather consult other scholars, and not issue a general fatwa except after obtaining agreement of a group of firmly grounded scholars. The third degree: taqlid of a mujtahid within the madhhab, who, although he is a follower of his imam in fundamentals, has attained a type of ijtihad in subsidiary issues or in novel cases, and includes those capable of takhrij and tarjih, and mujtahids in particular issues, as will come, Allah willing. And the fourth degree: taqlid of an absolute mujtahid, for although he is independent in deriving legal rulings from the Book and Sunnah, he cannot escape a type of taqlid, namely that he looks at the statements of the Salaf among the Companions and Successors, and adheres to them in explaining the rulings of the Qur'an and Sunnah. Perhaps there is no explicit text from the Book and Sunnah, but there is a statement from a Companion or Successor, so he gives it precedence over his own opinion. This is like how Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, frequently took the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, al-Shafi'i took the statement of Ibn Jurayj, and Malik took the statement of one of the seven jurists of Medina. Allamah Ibn al-Qayyim, may Allah have mercy on him, said concerning the absolute mujtahid: 'His ijtihad does not preclude his occasional taqlid of others. You will not find any of the imams except that they followed someone more knowledgeable than them in some rulings. Al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him, said in a place concerning Hajj: I said it following Ata.' (1) Source: I'lam al-Muwaqqi'in 4:179, the twenty-ninth benefit: the muftis are four categories.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Ifta by Shaykh Muhammad Taqi Usmani expounds the different levels of taqlid, which is the following of a madhhab. It is a foundational ruling for the conduct of muftis and seekers of knowledge. The author classifies taqlid into four degrees, each with its own ruling.

First degree: The layperson ('ammi), including graduates without deep mastery, must adhere strictly to one madhhab. Their imam's statement is the evidence for them; they cannot reject it based on personal reasoning.

Second degree: The deeply knowledgeable scholar ('alim mutabahhir) may leave his imam's statement if it directly contradicts an explicit text (nass sarih) after thorough research, or if there is dire necessity ('hurjat shadid) and a general need to adopt another madhhab. However, the author cautions that in times of widespread need, one should not act alone but consult and seek consensus of senior scholars.

Third degree: The mujtahid within the madhhab (mujtahid fi al-madhhab) – one who, though bound by the usul of his imam, can exercise ijtihad in subsidiary matters (furu') or new cases (nawazil). These include those who perform takhrij (deriving rulings from the imam's principles) and tarjih (preferring one opinion over another).

Fourth degree: The absolute mujtahid (mujtahid mutlaq), who can derive rulings independently, yet still practices a form of taqlid by following the statements of earlier authorities (Sahaba, Tabi'in) when no clear text exists, preferring their view over his own opinion. The author cites examples of imams doing so, quoting Ibn al-Qayyim's I'lam al-Muwaqqi'in.

This hierarchy is crucial for understanding the Hanafi approach to fatwa: it restricts who may depart from the madhhab and under what conditions, emphasising the need for scholarly consultation and caution.

Key Terms
الدرجة الأولى (al-daraja al-ula): The first degree of taqlid: the layperson who must strictly follow one madhhab.
مقلد (muqallid): A person who follows a mujtahid in legal rulings without knowing the detailed evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a first-degree muqallid regarding their imam's statement?
A) They may accept or reject it as they see fit.
B) They must treat it as evidence and not reject it based on personal opinion.
C) They must verify it by going directly to the Quran and Sunnah.
D) They can follow any madhhab as they wish.

Key Takeaway
The first-degree muqallid must adhere strictly to one madhhab; his imam's statement is his binding evidence.

The Second Degree of Taqlid: The Deeply Knowledgeable Scholar
Defining the second degree of taqlid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a second-degree scholar may leave his madhhab and apply the cautionary rule for widespread issues.

Core Idea
A deeply knowledgeable scholar may leave his madhhab only for an explicit text or dire necessity, but must consult peers in widespread issues.

The second degree of taqlid applies to scholars who, while not absolute mujtahids, have deep mastery of their madhhab and its proofs. The passage details two valid grounds for departing from the madhhab: an explicit text contradicting the imam's view, or severe hardship with general need. However, a crucial caution is added for matters of widespread affliction: no single scholar should issue a fatwa alone; consensus of senior scholars is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's qualifications
What makes a scholar 'deeply knowledgeable'? Extensive knowledge of Quran and Sunnah, deep immersion in the madhhab, long practice under skilled teachers, and a strong faculty for examining proofs.
Note: this degree is below absolute ijtihad.
2
State the two grounds for leaving the madhhab
First: if the imam's statement contradicts an explicit text (nass sarih) and no counterargument is found. Second: if there is severe hardship (hurjat shadid) and a general need to adopt another madhhab.
3
Apply the cautionary rule for widespread issues
In issues of public affliction, the scholar must not act alone; he should consult other scholars and not issue a general fatwa without agreement of a group of firmly grounded scholars.
This is a practical adab for muftis.
4
Note the example given
The Hanafis applied the second ground in the case of the wife of a missing person, adopting a non-Hanafi opinion to remove hardship.

ومن هنا يتبين أن التقليد له درجات
مناهج الفتوى في السلف
فالدرجة الأولى: تقليد العامي الذى ليس له معرفة بالقرآن والسنة، ولا تبحر في العلوم المنشعبة منهما، ويدخل فيهم الذين تخرجوا من المدارس والجامعات الدينية، ولم تحصل لهم ملكة يستطيعون بها المقارنة بين الآراء الفقهية في ضوء الكتاب والسنة. وحكم هؤلاء أن يلتزموا مذهب إمام معيّن، ولا يأخذوا إلا بأقوال إمامهم. فإن قول إمامهم دليل في حقهم، وليس لهم أن يحكموا على أقوال إمامهم بأنّها معارضة للكتاب أو السنة بمجرد رأيهم، لأنه لا يتوافر لديهم ما يجب لمثل هذا الحكم.
والدرجة الثانية: تقليد عالم متبحر، وهو الذى وإن لم يبلغ درجة الاجتهاد . الكلّي، ولكنّه لِسَعَة معرفته بعلوم القرآن والسنّة، وتبحره في مذهب إمامه، وطُولِ ممارسته بالفقه والفتيا لدى أساتذة مهَرَة، تحصل له ملكة قوية في النظر في دلائل الأحكام الفقهيّة، فإنّ مثل هذا العالم، وإن كان يقلد إمامه في معظم الأبواب الفقهيّة، ولكنه إذا وجد قولاً لإمامه معارضاً لنص صريح، ولم يجد مع طول بحثه ما يُعارض ذلك النّصّ، فإنّه يجوز له أن يترك قول إمامه من أجل ذلك النص الصريح، كما أسلفنا في عبارة الإمام الشيخ أشرف على التهانوی رحمه الله تعالى. وكذلك إذا شعر مثل هذا العالم بأن في مذهب إمامه في مسئلة من المسائل حرجاً شديداً، وأن هناك حاجة عامة لدفع هذا الحرج باختيار مذهب فقهى آخر من المذاهب الأربعة المتبوعة، جاز له أن يُفتي أو يعمل بقول مجتهد آخر غير إمامه، كما فعله الحنفية في مسئلة
.............
أصول الإفتاء
٨٤٠
مناهج الفتوى في السلف
زوجة المفقود وغيرها، وكما سيأتى إن شاء الله تعالى في موضعه، ولكن الأحوط فى هذا الزمان فى المسائل التى تعمّ بها البلوى أن لا يستبد الرجل في مثل هذه المسائل برأيه الفريد، بل يشاور غيره من العلماء، ولا يُفتى فتوى عامة إلا بعد حصول اتفاق جماعة من العلماء الراسخين. الدرجة الثالثة: تقليد مجتهد فى المذهب، وهو الذي وإن كان مقلدا لإمامه في الأصول، ولكنه حصل له نوع من الاجتهاد في الفروع أو في النوازل، و يندرج فيه أصحاب التخريج والترجيح والمجتهدون في المسائل كما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى.
والدرجة الرابعة: تقليد مجتهد مطلق، فإنّه وإن كان مستقلاً في استنباط الأحكام الشرعية من الكتاب والسنة، ولكن لا محيص له من نوع من التقليد، وهو أنّه ينظر فى أقوال السلف من الصحابة والتابعين، ويتمسك بها في شرح أحكام القرآن والسنّة، فربما لا يوجد نص صريح من الكتاب والسنة، ولكن يوجد قول من أحد الصحابة أو التابعين، فيُقدمه على رأيه الخاص وهذا كما أن أبا حنيفة رضي الله عنه كثيراً ما يأخذ بقول إبراهيم النخعي، والشافعي بقول ابن جريج، ومالكاً بقول أحد الفقهاء السبعة بالمدينة المنورة. قال العلامة ابن القيم رحمه الله تعالى فى المجتهد المطلق: "ولا ينافي اجتهاده تقليده لغيره أحياناً، فلا تجد أحداً من الأئمة إلا وهو مقلّد من هو أعلم منه في بعض الأحكام، وقد قال الشافعي رحمه الله ورضى عنه في موضع من الحج: " قلته تقليداً لعطاء. (۱)
(۱) إعلام الموقعين ٤:١٧٩ الفائدة التاسعة والعشرون: المفتون أربعة أقسام
From here it becomes clear that taqlid has degrees. Methodologies of fatwa among the Salaf. The first degree: taqlid of the layman, who has no knowledge of the Qur'an and Sunnah, nor deep immersion in the sciences derived from them. Included among them are those who have graduated from religious schools and universities, but have not acquired the faculty enabling them to compare juristic opinions in light of the Book and Sunnah. The ruling for these is that they adhere to a specific imam's madhhab and take only from their imam's statements. For their imam's statement is evidence for them, and they are not to judge their imam's statements as contradictory to the Book or Sunnah based merely on their own opinion, because they lack what is necessary for such a judgment. The second degree: taqlid of a deeply knowledgeable scholar, who, even if he has not reached the level of absolute ijtihad, yet due to his extensive knowledge of Qur'anic sciences and Sunnah, his deep immersion in his imam's madhhab, and his long practice of fiqh and fatwa under skilled teachers, acquires a strong faculty for examining the proofs of fiqh rulings. Such a scholar, although he follows his imam in most chapters of fiqh, if he finds a statement of his imam contradicting an explicit text and, despite prolonged research, finds nothing to oppose that text, it is permissible for him to leave his imam's statement for that explicit text, as we earlier quoted from Imam Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi, may Allah have mercy on him. Likewise, if such a scholar feels that in his imam's madhhab there is severe difficulty in a particular issue, and there is a general need to remove this difficulty by choosing another fiqh madhhab from the four followed madhhabs, it is permissible for him to give a fatwa or act according to the statement of another mujtahid besides his imam, as the Hanafis did in the issue of the wife of a missing person and others, and as will come, Allah willing, in its place. However, it is more cautious in this time concerning issues of widespread affliction that a man not act alone with his singular opinion in such matters, but rather consult other scholars, and not issue a general fatwa except after obtaining agreement of a group of firmly grounded scholars. The third degree: taqlid of a mujtahid within the madhhab, who, although he is a follower of his imam in fundamentals, has attained a type of ijtihad in subsidiary issues or in novel cases, and includes those capable of takhrij and tarjih, and mujtahids in particular issues, as will come, Allah willing. And the fourth degree: taqlid of an absolute mujtahid, for although he is independent in deriving legal rulings from the Book and Sunnah, he cannot escape a type of taqlid, namely that he looks at the statements of the Salaf among the Companions and Successors, and adheres to them in explaining the rulings of the Qur'an and Sunnah. Perhaps there is no explicit text from the Book and Sunnah, but there is a statement from a Companion or Successor, so he gives it precedence over his own opinion. This is like how Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, frequently took the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, al-Shafi'i took the statement of Ibn Jurayj, and Malik took the statement of one of the seven jurists of Medina. Allamah Ibn al-Qayyim, may Allah have mercy on him, said concerning the absolute mujtahid: 'His ijtihad does not preclude his occasional taqlid of others. You will not find any of the imams except that they followed someone more knowledgeable than them in some rulings. Al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him, said in a place concerning Hajj: I said it following Ata.' (1) Source: I'lam al-Muwaqqi'in 4:179, the twenty-ninth benefit: the muftis are four categories.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Ifta by Shaykh Muhammad Taqi Usmani expounds the different levels of taqlid, which is the following of a madhhab. It is a foundational ruling for the conduct of muftis and seekers of knowledge. The author classifies taqlid into four degrees, each with its own ruling.

First degree: The layperson ('ammi), including graduates without deep mastery, must adhere strictly to one madhhab. Their imam's statement is the evidence for them; they cannot reject it based on personal reasoning.

Second degree: The deeply knowledgeable scholar ('alim mutabahhir) may leave his imam's statement if it directly contradicts an explicit text (nass sarih) after thorough research, or if there is dire necessity ('hurjat shadid) and a general need to adopt another madhhab. However, the author cautions that in times of widespread need, one should not act alone but consult and seek consensus of senior scholars.

Third degree: The mujtahid within the madhhab (mujtahid fi al-madhhab) – one who, though bound by the usul of his imam, can exercise ijtihad in subsidiary matters (furu') or new cases (nawazil). These include those who perform takhrij (deriving rulings from the imam's principles) and tarjih (preferring one opinion over another).

Fourth degree: The absolute mujtahid (mujtahid mutlaq), who can derive rulings independently, yet still practices a form of taqlid by following the statements of earlier authorities (Sahaba, Tabi'in) when no clear text exists, preferring their view over his own opinion. The author cites examples of imams doing so, quoting Ibn al-Qayyim's I'lam al-Muwaqqi'in.

This hierarchy is crucial for understanding the Hanafi approach to fatwa: it restricts who may depart from the madhhab and under what conditions, emphasising the need for scholarly consultation and caution.

Key Terms
الدرجة الثانية (al-daraja al-thaniya): The second degree: a deeply knowledgeable scholar who can leave his madhhab for an explicit text or necessity, but with caution.
حرج شديد (hurjat shadid): Severe difficulty or hardship that justifies departing from the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What additional requirement does the passage specify for second-degree scholars when dealing with issues of widespread affliction?
A) They must follow the Hanafi ruling regardless.
B) They must consult other scholars and not issue a fatwa alone.
C) They must refer the matter to the government.
D) They can act on their own if they are confident.

Key Takeaway
A second-degree scholar may leave his madhhab for an explicit text or severe necessity, but must consult colleagues in widespread matters.

The Third Degree of Taqlid: The Mujtahid within the Madhhab
Defining the third degree of taqlid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the third degree of taqlid and explain the functions of takhrij, tarjih, and ijtihad in subsidiary issues within the Hanafi madhhab.

Core Idea
A mujtahid within the madhhab can derive rulings for new cases and weigh conflicting opinions, but remains bound by the imam's usul.

The third degree of taqlid describes scholars who, while still following the imam in fundamentals (usul), have attained a degree of ijtihad in subsidiary matters (furu') or novel cases (nawazil). They are the ones who perform takhrij (deriving rulings from the imam's principles) and tarjih (preferring one opinion over another). Understanding this degree is crucial for grasping how the Hanafi madhhab developed and adapted over time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the third-degree mujtahid's relationship to the imam
He is a follower (muqallid) of his imam in the fundamentals of the madhhab (uṣūl al-madhhab).
2
Define his ijtihad scope
He has a type of ijtihad in subsidiary issues (furu') and novel cases (nawazil). This includes the ability to derive rulings from the imam's principles.
3
List the functions of takhrij and tarjih
Takhrij: deriving a ruling on a new issue by applying the imam's usul. Tarjih: preferring one transmitted opinion over another within the madhhab.
4
Distinguish from the fourth degree
Unlike the absolute mujtahid (fourth degree), he does not have independent authority to establish his own usul.

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Ifta by Shaykh Muhammad Taqi Usmani expounds the different levels of taqlid, which is the following of a madhhab. It is a foundational ruling for the conduct of muftis and seekers of knowledge. The author classifies taqlid into four degrees, each with its own ruling.

However, the author cautions that in times of widespread need, one should not act alone but consult and seek consensus of senior scholars.

These include those who perform takhrij (deriving rulings from the imam's principles) and tarjih (preferring one opinion over another).

The author cites examples of imams doing so, quoting Ibn al-Qayyim's I'lam al-Muwaqqi'in.

This hierarchy is crucial for understanding the Hanafi approach to fatwa: it restricts who may depart from the madhhab and under what conditions, emphasising the need for scholarly consultation and caution.

Key Terms
الدرجة الثالثة (al-daraja al-thalitha): The third degree: a mujtahid within the madhhab, capable of takhrij and tarjih in subsidiary issues.
تخريج (takhrij): Deriving a ruling for a new case from the imam's principles or from existing rulings.
ترجيح (tarjih): Preferring one opinion over another within the madhhab based on strength of evidence or other criteria.

What does the passage say about the third-degree scholar's relationship to the imam's fundamentals?
A) He is independent of the imam's usul.

Key Takeaway
The third-degree mujtahid performs ijtihad in subsidiary issues while following the imam in fundamentals, enabling the madhhab's adaptation to new cases.

The Fourth Degree of Taqlid: The Absolute Mujtahid Who Follows the Salaf
Defining the fourth degree of taqlid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how an absolute mujtahid may still engage in taqlid of earlier authorities and apply the principle that following the salaf is part of their methodology.

Core Idea
Even absolute mujtahids practice taqlid of the Salaf when no explicit text exists, preferring their views over personal opinion.

The fourth degree of taqlid applies to absolute mujtahids (mujtahid mutlaq), who are capable of deriving rulings directly from the Quran and Sunnah. Yet, as the passage elucidates, they cannot completely escape taqlid: they frequently follow the statements of the Companions and Successors. This is illustrated by examples of the great imams—Abu Hanifa following Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, al-Shafi'i following Ibn Jurayj, and Malik following one of the seven jurists of Medina. The lesson underscores that taqlid, in this sense, is not a sign of deficiency but a mark of respect for earlier authority and methodological conservatism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of this degree
Absolute mujtahid who is independent in deriving rulings from primary sources.
2
Understand the type of taqlid they practice
They follow the statements of the Salaf (Companions and Successors) when no explicit primary text exists.
This is not blind taqlid but a methodological choice.
3
Examine the rationale
They give precedence to the sayings of the Salaf over their own opinion, because the Salaf had greater knowledge and proximity to revelation.
4
Study the examples
Abu Hanifa took from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i; al-Shafi'i from Ibn Jurayj; Malik from one of the seven jurists of Medina.
5
Quote the authority of Ibn al-Qayyim
Ibn al-Qayyim affirms that absolute ijtihad does not preclude occasional taqlid of others; even the great imams did so.

ومن هنا يتبين أن التقليد له درجات
مناهج الفتوى في السلف
فالدرجة الأولى: تقليد العامي الذى ليس له معرفة بالقرآن والسنة، ولا تبحر في العلوم المنشعبة منهما، ويدخل فيهم الذين تخرجوا من المدارس والجامعات الدينية، ولم تحصل لهم ملكة يستطيعون بها المقارنة بين الآراء الفقهية في ضوء الكتاب والسنة. وحكم هؤلاء أن يلتزموا مذهب إمام معيّن، ولا يأخذوا إلا بأقوال إمامهم. فإن قول إمامهم دليل في حقهم، وليس لهم أن يحكموا على أقوال إمامهم بأنّها معارضة للكتاب أو السنة بمجرد رأيهم، لأنه لا يتوافر لديهم ما يجب لمثل هذا الحكم.
والدرجة الثانية: تقليد عالم متبحر، وهو الذى وإن لم يبلغ درجة الاجتهاد . الكلّي، ولكنّه لِسَعَة معرفته بعلوم القرآن والسنّة، وتبحره في مذهب إمامه، وطُولِ ممارسته بالفقه والفتيا لدى أساتذة مهَرَة، تحصل له ملكة قوية في النظر في دلائل الأحكام الفقهيّة، فإنّ مثل هذا العالم، وإن كان يقلد إمامه في معظم الأبواب الفقهيّة، ولكنه إذا وجد قولاً لإمامه معارضاً لنص صريح، ولم يجد مع طول بحثه ما يُعارض ذلك النّصّ، فإنّه يجوز له أن يترك قول إمامه من أجل ذلك النص الصريح، كما أسلفنا في عبارة الإمام الشيخ أشرف على التهانوی رحمه الله تعالى. وكذلك إذا شعر مثل هذا العالم بأن في مذهب إمامه في مسئلة من المسائل حرجاً شديداً، وأن هناك حاجة عامة لدفع هذا الحرج باختيار مذهب فقهى آخر من المذاهب الأربعة المتبوعة، جاز له أن يُفتي أو يعمل بقول مجتهد آخر غير إمامه، كما فعله الحنفية في مسئلة

مناهج الفتوى في السلف
زوجة المفقود وغيرها، وكما سيأتى إن شاء الله تعالى في موضعه، ولكن الأحوط فى هذا الزمان فى المسائل التى تعمّ بها البلوى أن لا يستبد الرجل في مثل هذه المسائل برأيه الفريد، بل يشاور غيره من العلماء، ولا يُفتى فتوى عامة إلا بعد حصول اتفاق جماعة من العلماء الراسخين. الدرجة الثالثة: تقليد مجتهد فى المذهب، وهو الذي وإن كان مقلدا لإمامه في الأصول، ولكنه حصل له نوع من الاجتهاد في الفروع أو في النوازل، و يندرج فيه أصحاب التخريج والترجيح والمجتهدون في المسائل كما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى.
والدرجة الرابعة: تقليد مجتهد مطلق، فإنّه وإن كان مستقلاً في استنباط الأحكام الشرعية من الكتاب والسنة، ولكن لا محيص له من نوع من التقليد، وهو أنّه ينظر فى أقوال السلف من الصحابة والتابعين، ويتمسك بها في شرح أحكام القرآن والسنّة، فربما لا يوجد نص صريح من الكتاب والسنة، ولكن يوجد قول من أحد الصحابة أو التابعين، فيُقدمه على رأيه الخاص وهذا كما أن أبا حنيفة رضي الله عنه كثيراً ما يأخذ بقول إبراهيم النخعي، والشافعي بقول ابن جريج، ومالكاً بقول أحد الفقهاء السبعة بالمدينة المنورة. قال العلامة ابن القيم رحمه الله تعالى فى المجتهد المطلق: "ولا ينافي اجتهاده تقليده لغيره أحياناً، فلا تجد أحداً من الأئمة إلا وهو مقلّد من هو أعلم منه في بعض الأحكام، وقد قال الشافعي رحمه الله ورضى عنه في موضع من الحج: " قلته تقليداً لعطاء. (۱)
(۱) إعلام الموقعين ٤:١٧٩ الفائدة التاسعة والعشرون: المفتون أربعة أقسام
From here it becomes clear that taqlid has degrees. Methodologies of fatwa among the Salaf. The first degree: taqlid of the layman, who has no knowledge of the Qur'an and Sunnah, nor deep immersion in the sciences derived from them. Included among them are those who have graduated from religious schools and universities, but have not acquired the faculty enabling them to compare juristic opinions in light of the Book and Sunnah. The ruling for these is that they adhere to a specific imam's madhhab and take only from their imam's statements. For their imam's statement is evidence for them, and they are not to judge their imam's statements as contradictory to the Book or Sunnah based merely on their own opinion, because they lack what is necessary for such a judgment. The second degree: taqlid of a deeply knowledgeable scholar, who, even if he has not reached the level of absolute ijtihad, yet due to his extensive knowledge of Qur'anic sciences and Sunnah, his deep immersion in his imam's madhhab, and his long practice of fiqh and fatwa under skilled teachers, acquires a strong faculty for examining the proofs of fiqh rulings. Such a scholar, although he follows his imam in most chapters of fiqh, if he finds a statement of his imam contradicting an explicit text and, despite prolonged research, finds nothing to oppose that text, it is permissible for him to leave his imam's statement for that explicit text, as we earlier quoted from Imam Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi, may Allah have mercy on him. Likewise, if such a scholar feels that in his imam's madhhab there is severe difficulty in a particular issue, and there is a general need to remove this difficulty by choosing another fiqh madhhab from the four followed madhhabs, it is permissible for him to give a fatwa or act according to the statement of another mujtahid besides his imam, as the Hanafis did in the issue of the wife of a missing person and others, and as will come, Allah willing, in its place. However, it is more cautious in this time concerning issues of widespread affliction that a man not act alone with his singular opinion in such matters, but rather consult other scholars, and not issue a general fatwa except after obtaining agreement of a group of firmly grounded scholars. The third degree: taqlid of a mujtahid within the madhhab, who, although he is a follower of his imam in fundamentals, has attained a type of ijtihad in subsidiary issues or in novel cases, and includes those capable of takhrij and tarjih, and mujtahids in particular issues, as will come, Allah willing. And the fourth degree: taqlid of an absolute mujtahid, for although he is independent in deriving legal rulings from the Book and Sunnah, he cannot escape a type of taqlid, namely that he looks at the statements of the Salaf among the Companions and Successors, and adheres to them in explaining the rulings of the Qur'an and Sunnah. Perhaps there is no explicit text from the Book and Sunnah, but there is a statement from a Companion or Successor, so he gives it precedence over his own opinion. This is like how Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, frequently took the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, al-Shafi'i took the statement of Ibn Jurayj, and Malik took the statement of one of the seven jurists of Medina. Allamah Ibn al-Qayyim, may Allah have mercy on him, said concerning the absolute mujtahid: 'His ijtihad does not preclude his occasional taqlid of others. You will not find any of the imams except that they followed someone more knowledgeable than them in some rulings. Al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him, said in a place concerning Hajj: I said it following Ata.' (1) Source: I'lam al-Muwaqqi'in 4:179, the twenty-ninth benefit: the muftis are four categories.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Ifta by Shaykh Muhammad Taqi Usmani expounds the different levels of taqlid, which is the following of a madhhab. It is a foundational ruling for the conduct of muftis and seekers of knowledge. The author classifies taqlid into four degrees, each with its own ruling.

First degree: The layperson ('ammi), including graduates without deep mastery, must adhere strictly to one madhhab. Their imam's statement is the evidence for them; they cannot reject it based on personal reasoning.

Second degree: The deeply knowledgeable scholar ('alim mutabahhir) may leave his imam's statement if it directly contradicts an explicit text (nass sarih) after thorough research, or if there is dire necessity ('hurjat shadid) and a general need to adopt another madhhab. However, the author cautions that in times of widespread need, one should not act alone but consult and seek consensus of senior scholars.

Third degree: The mujtahid within the madhhab (mujtahid fi al-madhhab) – one who, though bound by the usul of his imam, can exercise ijtihad in subsidiary matters (furu') or new cases (nawazil). These include those who perform takhrij (deriving rulings from the imam's principles) and tarjih (preferring one opinion over another).

Fourth degree: The absolute mujtahid (mujtahid mutlaq), who can derive rulings independently, yet still practices a form of taqlid by following the statements of earlier authorities (Sahaba, Tabi'in) when no clear text exists, preferring their view over his own opinion. The author cites examples of imams doing so, quoting Ibn al-Qayyim's I'lam al-Muwaqqi'in.

This hierarchy is crucial for understanding the Hanafi approach to fatwa: it restricts who may depart from the madhhab and under what conditions, emphasising the need for scholarly consultation and caution.

Key Terms
الدرجة الرابعة (al-daraja al-rabi'a): The fourth degree: an absolute mujtahid who may still follow earlier authorities (taqlid al-salaf).
مقلد السلف (muqallid al-salaf): One who follows the statements of the Salaf as a methodological principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the absolute mujtahid give precedence to the statements of the Salaf over his own opinion?
A) Because he lacks confidence in his own ijtihad.
B) Because he respects the Salaf's knowledge and proximity to revelation.
C) Because the Salaf's statements are also primary texts.
D) Because he is forced to follow them.

Key Takeaway
Absolute mujtahids practice taqlid of the Salaf, showing that ijtihad and following earlier authorities are compatible.

The Hierarchical Classification of Hanafi Jurists (Tabaqat al-Fuqaha)
Introduction to the hierarchical classification of Hanafi jurists

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose of tabaqat al-fuqaha in Hanafi iftaa and identify the roles of Ibn Kamal Pasha and Ibn Abidin in systematizing it.

Core Idea
Tabaqat al-fuqaha ranks Hanafi jurists; the higher the class, the stronger the opinion for fatwa.

In Hanafi fatwa methodology, not all juristic opinions carry equal weight. This lesson introduces the hierarchical classification (tabaqat) of Hanafi jurists, a system that guides muftis in prioritizing authoritative views. The passage from Ibn Abidin's 'Rasm al-Mufti' credits Ibn Kamal Pasha with enumerating these classes, providing a foundation for later fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of tabaqat
Understand that the classification is not merely historical; it determines which opinion a mufti should prefer when multiple views exist.
The hierarchy is based on scholarly rank and proximity to the founding imams.
2
Recognize the key contributors
Note that Ibn Kamal Pasha enumerated the classes, while Ibn Abidin preserved and explicated the system in his commentary on Rasm al-Mufti.
Both are later authorities whose work shaped modern Hanafi iftaa.
3
Analyze the biographical illustration
The story of Ibn Kamal Pasha's inspiration shows how the dignity of knowledge motivated him, leading to his influential classification.
This reinforces the value placed on scholarly rank in the tradition.
4
Apply the principle to fatwa practice
Consider a scenario: if two Hanafi opinions differ, the one from a higher tabaqa (e.g., a mujtahid) is given precedence over a later muqallid's view, unless later tarjih dictates otherwise.
This is a core rule in rasm al-mufti.

Classes of Jurists

Principles of Issuing Fatwa
86
Classes of Hanafi Jurists
Classes of Jurists
Indeed, Allamah Ibn Abidin (1), may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned in Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti that the Hanafi jurists are divided into classes, which were enumerated by Allamah Ibn Kamal Pasha (2).

(1) Allamah Ibn Abidin al-Shami: Al-Zirikli said in al-A'lam: Muhammad Amin ibn Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz Abidin al-Dimashqi: the jurist of the Syrian lands and the imam of the Hanafis in his time. His birth and death were in Damascus. He authored 'Radd al-Muhtar ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar' five volumes of fiqh known as Hashiyat Ibn Abidin, and 'Raf al-Ansar amma awradahu al-Halabi ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar', and 'al-Uqud al-Durriyya fi Tanqih al-Fatawa al-[?] al-Hamidiyya' two parts, and 'Nasamat al-Ashar ala Sharh al-Manar' in usul, and a gloss on al-Mutawwal in balagha, and 'al-Rahiq al-Makhtum' on fara'id, and glosses on Tafsir al-Baydawi in which he committed to not mentioning anything that the commentators had mentioned, and 'Majmu'at Rasail' two volumes comprising 32 treatises, and 'Uqud al-Lali fi al-Asanid al-Awali' which is his register. Al-Zirikli dated his birth at 1198 AH and his death, may Allah have mercy on him, at 1252 AH (al-A'lam 6:42).

(2) He is Ahmad ibn Sulayman ibn Kamal Pasha. His grandfather was among the commanders of the Ottoman state, and he grew up in his youth in comfort. Allamah Tashkopru Zadah narrated in 'al-Shaqaiq al-Numaniyya fi Ulama al-Dawla al-Uthmaniyya' the reason for his engagement in learning: that he was in the company of Sultan Bayezid Khan on a journey, along with a vizier and an amir called Ahmad Beg, and he saw that a man from the scholars, of shabby appearance and lowly dress, came and sat above the aforementioned amir. Kamal Pasha was amazed by this and asked his companions the reason for his audacity towards the amir. He was told that he is a scholar and teacher called Mulla Lutfi, and his salary is thirty dirhams, and the amir honors him only for his knowledge, and the amir is not pleased that he should sit anywhere other than this seat. So the greatness of knowledge fell into the heart of Ibn Kamal Pasha, so he went to serve the aforementioned Mulla and studied with him the glosses on Sharh al-Matali. Summarized from al-Shaqaiq al-Numaniyya p.226. He also acquired knowledge from Mulla Muslih al-Din al-Qastalani, who traces his chain in fiqh to Akmal al-Din al-Babarti, author of al-Inayah, then to Husam al-Din Hasan al-Sighnaqi, author of al-Nihayah. Ibn Kamal, may Allah have mercy on him, became a teacher in the city of Edirne, then became a judge, and entered with the Sultan into Cairo when he took it from the Circassians, and its people testified to his excellence and mastery. Then he became Mufti in Constantinople, and he has many esteemed works, including a noble and excellent tafsir of the Quran close to completion, but death overtook him and he did not complete it, and glosses on al-Kashshaf,=
from
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage introduces the classification of Hanafi jurists into hierarchical layers (tabaqat), a key concept in Hanafi jurisprudence for determining the weight of opinions in fatwa. The author references the work of Allamah Ibn Abidin (d. 1252 AH) in his commentary on Rasm al-Mufti, where he states that the Hanafi jurists are divided into classes enumerated by Ibn Kamal Pasha (d. 940 AH). The text then provides a biographical note on Ibn Abidin, listing his major works including 'Radd al-Muhtar' and his glosses. Following that, a detailed biography of Ibn Kamal Pasha is given, recounting how his encounter with a humble scholar named Mulla Lutfi inspired him to pursue knowledge. The biography traces his education, his rise to become a teacher, judge, and finally Mufti of Constantinople, and lists some of his unfinished works. This classification system is fundamental to the science of ifta' because it establishes the authority of different juristic opinions; later muftis are bound to follow the most authoritative views from higher classes.

Key Terms
طبقات الفقهاء (tabaqat al-fuqaha): The hierarchical classes of Hanafi jurists as enumerated by Ibn Kamal Pasha, determining the precedence of their opinions.
ابن كمال باشا (Ibn Kamal Pasha): Ahmad ibn Sulayman, a prominent Ottoman Hanafi scholar who systematized the tabaqat of Hanafi jurists.
رسم المفتي (rasm al-mufti): The rules and conditions for issuing fatwas; a work by Ibn Abidin that sets forth the methodology for muftis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Ibn Kamal Pasha
C) Mulla Lutfi
D) Sultan Bayezid

Key Takeaway
The hierarchical classification of Hanafi jurists (tabaqat) is essential for determining authoritative opinions in fatwa, with higher classes taking precedence.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Three Layers of Hanafi Jurists
Defining juristic authority layers in Hanafi fatwa methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and differentiate the three layers of Hanafi jurists and apply the hierarchy to determine a scholar's authority in fatwa.

Core Idea
A Hanafi mufti must operate within his own layer; only founding imams have absolute ijtihad.

The Hanafi school is not a monolithic block; jurists operate at different levels of authority. Ibn Abidin, in his commentary on Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, cites Ibn Kamal Basha's classification of seven layers, of which three are essential for understanding the hierarchy. Knowing which layer a scholar belongs to determines whether he can establish new usul, derive rulings within the madhhab, or only address gaps not covered by existing texts. This lesson ensures you can place any Hanafi scholar in the correct tier.

Guided Path
1
Understand the layers framework
Grasp that the Hanafi school ranks jurists by their level of ijtihad: absolute (in shar‘), within the madhhab, and within issues with no narration.
Ibn Kamal Basha enumerated seven layers; this lesson focuses on the top three as they are foundational.
2
Identify the first layer: mujtahid fi al-shar‘
These are absolute mujtahids who establish their own usul from primary sources and are not bound by any previous scholar. They include the four founding imams and those who follow their method.
No taqlid in furu or usul.
3
Identify the second layer: mujtahid fi al-madhhab
These jurists follow the usul of the imam (Abu Hanifa) but can derive rulings and differ on furu. Examples: Abu Yusuf, Imam Muhammad.
They are bound by the imam's usul but can exercise ijtihad in new cases.
4
Identify the third layer: mujtahid fi al-masā’il
These jurists can only rule on issues for which there is no explicit ruling from the founder. They rely on the principles of the school. Examples: al-Khassaf, al-Tahawi.
They cannot contradict established rulings of the school.
5
Apply the hierarchy in practice
When consulting a Hanafi work, first identify the author's layer to understand the weight of his opinion. A fatwa must be based on the highest available authority unless a later consensus overrides.
A mufti must never claim a level above his own.
