أصول الإفتاء
1.8
طبقات الفقهاء
الزيادة عليها في الحكاية عنهم. وأمّا الغالب على أهل خراسان، ولا سيما ما وراء النهر في القرون الوسطى والمتأخرة، فهو المغالاة في الترفّع على غيرهم، وإعجاب حالهم ... فلقبوا بالألقاب النبيلة، ووصفوا بالأوصاف الجليلة، مثل شمس الأئمة، وفخر الإسلام، وصدر الشريعة، واستمر الحال فى أخلافهم على ذلك المنوال..... فإذا ذكروا واحداً من أنفسهم بالغُوا في وصفه وقالوا: الشيخ الإمام الأجل الزاهد الفقيه ونحو ذلك، وإذا نقلوا كلاماً من غيرهم فلا يزيدون على مثل قولهم: قال الكرخي، والجصاص، وربما يقتدى بهم من عداهم ممن يتلقى منهم الكلام، فيظن الجاهل بأحوال الرّجال، ومراتبهم فى الكمال، وطبقات العلماء، ودرجات الفقهاء، ظن سوء، فيأخذ في الاستدلال بنباهة الأوصاف على نباهة الموصوف، فيحمله ذلك على الإنكار بما عداهم، واستخفاف رجال الله سواهم. وقد كان ابن الكمال على ولاية عمل الإفتاء من جهة الدولة، فأحرجه ذلك إلى مراجعة كتب الفتاوى، والإكثار من مطالعة ما فيها في تحصيل أربه، والتخلّص عن كربه، ووقع نظره فيما سار به أهل ما وراء النهر من رفع أنفسهم والوضع من غيرهم، فانتزع إليهم. قال العبد الضعيف عفا الله عنه: إن كان التقسيم الذي ذكره ابن كمال باشا للوظائف، لا للأشخاص كما قدمنا، فربما يرتفع الإشكال الذي ذكره الإمامان اللكنوى والمرجاني رحمهما الله تعالى، حيث إن كونَ القدوري وصاحب الهداية من أصحاب الترجيح لا ينافي كونهما من المجتهدين في المسائل (1). وإن سبب ذكرهما في عداد أصحاب الترجيح راجع إلى ما كثر في كتبهما من ترجيح بعض روايات المذهب على بعض، وليس معنى ذلك أنهما غير قادرين على الاجتهاد في المسائل. والله سبحانه أعلم.
الملاحظة الرابعة أن ما ذكره ابن كمال باشا رحمه الله تعالى في الطبقة السابعة، إنما يُريدُ به مؤلّفى الكتب التى لا اعتماد عليها في الفتوى، مثل القنية والقُهستانى وغيرها مما سيأتي تفصيله إن شاء الله تعالى، ولذلك قال: "ويل لمن قلّدهم كل الويل." وقد ذكر ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى أن أصحاب الطبقة الثالثة والرابعة والخامسة من الطبقات السبعة التي ذكرها ابن كمال باشا (یعنی المجتهدين فى المسائل وأصحاب التخريج وأصحاب الترجيح) داخلون في معنى
(1) هو شمس الدين محمد بن حسام الدين القهستاني الحنفي، ( ضبطه السمعانى بضم القاف والهاء وسكون السين المهملة، وضبطه الحموي في معجم البلدان بكسر الهاء، وهو الأوفق بأصله الفارسي) نسبة إلى قهستان وهي ناحية بخراسان بين هراة ،ونيسابور فيما بين الجبال، وهي كوهستان بمعنى مواضع من الجبل، فعرب فقيل قهستان فتحها عبد الله بن عامر بن كريز، في سنة ٢٩ من.. الهجرة، في خلافة سيدنا عثمان رضي الله عنه كما في الأنساب للسمعاني ٤ / ٥٦٤) كان مفتيا ببخارا، وهو من شركاء المولى عصام الدين من تصانيفه جامع الرموز في شرح النقاية مختصر الوقاية، وجامع المباني في شرح فقه الكيداني، وشرح مقدمة الصلاة وكلها في فروع الفقه الحنفي. لكن قال المولى عصام الدين في حق القهستاني: إنه لم يكن من تلامذة شيخ الإسلام الهروي لا من أعاليهم ولا أدانيهم، وإنّما كان دلال الكتب في زمانه، ولا كان يعرف بالفقه ولا غيره بين أقرانه، ويؤيده أنه يجمع في شرحه هذا بين الغث والسمين والصحيح والضعيف من غير تحقيق ولا تصحيح وتدقيق." (كشف الظنون ج ۲ ص (۱۹۷۲) وهناك اختلاف في تاريخ وفاته، فذكر ابن العماد في شذرات الذهب ( ج ۱۰ ص ٤۳۰) أنه توفّي في حدود سنة ٩٥٣ هـ ، وذكر حاجي خليفة في (ج۱۰) ٤٣٠) كشف الظنون (ج۲ ص ۱۹۷۲) أنه توفى سنة ٩٦٢ هـ، وقيل سنة ٩٥٠ هـ. (ملخص من شذرات الذهب ج ١٠ ص ٤٣٠ ومعجم المؤلفين ۹ / ۱۷۹ وكشف الظنون ج ۲ ص ۱۹۷۲)
Principles of Ifta
1.8
Layers of Jurists
Exaggeration in reporting about them. As for the common practice among the people of Khurasan, especially Transoxiana in the middle and later centuries, it is excess in elevating themselves over others and self-admiration... So they gave themselves noble titles and described themselves with grand descriptions, such as Shams al-A'immah, Fakhr al-Islam, Sadr al-Shari'ah, and this practice continued among their successors on that path... So when they mention one of themselves, they exaggerate in describing him and say: the Shaykh, the Imam, the most venerable, the ascetic, the jurist, and the like, and when they quote speech from others, they do not add more than saying: al-Karkhi said, or al-Jassas, and perhaps others who take speech from them follow them, so the ignorant person about the conditions of men, their ranks in perfection, the layers of scholars, and the degrees of jurists thinks ill, and begins to infer from the prominence of descriptions the prominence of the described, and that leads him to deny others and to belittle other men of Allah. Ibn Kamal, who was in charge of the office of ifta by the state, was compelled to refer to fatwa books and to read extensively in them to achieve his goal and relieve his distress, and his eye fell upon the practice of the people of Transoxiana of elevating themselves and belittling others, so he inclined towards them. The weak slave, may Allah forgive him, said: If the division that Ibn Kamal Pasha mentioned is for functions, not for persons as we explained, then perhaps the objection raised by the two imams, al-Laknawi and al-Marjani, may Allah have mercy on them, is resolved, for that al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah are among the as-hab al-tarjih does not negate that they are among the mujtahidun fi al-masa'il (1). The reason for mentioning them among the as-hab al-tarjih is due to the abundance in their books of giving preponderance to some narrations of the madhhab over others, and it does not mean that they are incapable of ijtihad in the issues. And Allah Most High knows best.
The fourth observation: What Ibn Kamal Pasha, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned in the seventh layer, he only means the authors of books that are not relied upon in fatwa, such as al-Qunyah and al-Qahistani and others, whose details will come later, Allah willing. Therefore he said: "Woe to whoever follows them, all woe." And Ibn Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned that the people of the third, fourth, and fifth layers of the seven layers that Ibn Kamal Pasha mentioned (i.e., the mujtahidun fi al-masa'il, the as-hab al-takhrij, and the as-hab al-tarjih) are included in the meaning
(1) He is Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Husam al-Din al-Qahistani al-Hanafi... (biography continues) ... (Summarized from Shadharat al-Dhahab, etc.)
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage addresses two interrelated issues: the improper exaggeration in praising scholars among later Hanafis of Khurasan and Transoxiana, and the correct understanding of Ibn Kamal Pasha's classification of mujtahid layers. The author, Muhammad Taqi Usmani, begins by criticizing the practice of bestowing grand titles (e.g., Shams al-A'immah, Fakhr al-Islam) on their own scholars while only naming earlier figures like al-Karkhi and al-Jassas without such fanfare. This leads ignorant people to wrongly assess scholarly rank. He then relates how Ibn Kamal Pasha, as the official mufti, was forced to consult fatwa books and noted this self-aggrandizing tendency among Transoxianan scholars.
The core of the lesson is the clarification of Ibn Kamal's tabaqat (layers). The author resolves an objection by Laknawi and Marjani: they thought it problematic that al-Quduri (author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri) and al-Marghinani (author of al-Hidayah) are listed as 'as-hab al-tarjih' (those who give preponderance) rather than as higher-level mujtahids. The author explains that this classification is based on the function of their books—which contain many preponderations—not on their personal capacity; they were indeed capable of ijtihad but their written works served the role of tarjih. Thus there is no contradiction.
The fourth observation specifies that Ibn Kamal's seventh (lowest) layer refers specifically to authors of unreliable fatwa books, such as al-Qunyah and al-Qahistani, about whom Ibn Kamal said 'woe to whoever follows them.' The author then quotes Ibn Abidin to remind that the third, fourth, and fifth layers (mujtahidun fi al-masa'il, as-hab al-takhrij, as-hab al-tarjih) are all reliable sources, and that the seventh layer is an exception of unreliable compilations. The footnote provides a biography of al-Qahistani, noting that he was not a recognized scholar but a book dealer, and his works mix weak and strong without discernment, confirming why his books are not reliable for fatwa.
This lesson guards against two pitfalls: excessive veneration of later scholars based on titles, and the opposite error of dismissing capable mujtahids like al-Quduri and al-Marghinani as mere compilers. The rule for a mufti is to recognize the hierarchy: rely on the works of mujtahidun fi al-masa'il (3rd layer), as-hab al-takhrij (4th), and as-hab al-tarjih (5th), and avoid using books of the 7th layer such as Qahistani's unless verified.

Key Terms
طبقات الفقهاء (Tabaqat al-Fuqaha): The hierarchical classification of Hanafi jurists into layers based on their level of ijtihad and authority in the madhhab, as systematized by Ibn Kamal Pasha.
أصحاب الترجيح (As-hab al-Tarjih): Those jurists who are capable of giving preponderance to one narration or opinion of the madhhab over another, typically from among the later scholars like al-Quduri and al-Marghinani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why are al-Quduri and al-Marghinani classified as as-hab al-tarjih rather than mujtahidun fi al-masa'il?
A) Because they were not capable of performing ijtihad.
B) Because their books contain many preponderances of narrations, and Ibn Kamal's classification is by function, not person.
C) Because they lived in a later period when ijtihad was closed.
D) Because they were followers of Abu Hanifa and not independent mujtahids.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Kamal's classification of Hanafi mujtahid layers is by function, not personal capacity; al-Quduri and al-Marghinani are both mujtahids and preponderators, and their works are authoritative for fatwa.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Classification of Mujtahids: Independent and Affiliated
Explains hierarchy and a key dispute on fatwa authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a mujtahid mutlaq mustaqill and a mujtahid mutlaq muntasib, and apply the Hanafi rule for giving fatwa based on the hierarchy of jurists.

Core Idea
Fatwa authority depends on the jurist's rank; the Imam's statement is primary but later scholars' informed preferences are not dismissed.

This lesson unpacks the hierarchical classification of mujtahids as presented in Rasm al-Mufti. Understanding these ranks is essential for a mufti to know which opinions carry authoritative weight. We will also explore a nuanced dispute among Hanafi scholars: should a mufti always adhere to the Imam's statement, or can he follow the tarjih of later scholars? The passage provides the foundation for answering this question.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ranks of mujtahid
Locate the definitions of mujtahid mutlaq mustaqill and mujtahid mutlaq muntasib in the passage. Note the key difference: the former is independent of any madhhab, the latter follows the method of an imam without blind imitation.
The passage discusses these from the Shafi'i perspective, but the concept applies across all madhhabs.
2
Analyze the Hanafi position on relying on later scholars
The passage contrasts Ibn Nujaym's view (fatwa always follows the Imam's statement even if later scholars disagree) with the author's view (later scholars' tarjih is based on knowledge and can be relied upon). Identify the rationale behind each position.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
3
Apply the hierarchy in fatwa practice
Consider a scenario where a later Hanafi scholar (like al-Haskafi) gives a preferred ruling that contradicts a statement of Abu Hanifa. Using the principles from this passage, decide which opinion to give in fatwa and justify your choice.
The mufta bihi in most cases remains the Imam's statement, but later tarjih may be considered if it is well-supported.

أصول الإفتاء
طبقات الفقهاء
المجتهد في المذهب. ثم قال رحمه الله تعالى: "وإن من عداهم يكتفى بالنقل، فإن علينا اتباع ما نقلوه لنا عنهم من استنباطاتهم الغير المنصوصة عن المتقدمين، ومن ترجيحاتهم، ولو كانت لغير قول الإمام ... لأنهم لم يُرجحوا ما رجّحوه جزافاً. وإنما رجّحوا بعد اطلاعهم على المأخذ، كما شهدت مصنفاتهم بذلك، خلافاً لما قاله في البحر.
شرح عقود رسم المفتى ص ٥٤ والذي قاله ابن نجيم في البحر أنه لا يفتي بقول المشايخ بخلاف قول الإمام، بل الفتوى على قول الإمام دائما وإن خالفه المشايخ. راجع البحر الرائق، كتاب القضاء ٦:٤٥.
طبقات الفقهاء الشافعية
وكما قسم الحنفية فقهاءهم على أقسام سبعة مذكورة فيما سبق، فالشافعية قسموا فقهاءهم على خمس طبقات فصلها الحافظ ابن الصلاح رحمه الله تعالى. فالطبقة الأولى هي طبقة المجتهد المطلق المستقل، وقد عرفه ابن الصلاح رحمه الله تعالى بقوله: "هو الذي يستقل بإدراك الأحكام الشرعية من الأدلة الشرعية من غير تقليد وتقيد بمذهب أحد". وقوله "الذي يستقل" خرج به المجتهد المنتسب.
والطبقة الثانية: المجتهد المطلق المنتسب وهو الذي سبق بيانه من عبارة شرح المهذب للإمام النووي المنقولة عن أبي إسحق الإسفرائيني رحمهما الله تعالى من أنه إنما انتسب إلى الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى لأنه سلك مسلكه في الاجتهاد فوافق اجتهاده اجتهاد الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى لا أنه قلده. ويندرج فيه أمثال المزني وأبي ثور وابن المنذر رحمهم الله تعالى، كما ذكره النووي رحمه الله تعالى في مقدمة المجموع شرح المهذب.
ولكن قال ابن الصلاح رحمه الله تعالى: قلت: دعوى انتفاء التقليد عنهم مطلقاً من كل وجه لا يستقيم، إلا أن يكونوا قد أحاطوا بعلوم الاجتهاد المطلق، وفازوا برتبة المجتهدين المستقلين، وذلك لا يلائم المعلوم من أحوالهم أو أحوال أكثرهم. " ولعل مثل هذا التقليد في بعض المسائل لا ينافي كون الرجل مجتهداً مطلقاً، كما أسلفنا عن ابن القيم رحمه الله تعالى.
وقال ابن الصلاح رحمه الله تعالى بعد بيان هذا القسم: "فتوى المنتسبين"
الإمام أبو ثور هو إبراهيم بن خالد بن أبي اليمان الكلبي البغدادي الإمام الجليل، أحد الأئمة المجتهدين وصاحب مذهب مستقل، أبو ثور الفقيه الإمام، عده الإمام النووي من أصحاب الشافعية، لكن قال: ومع هذا الذي ذكرته من كون أبي ثور من أصحاب الشافعي، وأحد تلامذته... والناقلين كتابه، وأقواله فهو صاحب مذهب مستقل، لا يعد تفرده وجها في المذهب. وقال الحافظ ابن عبد البر رحمهما الله تعالى: "كان يذهب إلى مذهب أهل العراق وصحب الشافعي... وهو أكثر ميلاً إلى الشافعي في ذلك الكتاب وفي كتبه كلها." روى عنه الإمام مسلم بن الحجاج، وأكثر عنه في صحيحه توفي رحمه الله ببغداد سنة ٢٤٠ هـ. ملخص من تهذيب الأسماء واللغات ۲: ۲۰۰ و ۲۰۱ والانتقاء في فضائل الثلاثة الأئمة الفقهاء، في عداد أصحاب الإمام الشافعي الذين أخذوا عنه رحمهم الله ببغداد)
الإمام ابن المنذر الشافعي: الإمام الحافظ العلامة، شيخ الإسلام أبو بكر، محمد بن إبراهيم ابن المنذر النيسابوري الفقيه نزيل مكة، وصاحب التصانيف مثل "الإشراف في اختلاف العلماء"، وكتاب: "الإجماع"، وكتاب: "المبسوط"، وغير ذلك. ولد رحمه الله سنة ٢٤٢ هـ. قال الإمام النووي: "لا يلتزم التقيد في الاختيار مذهب أحد بعينه... بل يدور مع ظهور الدليل ودلالة السنة الصحيحة، ويقول بها مع من كانت، ومع هذا فهو عند أصحابنا معدود من أصحاب الشافعي، مذكور في جميع كتبهم في الطبقات." وتوفي رحمه الله بمكة سنة ٣٠٩ هـ. ملخص من سير أعلام النبلاء ١٤: ٤٩٠ إلى ٤٩٢، وتهذيب الأسماء واللغات ۲: ۱۹۶ و ۱۹۷ والأعلام ٥: ٢٩٤.
المجموع ۱:۷۲
The foundations of issuing fatwas: Categories of Jurists. The mujtahid within the madhhab. Then he (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And as for others besides them, they suffice with transmission, for we must follow what they have transmitted to us from them of their deductions not explicitly stated by the earlier scholars, and of their preferences, even if those preferences were against the statement of the Imam... because they did not prefer what they preferred haphazardly. Rather, they gave preference after having access to the legal bases, as their works testify, contrary to what was said in al-Bahr.' Explanation of 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti p. 54: What Ibn Nujaym said in al-Bahr is that one does not give fatwa according to the statements of the later scholars contrary to the Imam's statement; rather, fatwa is always according to the Imam's statement even if the later scholars contradict him. Refer to al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Book of Judgments, 6:45. Categories of Shafi'i Jurists: Just as the Hanafis divided their jurists into seven categories mentioned previously, the Shafi'is divided their jurists into five categories, detailed by al-Hafiz Ibn al-Salah, may Allah have mercy on him. The first category is the category of the absolute independent mujtahid, and Ibn al-Salah defined him saying: 'He is the one who independently comprehends the legal rulings from the legal evidences without taqlid and without adhering to any one madhhab.' And his statement 'the one who independently' excludes the affiliated mujtahid. The second category: the absolute affiliated mujtahid, which was previously explained in the words of Sharh al-Muhadhdhab by Imam al-Nawawi, transmitted from Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, may Allah have mercy on them both, that he only affiliated himself to al-Shafi'i because he followed his method in ijtihad, so his ijtihad agreed with the ijtihad of al-Shafi'i, not because he followed him blindly. Included in this category are examples such as al-Muzani, Abu Thawr, and Ibn al-Mundhir, may Allah have mercy on them, as mentioned by al-Nawawi in the introduction to al-Majmu' Sharh al-Muhadhdhab. However, Ibn al-Salah said: 'I say: The claim of absolute freedom from taqlid on all fronts is not sound, unless they had encompassed the sciences of absolute ijtihad and attained the rank of independent mujtahids, and that does not match what is known of their conditions or the conditions of most of them.' 'Perhaps such taqlid in some matters does not negate a person being an absolute mujtahid, as we previously mentioned from Ibn al-Qayyim.' Ibn al-Salah said after explaining this category: 'The fatwa of the affiliates...' [Biographical notes on Abu Thawr and Ibn al-Mundhir follow.] Al-Majmu' 1:72.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage from 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti (with its commentary) discusses the classification of jurists (tabaqat al-fuqaha), which is a core topic in the principles of ifta. The author begins by referencing the Hanafi classification (seven categories) and then turns to the Shafi'i classification (five categories) as detailed by Ibn al-Salah. The passage first addresses the level of independent absolute mujtahid (mujtahid mutlaq mustaqill), defined as one who derives rulings directly from the sources without taqlid to any school. Then it discusses the affiliated absolute mujtahid (mujtahid mutlaq muntasib), who follows the method of a specific imam (al-Shafi'i) not out of blind imitation but because his own ijtihad coincidentally aligns with that imam's approach. Ibn al-Salah critiques the idea that such mujtahids are entirely free from taqlid, noting that absolute independence is unlikely for most. The passage includes biographical details of Abu Thawr and Ibn al-Mundhir, who are considered affiliated mujtahids. The Hanafi perspective on the hierarchy of jurists is similar, emphasizing that the later scholars (mashayikh) are not completely independent but their preferences are given weight. A key practical point is that the fatwa is always based on the Imam's (Abu Hanifa's) statement, even if later scholars disagree, as stated by Ibn Nujaym. This classification helps muftis know the authority of different rulings.

Key Terms
مجتهد مطلق مستقل (mujtahid mutlaq mustaqill): A jurist who independently derives rulings from the primary sources without adhering to any specific madhhab.
مجتهد مطلق منتسب (mujtahid mutlaq muntasib): A jurist who follows the methodology of a particular imam (e.g., al-Shafi'i) but exercises independent ijtihad within that framework, not performing blind taqlid.
طبقات الفقهاء (tabaqat al-fuqaha): Hierarchical classification of jurists based on their level of ijtihad and authority in deriving legal rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn al-Salah's classification, what distinguishes an 'absolute independent mujtahid' from an 'absolute affiliated mujtahid'?
A) The independent mujtahid does not adhere to any madhhab, while the affiliated one follows a specific imam's methodology.
B) The independent mujtahid is only from the Hanafi school, while the affiliated one is from the Shafi'i school.
C) The affiliated mujtahid is superior because he has a chain of transmission.
D) There is no distinction; both are the same level.

Key Takeaway
The classification of mujtahids into independent and affiliated ranks is essential for determining the authority of their opinions, and within the Hanafi school, the Imam's statement is primary but later scholars' informed tarjih may be considered.

The Independent Muqallid: Ruling on Their Fatwa
Concluding discussion with critique and reconciliation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the second category of mujtahids (mujtahid muntasib), evaluate the dispute over their independence, and apply the rule that their fatwa is valid for consensus and disagreement.

Core Idea
Limited taqlid does not negate absolute ijtihad – the fatwa of an independent muqallid is authoritative.

In the hierarchy of muftis, the second category comprises scholars who are mujtahids in their own right but affiliate with a particular imam. Al-Nawawi includes figures like al-Muzani, Abu Thawr, and Ibn al-Mundhir. However, Ibn al-Salah challenges their absolute independence, while Ibn al-Qayyim reconciles by asserting that partial taqlid does not preclude full ijtihad. This lesson examines the dispute and the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
The passage defines the second category of mujtahids: those who are independent in ijtihad but associate themselves with a specific imam (e.g., al-Muzani with al-Shafi'i). Recognize that they are not bound to the imam in all issues.
The term 'mujtahid muntasib' is key – note the nuance of affiliation without loss of independence.
2
Extract the defining characteristic
These scholars are mujtahid mutlaq (absolute) in their own right, yet they choose to follow an imam in some matters. Their work is considered part of the school's development.
Al-Nawawi includes them in the Shafi'i school despite their independence.
3
Analyze the dispute
Ibn al-Salah objects: they cannot be fully independent because they lack complete mastery of all ijtihad sciences. Contrast this with al-Nawawi's classification.
The dispute is methodological – what qualifies as absolute ijtihad?
4
Apply Ibn al-Qayyim's reconciliation
Ibn al-Qayyim argues that limited taqlid in some issues does not negate absolute ijtihad. This resolves the tension and supports the validity of their fatwa.
The principle: partial taqlid is compatible with overall independence.
5
Conclude the operative ruling
Ibn al-Salah himself rules that the fatwa of such scholars is acted upon and considered in consensus and disagreement – legally equivalent to that of fully independent mujtahids.
This is the mufta bihi position: their fatwa is authoritative.

Commentary
This passage concludes the discussion of the second category of mujtahids—those who are independent but still follow an imam in some matters. Al-Nawawi includes scholars like al-Muzani, Abu Thawr, and Ibn al-Mundhir in this category. Ibn al-Salah objects, arguing that claiming they are completely independent is untenable because they lack some tools of absolute ijtihad. Ibn al-Qayyim reconciles by stating that limited taqlid in some issues does not negate absolute ijtihad. Ibn al-Salah then rules that the fatwa of such scholars is valid and counts in consensus and disagreement, equating them legally to independent mujtahids. The footnotes provide biographical details of Abu Thawr and Ibn al-Mundhir, noting their independence and affiliation with the Shafi‘i school.

Key Terms
مجتهد منتسب (mujtahid muntasib): A mujtahid who is independent in his own right but associates himself with a particular imam's school.
تقليد (taqlid): Following the opinion of another without independent verification of the evidence.

The Restricted Mujtahid: Definition, Qualifications, and Takhrij
Defining the restricted mujtahid and his role in takhrij

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of a restricted mujtahid, identify his qualifications, and explain the first meaning of takhrij within a madhhab.

Core Idea
The restricted mujtahid derives rulings using his imam's principles but cannot challenge his imam's proofs.

In the hierarchy of mujtahids, the restricted mujtahid occupies a crucial middle ground. He is not merely a muqallid, nor is he fully independent. This lesson unpacks ibn al-Salah's description of the restricted mujtahid and his primary function: takhrij. Understanding this category is essential for anyone who aspires to issue fatwa within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category and its defining feature
The restricted mujtahid works within his imam's principles; he does not go beyond them. He independently establishes the madhhab with evidence but is bound by the imam's usul.
Note the phrase 'لا يتجاوز في أدلته أصول إمامه وقواعده'.
2
List the qualifications required
He must be knowledgeable in fiqh, usul al-fiqh, detailed evidences, analogy, and trained in takhrij. However, he falls short in some tools like hadith or Arabic, which leaves a trace of taqlid.
Ibn al-Salah emphasizes knowledge of 'مسالك الأقيسة والمعاني'.
3
Understand the trace of taqlid
Because he lacks full mastery in hadith or Arabic, he does not independently verify every evidence but relies on his imam's proofs. He does not search for counter-evidence or fully examine conditions.
This distinguishes him from the independent mujtahid.
4
Explain the function of takhrij
Takhrij means deriving rulings for new cases when the imam has no explicit text. The restricted mujtahid finds evidence of the type his imam would use and applies the imam's principles.
The passage states 'يُخرج حكمها على وفق أصوله'.
5
Note the first meaning of takhrij
When there is no text from the imam, the restricted mujtahid analogizes using the imam's principles by finding evidence that meets his imam's conditions.
The second meaning is not mentioned in this excerpt.

ثم ذكر رحمه الله تعالى فوائد مهمة بالنسبة إلى هذا القسم. منها: أنّه قد يُوجد من المجتهد المقيد الاستقلال بالاجتهاد والفتوى في
مسئلةٍ خاصة أو باب خاص، كما تقدم في النوع الذي قبله.
ومنها: أنّ مثل هذا المجتهد المقيّد من وظائفه التخريج على مذهب إمامه، والتخريج له معنيان: الأول: أن لا يكون في مسئلة نص من إمامه، فيُخرج حكمها على وفق أصوله، بأن يجد دليلاً من جنس ما يحتج به إمامه، وعلى شرطه
The third class: the restricted mujtahid: he is one who independently establishes the madhhab of his imam with evidence, but he does not go beyond the principles and rules of his imam in his proofs. Ibn al-Salah said: 'His characteristic is that he is knowledgeable in fiqh, expert in usul al-fiqh, knows the detailed evidences of rulings, insightful in the paths of analogies and meanings, fully trained in takhrij and deduction, capable of attaching what is not explicitly stated in his imam's madhhab to the principles and rules of his madhhab, and he is not free from some taqlid because he falls short in some sciences and tools required of the independent mujtahid, such as deficiency in hadith or Arabic. Often these two sciences are deficient in the people of restricted ijtihad. He takes his imam's texts as principles from which he deduces, like what the independent does with the texts of the Lawgiver, and perhaps he encounters a ruling that his imam mentioned with its evidence, so he suffices with that, and does not investigate whether there is a counter-evidence, nor does he fully examine its conditions as the independent does. This is the description of the people of wujuh and turuq in the madhhab, and on this description were our leading scholars or most of them.' Then he mentioned important benefits regarding this category. Among them: that a restricted mujtahid may occasionally have independent ijtihad and fatwa in a specific issue or chapter, as earlier in the preceding type. And among them: that from the functions of such a restricted mujtahid is takhrij on his imam's madhhab, and takhrij has two meanings: first: that there is no text from his imam on an issue, so he derives its ruling according to his [imam's] principles, by finding evidence of the type that his imam would use, and on his condition.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage defines the third category: the restricted mujtahid (al-mujtahid al-muqayyad). Unlike the independent mujtahid, he works entirely within the framework of his imam's usul and qawaid. Ibn al-Salah lists his qualifications: deep knowledge of fiqh and usul, ability to perform takhrij, but he is deficient in some areas like hadith or Arabic, hence a trace of taqlid remains. This describes the 'as-hab al-wujuh wa al-turuq' (scholars of aspects and paths) in the madhhab. The text then notes two benefits: (1) a restricted mujtahid might still achieve independent ijtihad in a particular issue or chapter; (2) his primary function is takhrij—extending the madhhab to new cases. The first meaning of takhrij is when the imam has no explicit text, so the mujtahid derives a ruling using the imam's principles and types of evidence.

Key Terms
مجتهد مقيد (mujtahid muqayyad): A mujtahid who works within the principles and rules of his imam, lacking some independent ijtihad tools.
تخريج (takhrij): Deriving rulings for new cases by analogy to the imam's principles when no explicit text exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Lack of knowledge of fiqh.
B) Deficiency in hadith or Arabic language.
C) Inability to perform analogy.
D) Lack of access to his imam's books.

Key Takeaway
The restricted mujtahid exercises ijtihad within his imam's framework but retains a trace of taqlid due to deficiency in some tools like hadith or Arabic.

The Restricted Mujtahid: Definition and Qualifications
Definition and characteristics of the restricted mujtahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the restricted mujtahid, list his qualifications, and distinguish him from an absolute mujtahid.

Core Idea
A restricted mujtahid derives rulings within his imam's framework but lacks full independence.

The second highest level of mujtahids in the Hanafi hierarchy is the restricted mujtahid (al-mujtahid al-muqayyad). Unlike the absolute mujtahid, he operates within the boundaries of his imam's principles and does not possess mastery in every required discipline. This lesson unpacks his definition, qualifications, and function in the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Third Class
Locate the definition of the third class of mujtahids in the passage. Note that it is introduced after the independent mujtahid.
2
Parse the Qualifications
List the conditions mentioned: knowledge of fiqh, usul, evidences, methods of analogy, ability in takhrij, and adherence to imam's principles.
Notice the deficiency in hadith or Arabic as a distinguishing factor.
3
Understand the Role
The restricted mujtahid uses his imam's texts as principles to derive rulings, similar to how an independent mujtahid uses the Quran and Sunnah, but without full scrutiny of evidence.
He may simply accept the imam's ruling with its evidence without checking for counter-evidence.
4
Recognize the Subcategories
The passage mentions 'as'hab al-wujuh' and those of 'turuq' as examples. Note that these are scholars who produce distinct takhrij.
This connects to the next lesson on takhrij.

ثم ذكر رحمه الله تعالى فوائد مهمة بالنسبة إلى هذا القسم. منها: أنّه قد يُوجد من المجتهد المقيد الاستقلال بالاجتهاد والفتوى في مسئلةٍ خاصة أو باب خاص، كما تقدم في النوع الذي قبله.
ومنها: أنّ مثل هذا المجتهد المقيّد من وظائفه التخريج على مذهب إمامه، والتخريج له معنيان: الأول: أن لا يكون في مسئلة نص من إمامه، فيُخرج حكمها على وفق أصوله، بأن يجد دليلاً من جنس ما يحتج به إمامه، وعلى شرطه فيفتى بموجبه. وفي هذه الحالة قد يكون تخريجه مخالفاً لتخريج غيره من الأصحاب، وحينئذٍ يُسمّى كل واحد من التخريجين "وجها" في الاصطلاح، وهؤلاء "أصحاب الوجوه" والمعنى الثاني من التخريج أن يوجد من الإمام نصان مختلفان فى صورتين مختلفتين، وكلاهما يمكن أن يُخرج منه الحكم فى الصورة المطلوبة، فيختار هذا المجتهد أحد النصين للتخريج على أساسه، فهذا القول يُسمّى "مُخرَّجا" وشرط التخريج المذكور عند اختلاف النصين ألا يجد بين المسئلتين فارقاً، ولاحاجة في مثل ذلك إلى علةٍ جامعة، وهو من قبيل إلحاق الأمة بالعبد في قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: من أعتق شركاله فى عبدٍ قُوم عليه" ومهما أمكنه الفرق بين المسئلتين، لم يجزله على الأصح التخريج، ولزمه تقرير النصين على ظاهر هما معتمداً على الفارق. وكثيراًما يختلفون فى القول بالتخريج في مثل ذلك لاختلافهم في إمكان الفرق
ومنها: أنّه إن أفتى مثل هذا المجتهد فى مسئلةٍ غير منصوصة من إمامه ولكن خرج المسئلة حسب ما ذكرنا فهل العامل بفتياه يعتبر مقلدا لإمامه أم مقلد الهذا المجتهد المقيد؟ فاختار إمام الحرمين الجُوَيْنى وابن الصلاح أنه يُعتبر مُقلّداً لإمامه، لأن القولَ مُخرَّج على أصوله. وخالفهم الشيخ أبو إسحق الشيرازي رحمهم الله تعالى، وقال: إنّه لا يجوز أن تُنسب تلك المسئلة
Jurist Tabaqat. In this situation concerning the ruling of the fatwa of the independent absolute mujtahid, it is acted upon and considered in consensus and disagreement. The third class: the restricted mujtahid: He is the one who independently determines the madhhab of his imam with evidence, but he does not go beyond in his evidence the principles and rules of his imam. Ibn al-Salah (may Allah have mercy on him) said: "His description is that he is knowledgeable in fiqh, expert in usul al-fiqh, cognizant of the detailed evidences of rulings, insightful in the methods of analogies and meanings, fully practiced in takhrij and derivation, capable of appending what is not explicitly stated in the madhhab of his imam to the principles and rules of his madhhab, and he is not free from a tinge of taqlid towards him because of his deficiency in some sciences and tools considered for the independent mujtahid, such as being deficient in hadith or Arabic language. Deficiency in these two sciences is frequent among those of restricted ijtihad. He takes the texts of his imam as principles from which he derives just as the independent mujtahid does with the texts of the Lawgiver. Sometimes a ruling occurs to him that his imam has mentioned with its evidence, so he suffices with that and does not investigate whether that evidence has any contradiction, and he does not fulfill the scrutiny of its conditions as the independent mujtahid does. This is the description of the "as'hab al-wujuh" and the "turuq" in the madhhab, and upon this description were the imams of our companions or most of them." Then he (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned important benefits concerning this category. Among them: that it is possible for the restricted mujtahid to have independence in ijtihad and fatwa in a specific issue or specific chapter, as preceded in the previous type. Among them: that among the functions of this restricted mujtahid is takhrij upon the madhhab of his imam. Takhrij has two meanings: First: that there is no text from his imam regarding an issue, so he derives its ruling according to his principles, by finding evidence of the kind that his imam uses and upon his condition, then he gives fatwa accordingly. In this case, his takhrij may differ from the takhrij of other companions, and then each of the two takhrij is called a "wajh" in terminology, and these are the "as'hab al-wujuh". The second meaning of takhrij: that there exist from the imam two different texts in two different situations, and both can be used to derive the ruling in the desired situation, so this mujtahid selects one of the two texts for takhrij based on it, so this statement is called "mukharraj". The condition for the mentioned takhrij when texts differ is that he finds no difference between the two issues, and there is no need in such a case for a unifying effective cause. It is like annexing a female slave to a male slave in the hadith: "Whoever emancipates his share in a male slave, he is valued." And if he can make a difference between the two issues, it is not permissible for him, according to the most correct view, to do takhrij, and he must leave the two texts as they are, relying on the difference. Often they differ regarding the permissibility of takhrij in such cases due to their difference in the possibility of a difference. Among them: that if such a mujtahid gives a fatwa in an issue not explicitly stated by his imam, but he derived the issue as we mentioned, is the one acting upon his fatwa considered a muqallid of his imam or a muqallid of this restricted mujtahid? Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and Ibn al-Salah chose that he is considered a muqallid of his imam, because the statement is derived upon his principles. They were opposed by Sheikh Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi (may Allah have mercy on them), who said: it is not permissible to attribute that issue...
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage defines the third level of jurists in the Hanafi mufti hierarchy: the restricted mujtahid (al-mujtahid al-muqayyad). It begins by contrasting it with the absolute independent mujtahid mentioned earlier. The restricted mujtahid is one who is capable of independently establishing the rulings of his imam (e.g., Abu Hanifa) using evidence, but he does not go beyond the principles and rules of his imam. He is knowledgeable in fiqh and usul al-fiqh but may lack proficiency in some auxiliary sciences like hadith or Arabic, which prevents him from being an independent mujtahid. He uses his imam's texts as principles for derivation, similar to how an independent mujtahid uses the primary sources. However, he may simply accept his imam's ruling and evidence without checking for counter-evidence or conditions. The text identifies such scholars as 'as'hab al-wujuh (people of specific views) and those following the methods (turuq) of the madhhab. The author then lists important points regarding this category. First, sometimes a restricted mujtahid may exhibit independence in a specific issue or chapter. Second, his primary function is takhrij, which has two meanings: (a) when there is no explicit text from the imam on an issue, he derives the ruling by finding evidence in line with the imam's method; such derivations are called 'wajh' (plural 'wujuh'), and the scholars doing this are 'as'hab al-wujuh'. (b) When the imam has two conflicting texts on different cases, the mujtahid selects one of them to apply to a new case; this derived ruling is called 'mukharraj'. The condition for this second type is that there is no discernible difference between the original and new cases; if a difference is found, takhrij is not permissible and both texts must be applied as they are, based on the distinguishing factor. Third, there is a dispute regarding the follower of such a fatwa: is he imitating the imam or the restricted mujtahid? Juwayni and Ibn al-Salah (Shafi'is) hold that he imitates the imam because the ruling is derived from the imam's principles. Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi (also Shafi'i) disagrees, implying the follower imitates the restricted mujtahid. The author presents both views without explicit preference.

Key Terms
المجتهد المقيّد (al-mujtahid al-muqayyad): A mujtahid who independently establishes his imam's madhhab with evidence but does not go beyond his imam's principles and rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary deficiency that separates a restricted mujtahid from an absolute mujtahid according to the passage?
A) Lack of knowledge in fiqh
B) Lack of knowledge in hadith or Arabic
C) Inability to perform qiyas
D) Inability to read Arabic

Key Takeaway
The restricted mujtahid is a key figure in the Hanafi madhhab, deriving rulings within the imam's framework while lacking full independence due to deficiencies in subsidiary sciences.

Takhrij in the Hanafi Madhhab: Two Meanings and a Taqlid Dispute
Functions of restricted mujtahid: takhrij (two types) and a dispute on taqlid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two types of takhrij, apply the condition for the second type, and analyze the dispute on who the follower imitates.

Core Idea
Takhrij extends the madhhab by deriving new rulings from principles or by choosing between conflicting texts when no difference exists.

The restricted mujtahid's primary function is takhrij (derivation). This lesson explores its two meanings: deriving from principles when no text exists, and selecting between two conflicting texts of the imam. It also presents a dispute among Shafi'i scholars about whom the follower imitates, a discussion relevant to Hanafi usul as well.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Meanings
Find where the passage discusses the two meanings of takhrij. Note the first: no text from the imam, derive from principles. The second: two conflicting texts, select one.
2
Understand the Condition for the Second Type
The condition is that there should be no difference (farq) between the two original cases. If a difference exists, takhrij is not allowed and both texts are applied based on the distinguishing factor.
The passage gives an example from a hadith about emancipating a share in a slave to illustrate the concept of annexing a case to another when no difference exists.
3
Analyze the Taqlid Dispute
The passage presents a dispute: when a restricted mujtahid issues a fatwa on a new case via takhrij, is the follower imitating the imam or the mujtahid? Juwayni and Ibn al-Salah say the imam; Shirazi says the follower cannot attribute to the imam.
The Hanafi position is not explicitly stated, but the author may lean towards Juwayni's view.
4
Apply the Concept
Work through a hypothetical: If Abu Hanifa has two rulings on different cases, can a restricted mujtahid use them to derive a third?
Check if there is a significant difference between the cases.

في هذه الحالة فى حكم فتوى المجتهد المستقل المطلق، يُعمل بها ويُعتد بها في الإجماع والخلاف " الطبقة الثالثة: المجتهد المقيّد: وهو الذى يستقل بتقرير مذهب إمامه بالدليل، غير أنه لا يتجاوز في أدلته أصول إمامه وقواعده، قال ابن الصلاح رحمه الله تعالى: "ومن شأنه أن يكون عالماً بالفقه، خبيراً بأصول الفقه، عارفاً بأدلة الأحكام تفصيلاً بصيراً بمسالك الأقيسة والمعاني، تام الارتياض في التخريج والاستنباط، قيماً بإلحاق ما ليس بمنصوص عليه في مذهب إمامه بأصول مذهبه وقواعده ولا يعرى عن شوب من التقليد له لإخلاله ببعض العلوم والأدوات المعتبرة في المستقل، مثل أن يُخل بعلم الحديث أو بعلم اللغة العربية. وكثيراً ما وقع الإخلال بهذين العلمين في أهل الاجتهاد المقيد. ويتخذ نصوص إمامه أصولاً يستنبط منها نحو ما يفعله المستقل بنصوص الشارع، وربما مرّ به الحكم وقد ذكره إمامه بدليله فيكتفى بذلك، ولا يبحث هل لذلك الدليل من معارض؟ ولا يستوفى النظر في شروطه كما يفعله المستقل. وهذه صفة أصحاب الوجوه والطُّرُق في المذهب، وعلى هذه الصفة كان أئمة أصحابنا أو أكثرهم."

Commentary
This passage defines the third level of jurists in the Hanafi mufti hierarchy: the restricted mujtahid (al-mujtahid al-muqayyad). It begins by contrasting it with the absolute independent mujtahid mentioned earlier. The restricted mujtahid is one who is capable of independently establishing the rulings of his imam (e.g., Abu Hanifa) using evidence, but he does not go beyond the principles and rules of his imam. He is knowledgeable in fiqh and usul al-fiqh but may lack proficiency in some auxiliary sciences like hadith or Arabic, which prevents him from being an independent mujtahid. He uses his imam's texts as principles for derivation, similar to how an independent mujtahid uses the primary sources. However, he may simply accept his imam's ruling and evidence without checking for counter-evidence or conditions. The text identifies such scholars as 'as'hab al-wujuh (people of specific views) and those following the methods (turuq) of the madhhab. The author then lists important points regarding this category. First, sometimes a restricted mujtahid may exhibit independence in a specific issue or chapter. Second, his primary function is takhrij, which has two meanings: (a) when there is no explicit text from the imam on an issue, he derives the ruling by finding evidence in line with the imam's method; such derivations are called 'wajh' (plural 'wujuh'), and the scholars doing this are 'as'hab al-wujuh'. Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi (also Shafi'i) disagrees, implying the follower imitates the restricted mujtahid. The author presents both views without explicit preference.

Key Terms
التخريج (al-takhrij): The process of deriving a ruling for a new case from the imam's existing texts or principles. Two meanings: (1) deriving from principles when no explicit text exists; (2) selecting between two conflicting texts of the imam for a new case.
أصحاب الوجوه (as'hab al-wujuh): Jurists who produce distinct takhrij (wajh) for a given issue, each deriving a different ruling based on the imam's principles.
مُخرَّج (mukharraj): A ruling derived from a choice between two conflicting texts of the imam, based on the absence of a significant difference between the cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the passage, when can a restricted mujtahid perform the second type of takhrij (selecting between two conflicting texts)?
A) When one text is stronger than the other
B) When he finds no difference between the two original cases
C) When he is authorized by the imam
D) When the two texts agree on the same ruling

Key Takeaway
Takhrij is a systematic method that allows the restricted mujtahid to expand the madhhab, but it is bound by strict conditions and leads to a dispute about attribution.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Takhrij: Its Two Meanings and Conditions
Explains two meanings of takhrij and condition for analogical extension.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two meanings of takhrij and identify the condition for valid takhrij when the Imam's texts differ.

Core Idea
Takhrij derives rulings from the Imam's principles; if no difference between cases, analogy is valid without a unifying cause.

The concept of takhrij is central to understanding how a restricted mujtahid (or 'muqallid mujtahid') extends the school's rulings to new cases. This passage from the usul al-iftaa literature clarifies two distinct meanings of takhrij: one that produces multiple 'wujuh' (aspects) within the school, and another that chooses between conflicting texts of the Imam. The condition for the latter is very specific—the absence of a perceived difference between the two cases.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two meanings of takhrij
First, a mujtahid derives a ruling differently from other scholars → each derivation is a 'wajh' and the scholars are 'ashab al-wujuh'. Second, when the Imam has two different texts on similar cases, the mujtahid chooses one to derive the ruling for a new case → that derived opinion is called 'mukharraj'.
The first meaning is more about ijtihad within the school; the second is about resolving apparent inconsistency in the Imam's texts.
2
Identify the condition for the second type of takhrij
The condition is that the mujtahid must not perceive any difference between the two cases (the Imam's original cases and the new case). If a difference exists, takhrij is not allowed and both texts must be applied as they are.
No unifying cause (illa) is needed if no difference is perceived; the analogy is direct (ilhāq).
3
Analyze the example given
The hadith 'Whoever frees a share he has in a slave, it is valued for him' is used as a basis for analogy to the case of a slave-girl. If there is no difference between the two cases, takhrij is valid.
This example illustrates takhrij without a unifying cause—just direct extension.
4
Note the dispute on the validity of takhrij when a difference is claimed
Scholars may differ on whether a difference exists; if they disagree, takhrij may be contested. The text says the correct opinion is that if a difference can be found, takhrij is not permitted.
This ties to the broader discussion of ikhtilaf in ilhāq.

بعض طبقات الفقهاء فيفتى بموجبه. وفي هذه الحالة قد يكون تخريجه مخالفاً لتخريج غيره من الأصحاب، وحينئذٍ يُسمّى كل واحد من التخريجين "وجها" في الاصطلاح، وهؤلاء "أصحاب الوجوه" والمعنى الثاني من التخريج أن يوجد من الإمام نصان مختلفان فى صورتين مختلفتين، وكلاهما يمكن أن يُخرج منه الحكم فى الصورة المطلوبة، فيختار هذا المجتهد أحد النصين للتخريج على أساسه، فهذا القول يُسمّى "مُخرَّجا" وشرط التخريج المذكور عند اختلاف النصين ألا يجد بين المسئلتين فارقاً، ولاحاجة في مثل ذلك إلى علةٍ جامعة، وهو من قبيل إلحاق الأمة بالعبد في قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "من أعتق شركاله فى عبدٍ قُوم عليه" ومهما أمكنه الفرق بين "من المسئلتين، لم يجزله على الأصح التخريج، ولزمه تقرير النصين على ظاهر هما معتمداً على الفارق. وكثيراًما يختلفون فى القول بالتخريج في مثل ذلك لاختلافهم في إمكان الفرق ومنها: أنّه إن أفتى مثل هذا المجتهد فى مسئلةٍ غير منصوصة من إمامه ولكن خرج المسئلة حسب ما ذكرنا فهل العامل بفتياه يعتبر مقلدا لإمامه أم مقلد الهذا المجتهد المقيد؟ فاختار إمام الحرمين الجُوَيْنى وابن الصلاح أنه يُعتبر مُقلّداً لإمامه، لأن القولَ مُخرَّج على أصوله. وخالفهم الشيخ أبو إسحق الشيرازي رحمهم الله تعالى، وقال: إنّه لا يجوز أن تُنسب تلك المسئلة إلى الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى. (1) (1) الإمام أبو إسحاق الشيرازي: إبراهيم بن على ابن يوسف بن عبد الله، إمام الشافعية في زمانه، أبو إسحاق الشيرازي، صاحب "المهذب" و"التنبيه"، وتكرر ذكره فى "الروضة". ولد سنة ٣٩٣ هـ ، وتمن تفقه عليه القاضي أبو الطيب الطبري رحمه الله شيخ الشافعية ببغداد في زمانه. وكان جامعا بين العلم والعمل مراعياً في عمله لدقائق الاحتياط، وكان مُجاب الدعوة، توفّي رحمه الله ببغداد سنة ٤٧٢ هـ . ملخص من تهذيب الأسماء واللغات ٢: ١٧٢ إلى ١٧٤)
Some classes of jurists: He gives fatwa accordingly. And in this case, his takhrij may differ from the takhrij of other companions, and then each of the two takhrij is called 'wajh' in terminology, and these are 'ashab al-wujuh'. The second meaning of takhrij is that there exist from the Imam two different texts in two different cases, and from both it is possible to derive the ruling in the requested case, so this mujtahid chooses one of the two texts for takhrij based on it. Thus this saying is called 'mukharraj'. The condition for the mentioned takhrij when the two texts differ is that he does not find a difference between the two issues, and there is no need in such a case for a unifying cause. It is like attaching the slave girl to the slave in his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever frees a share he has in a slave, it is valued for him.' And whenever he can find a difference between the two issues, it is not permissible for him to do takhrij according to the correct opinion, and he must affirm both texts in their apparent meaning relying on the difference. And often they differ on the validity of takhrij in such cases due to their difference in the possibility of finding a difference. And among them: If such a mujtahid gives a fatwa in a case not explicitly stated by his Imam, but he derived the case as we mentioned, then is the one who acts on his fatwa considered a muqallid of his Imam or a muqallid of this restricted mujtahid? Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and Ibn al-Salah chose that he is considered a muqallid of his Imam, because the statement is derived from his principles. They were opposed by Sheikh Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi (may Allah have mercy on them), who said: It is not permissible to attribute that case to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him). (1) (1) Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi: Ibrahim ibn Ali ibn Yusuf ibn Abdullah, Imam of the Shafi'is in his time, author of 'al-Muhadhdhab' and 'al-Tanbih', mentioned frequently in 'al-Rawda'. Born 393 AH, studied under Qadi Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari. He combined knowledge and action, careful in his practice, and his supplications were answered. He died in Baghdad in 472 AH. Summarized from Tahdhib al-Asma' wa al-Lughat 2:172-174.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage discusses the concept of 'takhrij' in the context of juristic classes. The author explains two meanings of takhrij: first, when a mujtahid derives a ruling differently from other scholars, each such derivation is called a 'wajh' (aspect), and the scholars are called 'ashab al-wujuh'. Second, when there exist two different texts from the Imam on two cases, and the mujtahid chooses one to derive the ruling for a new case, the derived opinion is called 'mukharraj'. The condition for takhrij is that there is no perceived difference between the two cases; if a difference is found, takhrij is not allowed. The example given is the hadith about freeing a share in a slave, which is used as a basis for analogy. The passage then addresses a dispute: when a restricted mujtahid (who does not perform independent ijtihad but derives rulings from his Imam's principles) gives a fatwa, is the follower a muqallid of the Imam or of that mujtahid? Al-Juwayni and Ibn al-Salah say the follower is a muqallid of the Imam, because the ruling is derived from his principles. Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi disagrees, saying the fatwa cannot be attributed to the Imam. This dispute reflects differences on how far taqlid extends in the case of non-textual rulings derived from the Imam's methodology. The footnote provides a brief biography of al-Shirazi.

Key Terms
تخريج (takhrij): Deriving a ruling for a new case from the principles or existing texts of the Imam, using analogy or textual similarity.
أصحاب الوجوه (ashab al-wujuh): Jurists who perform takhrij and produce multiple 'wujuh' (opinions) within a madhhab, ranking below absolute mujtahids.
مُخرَّج (mukharraj): A ruling derived through takhrij by choosing one of the Imam's texts as the basis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for the second type of takhrij (when the Imam has two different texts) according to the passage?
A) The mujtahid must find a unifying cause (illa).
B) The mujtahid must not perceive any difference between the two cases.
C) The mujtahid must have permission from the Imam.
D) The mujtahid must be an absolute mujtahid.

Key Takeaway
Takhrij is a legitimate method within the madhhab, but it is only valid when no material difference is perceived between the original case and the new case.

Dispute on Attribution of Fatwa from Takhrij
Presents a dispute on attribution of fatwa from takhrij between al-Juwayni/Ibn al-Salah and al-Shirazi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the argument on the attribution of fatwa from takhrij and evaluate the positions of al-Juwayni/Ibn al-Salah vs. al-Shirazi.

Core Idea
Fatwa based on takhrij is attributed to the Imam, not the derivative mujtahid, per al-Juwayni and Ibn al-Salah.

When a restricted mujtahid issues a fatwa on a case not explicitly covered by his Imam's texts, but derives it through takhrij, a natural question arises: to whom is this fatwa attributed? This seemingly technical question has significant implications for how later scholars reference and weigh such rulings. The passage presents two competing views among Shafi'i scholars, but the issue is equally relevant to the Hanafi school and its hierarchy of authority.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
A restricted mujtahid (one who follows a particular Imam but can derive rulings from his principles) gives a fatwa in a case not explicitly stated by the Imam, using takhrij from the Imam's texts.
This is a common situation in all madhhabs, especially when new issues arise.
2
Outline the view of al-Juwayni and Ibn al-Salah
They hold that the follower (the one acting on the fatwa) is a muqallid of the Imam, not of the derivative mujtahid. The ruling is attributed to the Imam because it is derived from his principles.
This view emphasizes the continuity of the madhhab and the reliance on the Imam's foundational rules.
3
Outline the opposing view of Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi
Al-Shirazi argues that the fatwa cannot be attributed to the Imam; it should be attributed to the derivative mujtahid because the specific derivation is his own intellectual effort.
This view highlights the active role of the derivative mujtahid in formulating the ruling.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference affects how such rulings are recorded and referenced in legal literature. Under the first view, they are cited as part of the madhhab (e.g., 'this is the Hanafi ruling'); under the second, they are cited as individual opinions of later scholars.
This affects the authority and weight of such rulings in later tarjih.
5
Determine which view is relied upon (tarjih)
According to the text, the view of al-Juwayni and Ibn al-Salah is chosen (they 'chose' that view). The passage does not give a separate tarjih, but in Hanafi tradition, the same view is generally preferred.
This is consistent with the hierarchical nature of the madhhab where the Imam's authority is central.

Source Text

Key Terms
مُقلّد (muqallid): One who follows a mujtahid's ruling without knowing the evidence.
أصول (usul): Principles; in this context, the foundational legal methodology of the Imam.

The Fourth Class of Jurists – Guardians of the Madhhab
Definition and role of the fourth class of jurists

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the characteristics and limitations of the fourth class of Hanafi jurists and evaluate the authority of their fatwas within the madhhab.

Core Idea
The fourth class preserves and applies the madhhab but cannot perform independent takhrij or ijtihad.

This lesson explores the fourth tier of jurists in the Hanafi iftaa hierarchy. These scholars are deeply knowledgeable of the madhhab and its evidences, yet they fall short of the higher ranks who can derive new rulings. Understanding their role and limitations is crucial for evaluating the weight of fatwas in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Class
The fourth class jurist is a 'faqih al-nafs' who preserves the madhhab but does not reach the level of ashab al-wujuh wa al-turuq. Note the four possible reasons for deficiency: lack of memorization, weak takhrij, shallow usul, or missing auxiliary sciences.
Memorize the four deficiencies as diagnostic criteria.
2
Understand Their Role
They engage in taswir, tajrid, tamhid, taqrir, muwazana, and tarjih. They can clarify and support the madhhab, and their fatwas are comprehensive, though weaker than those of the higher class.
These tasks are explained in the commentary.
3
Scope of Analogy
They use analogy beyond qiyas jali and qiyas 'la fariq'. Examples: freeing a partner in a slave and seller's recourse. This shows they have some ijtihadi capacity.
The passage stresses they are not restricted to only the clearest analogies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطبقة الرابعة: أن لا يبلغ رتبة أئمة المذاهب أصحاب الوجوه والطرق، أنّه فقيه النّفس، حافظ لمذهب إمامه، عارف بأدلته، قائم بتقريرها غیر وبنصرته، يصوّر ويجرد ويمهد ويقرر ويوازن ويرجح ، لكنه قصر عن درجة أولئك، إما لكونه لم يبلغ في حفظ المذهب مبلغهم، وإما لكونه لم يرتض في التخريج والاستنباط كارتياضهم، وإما لكونه غير متبحر في علم أصول الفقه، على أنّه لا يخلو مثله فى ضمن ما يحفظ من الفقه ويعرفه من أدلته، عن أطراف من قواعد أصول الفقه، وإما لكونه مقصرا في غير ذلك من العلوم التي هي أدوات الاجتهاد الحاصل لأصحاب الوجوه والطرق. وهذه صفةٌ كثير من المتأخرين إلى أواخر المائة الرابعة من الهجرة المصنفين الذين رتبوا المذهب وحرروه وصنفوا فيه تصانيف بها معظم اشتغال الناس اليوم، ولم يلحقوا بأرباب الحالة الثانية في تخريج الوجوه، وتمهيد الطرق في المذهب. وأما في فتاواهم فقد كانوا يتبسطون فيها كتبسط أولئك، أو قريباً منه، ويقيسون غير المنقول والمسطور على المنقول والمسطور في المذهب، غير مقتصرين في ذلك على القياس الجلي وقياس "لا فارق" الذي هو نحو قياس الأمة على العبد في إعتاق الشريك، وقياس المرأة على الرجل في رجوع البائع إلى غير ماله عند تعذر الثّمن. وفيهم من جمعت فتاواه وأفردت بالتدوين، ولا يبلغ فى التحاقها بالمذهب مبلغ فتاوى أصحاب الوجوه، ولا يقوى كقوتها والله أعلم.
The fourth class: That he does not reach the rank of the Imams of the schools, the people of wujuh and turuq, but he is a faqih in himself, a guardian of his Imam's madhhab, knowledgeable of its evidences, engaged in their clarification and support, he depicts, abstracts, prepares, establishes, balances, and weighs (preponderates), but he is deficient compared to those preceding him, either because he did not reach their level in preserving the madhhab, or because he did not attain proficiency in takhrij and istinbat as they did, or because he is not deeply versed in the science of usul al-fiqh, though such a person does not lack within what he preserves of fiqh and knows of its evidences, some aspects of usul al-fiqh principles, or because he is deficient in other sciences that are the tools of ijtihad attained by the people of wujuh and turuq. This is the description of many of the later scholars up to the end of the fourth century of Hijrah, the authors who arranged and compiled the madhhab and authored works in it that occupy most people today, and they did not join the people of the second state in takhrij of wujuh and paving of turuq in the madhhab. As for their fatwas, they would expand in them like those predecessors, or close to it, and they analogize what is not transmitted and written to what is transmitted and written in the madhhab, not restricting themselves in that to clear analogy (qiyas jali) and the analogy of 'la fariq' which is like the analogy of a female slave to a male slave in freeing a partner, and the analogy of a woman to a man in the seller's recourse to other than his property when payment is impossible. Among them are those whose fatwas were collected and separately recorded, but they do not reach in their attachment to the madhhab the level of the fatwas of the people of wujuh, nor are they as strong. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth class of jurists according to the classification in the usul al-iftaa tradition. These jurists are knowledgeable in fiqh, memorize the madhhab of their Imam, understand its evidences, and can perform tasks like taswir (conceptualization), tajrid (abstraction), tamhid (preparation), taqrir (establishment), muwazana (balancing), and tarjih (preponderance). However, they fall short of the higher classes (the mujtahidun fi al-madhhab, i.e., ashab al-wujuh wa al-turuq) for various reasons: insufficient memorization of the madhhab, lack of skill in takhrij and istinbat, insufficient mastery of usul al-fiqh (though they know some principles), or deficiency in auxiliary sciences needed for ijtihad. The author notes that many later scholars up to the end of the fourth century Hijri belong to this class, as they compiled and organized the madhhab but did not reach the level of the second class (the ashab al-wujuh) in generating new legal aspects and paving methodological paths. However, their fatwas are comprehensive and they use analogy beyond the two types of qiyas jali and 'la fariq' (where no difference exists), giving examples from the hadith of freeing a partner in a slave and the seller's recourse. Their collected fatwas are valid but not as authoritative as those of the ashab al-wujuh.

Key Terms
فقيه النّفس (faqih al-nafs): A jurist who has an intuitive understanding and aptitude for fiqh, even if not a fully independent mujtahid.
أصحاب الوجوه والطرق (ashab al-wujuh wa al-turuq): The second class of mujtahids who can derive new rulings (wujuh) within the madhhab and establish methodological paths (turuq).
قياس "لا فارق" (qiyas 'la fariq'): Analogy where no effective difference exists between the original case and the new case, thus the ruling is directly applied.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes the fourth class from the second class (ashab al-wujuh wa al-turuq)?
A) The fourth class does not possess any knowledge of usul al-fiqh.
B) The fourth class cannot engage in tarjih or muwazana.
C) The fourth class cannot perform takhrij and pave turuq in the madhhab.
D) The fourth class cannot give fatwas on new cases.

Key Takeaway
The fourth class of jurists are knowledgeable guardians of the madhhab who can issue fatwas and use analogy, but their rulings carry less authority than those of the higher classes who perform takhrij and turuq.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Fifth-Level Mufti and Classification of Hanafi Issues
Describes fifth-level mufti and introduces three-tier issue classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the qualifications of a fifth-level mufti and apply the three-tier classification of Hanafi issues to resolve conflicts in fatwa.

Core Idea
A fifth-level mufti may only analogize clear parallels; Hanafi issues are graded to resolve conflicts.

This passage from Uthmani's work on the principles of fatwa introduces the fifth category of muftis and the three-level classification of Hanafi legal issues. Understanding these distinctions is critical for a mufti to know his own limits and to choose the correct ruling when conflicts arise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fifth-level mufti's function and limitation
The fifth-level mufti memorizes the school and transmits rulings from the imam and earlier mujtahids, but he is weak in presenting proofs and refining analogies. His fatwa is relied upon only for issues explicitly found in transmitted texts.
This level is above a mere narrator but below a mujtahid within the school.
2
Determine when analogical extension (ilhaq) is permissible
He may analogize a new case to a transmitted ruling only if the parallel is so clear that it requires no extra thought (e.g., female slave compared to male slave in freeing a partner). Similarly, if the case falls under an established principle (ضابط) of the school, he may issue a fatwa.
If neither condition applies, he must refrain from giving a fatwa.
3
Recognize the requirement of 'faqih al-nafs'
Even this limited mufti must be a 'faqih al-nafs' – a jurist by nature – who can accurately conceptualize issues in all their aspects. The author emphasizes that this quality is necessary for properly depicting and conveying rulings.
'Faqih al-nafs' is distinct from mere memorization; it implies intuitive juristic understanding.
4
Explain the purpose of classifying Hanafi issues into grades
Hanafis classify issues into three levels so that when there is a conflict (ta'arud), the mufti can choose the ruling from the higher grade over the lower. This ensures that outweighed rulings are not preferred.
The three levels are not enumerated in this excerpt but are referenced from Ibn 'Abidin's works.
5
Apply the classification principle to a hypothetical conflict
Imagine a mufti finds two Hanafi rulings on a new matter: one from the explicit texts of the imam (higher grade) and another from a less authoritative opinion (lower grade). According to the classification, he must select the higher-grade ruling.
This step consolidates the idea that classification aids in preference during conflict.

الطبقة الخامسة: أن يقوم بحفظ المذهب ونقله وفهمه في واضحات المسائل ومشكلاتها، غير أن عنده ضعفاً في تقرير أدلته وتحرير أقيسته. فهذا يُعتمد نقله وفتواه به فيما يحكيه من مسطورات مذهبه من منصوصات إمامه، وتفريعات أصحابه المجتهدين فى مذهبه وتخريجاتهم. وأما ما لا يجده منقولاً فى مذهبه، فإن وجد فى المنقول ما هذا في معناه بحيث يُدرك من غير فضل فكر وتأمّل أنّه لا فارق بينهما ، كما في الأمة بالنسبة إلى العبد المنصوص عليه في إعتاق الشريك، جاز له إلحاقه به، والفتوى به. وكذلك ما يعلم اندراجه تحت ضابط منقول ممهد فى المذهب، وما لم يكن كذلك فعليه الإمساك عن الفتيا منه. ومثل هذا يقع نادراً في مثل الفقيه المذكور إذ يَبْعُد كما ذكر الإمام أبو المعالي الجويني _ ، تقع واقعةٌ لم يُنص على حكمها في المذهب، ولا هي فى معنى شيئ فى المنصوص عليه فيه من غير فرق، ولا هي مندرجة تحت شيئ من ضوابط المذهب المحرّرة فيه. ثمّ إنّ هذا الفقية لا يكون إلا "فقيها النفس " لأنّ تصوير المسائل على وجهها، ثم نقل أحكامها بعد استتمام تصويرها جليّاتها وخفيّاتِها، لا يقوم به إلا فقيه النفس ذو حظ من الفقه . قلت: وينبغي أن يكتفي في حفظ المذهب في هذه الحالة، وفى الحالة التي قبلها بأن يكون المُعْظم على ذهنه لدربته، متمكناً من الوقوف على الباقي بالمطالعة أو ما يلتحق بها على القُرب.
ثم قال ابن الصلاح رحمه الله تعالى: "وهذه أصناف المفتين وشروطهم، وهي خمسة. وما من صِنْفِ منها إلا ويُشترط فيه حفظ المذهب وفقه النفس. وذلك فيما عدا الصنف الأخير الذي هو أخسها... فمن انتصب في منصب الفتيا وتصدى لها، وليس على صفة واحدٍ من هذه الأصناف الخمسة، فقد باء بأمرٍ عظيم. أَلَا يَظُنُّ أُولَئِكَ أَنَّهُمْ مَبْعُوثُونَ لِيَوْمٍ عَظِيمٍ؟ ومَن أراد التصدي للفتيا طاناً كونه من أهلها فليئهم نفسه، وليتق الله ربّه تبارك وتعالى، ولا يُخدعن عن الأخذ بالوثيقة لنفسه والنظر لها. ولقد قطع الإمام أبو المعالى وغيره بأنّ الاصولي الماهر المتصرف فى الفقه لا يحل له الفتوى بمجرد ذلك، ولو وقعت له في نفسه واقعة لزمه أن يستفتي غيره فيها، ويلتحق به المتصرف النظّار البحاث فى الفقه من أئمّة الخلاف وفحول المناظرين. وهذا لأنه ليس أهلاً لإدراك حكم الواقعة استقلالاً لقصور آلته، ولا من مذهب إمام متقدم لعدم حفظه له، وعدم اطلاعه عليه على الوجه المعتبر، والله أعلم. وهذه الطبقات التي ذكرها ابن كمال باشا من الحنفية والحافظ ابن الصلاح رحمهما الله تعالى من الشافعية تُوجد فى المالكية والحنابلة أيضاً، وإن لم أجد منهم التصريح بهذه الأسماء. (۳)

الحنفية على ثلاث طبقات:
Principles of Issuing Fatwa. Levels of Jurists. The fifth level: that he memorizes the school, transmits it, and understands clear and problematic issues, but he has weakness in presenting proofs and refining analogies. So his transmission and fatwa are relied upon regarding what he reports from the recorded positions of his school, from the explicit texts of his imam, and the derivations of his companions who are mujtahids in his school and their deductions. As for what he does not find transmitted in his school, if he finds in the transmitted something that is in its meaning such that it is perceived without extra thought and reflection that there is no difference between them, like the case of a female slave in relation to a male slave regarding the explicit ruling on freeing a partner, it is permissible for him to analogize it to it and issue a fatwa accordingly. Likewise, what he knows is included under a transmitted principle established in the school. And what is not like that, then he must refrain from giving a fatwa on it. Such a situation rarely occurs for the mentioned jurist, since it is unlikely, as Imam Abu al-Ma'ali al-Juwayni mentioned, that an event occurs whose ruling is not stated in the school, nor is it in the meaning of something in the stated text without difference, nor is it included under any of the school's established principles. Then, this jurist is only a 'jurist of soul' (faqih al-nafs) because depicting issues accurately, then conveying their rulings after complete depiction of their clear and subtle aspects, is only done by a jurist of soul who has a share of fiqh. I say: It is sufficient in memorizing the school in this case and the preceding case that most of it be on his mind due to practice, and he be able to find the rest by reviewing or the like soon after. Then Ibn al-Salah, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'These are the categories of muftis and their conditions, and they are five. There is none of these categories except that memorization of the school and fiqh of the soul are required, except the last category which is the lowest... Whoever assumes the position of fatwa and undertakes it while not being qualified according to one of these five categories, then he has committed a grave matter. Do those not think that they will be resurrected for a great day? And whoever wants to undertake fatwa thinking he is qualified, let him blame himself, fear Allah, his Lord, Blessed and Exalted, and not be deceived into neglecting taking precautions for himself and looking out for it. Imam Abu al-Ma'ali and others have definitively stated that a proficient usuli who is skilled in fiqh is not permitted to issue fatwa merely by virtue of that. If an event occurs in his mind, he must ask another for a fatwa regarding it. Similarly, the skilled examiner and researcher in fiqh from the imams of dispute and the prominent debaters is also included. This is because he is not qualified to independently derive the ruling of an event due to the deficiency of his tools, nor does he belong to the school of a preceding imam due to his lack of memorization and lack of proper knowledge of it. And Allah knows best. These levels mentioned by Ibn Kamal Pasha of the Hanafis and al-Hafiz Ibn al-Salah, may Allah have mercy on them, of the Shafi'is are also found among the Malikis and Hanbalis, although I have not found them explicitly stating these names. (3) Levels of Hanafi Issues. (1) Know that the Hanafis, just as they divided jurists into levels, also divided issues into grades, so that the mufti, when there is conflict, chooses the one of the higher grade and does not give preference to one that is outweighed. Allamah Ibn ‘Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned in Sharh al-Mufti and in the commentary of the introduction of al-Durr al-Mukhtar that the issues of our companions the Hanafis are of three levels:
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition on the fifth level of muftis according to the Hanafi classification of jurists, followed by an introduction to the classification of Hanafi issues. The author, Muhammad Taqi al-Uthmani, is quoting and commenting on earlier sources, including Ibn al-Salah and Ibn Kamal Pasha. The fifth-level mufti is one who has memorized the school and can narrate rulings from the transmitted texts, but he is weak in articulating proofs and constructing analogies. His fatwa is accepted only for issues explicitly found in the transmitted sources of the school. For new issues, he may analogize only if there is a clear parallel in the transmitted rulings (e.g., the case of a female slave compared to a male slave in freeing a partner) or if the issue falls under an established principle (ضابط) of the school. If neither applies, he must refrain from giving a fatwa. Such a situation is rare, as Imam al-Juwayni noted. The passage emphasizes that even such a mufti must be a 'faqih al-nafs' – a jurist by nature – who can accurately conceptualize issues in all their aspects. The author adds that memorization of most of the school suffices if he can find the rest through quick review. Ibn al-Salah's quote underscores that all five categories of muftis require both memorization of the school and 'fiqh al-nafs', except the lowest. A person who issues fatwas without meeting these categories commits a grave sin. The passage further states that even a skilled usuli (methodologist) or a proficient researcher in fiqh is not allowed to give fatwa independently; he must refer to a qualified mufti. Finally, the passage introduces the three-level classification of Hanafi issues itself (though the detailed levels are not listed in this excerpt), explaining that this classification helps the mufti choose the higher-grade ruling when conflicts arise. This system is common across madhhabs, though the terminology may differ.

Key Terms
طبقات الفقهاء (tabaqat al-fuqaha'): Hierarchical categories of jurists based on their level of knowledge and ijtihad capacity within the Hanafi school.
فقيه النفس (faqih al-nafs): A jurist with an intuitive, natural understanding of fiqh who can accurately conceive issues and derive rulings without relying solely on transmitted texts.
طبقات المسائل (tabaqat al-masa'il): The three-level classification of Hanafi legal issues (e.g., categorical, probable, etc.) to resolve conflicts between rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Whenever he feels confident in his analogy.
B) Only when the new case is exactly parallel to a transmitted ruling without needing extensive reasoning, or falls under an established principle.

D) Only after consulting a higher-level mufti.

Key Takeaway
A fifth-level mufti may only issue fatwas on new issues if they clearly parallel an existing ruling or fall under an established principle; otherwise, he must refrain, and Hanafi issues are graded to resolve conflicts.

The First Level of Hanafi Masail: Zahir al-Riwayah
Defining the first level of Hanafi rulings for fatwa prioritization

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the first level of Hanafi masail (Zahir al-Riwayah), list the books that contain it, and apply the rule that the mufti must prioritize this level over lower grades.

Core Idea
The mufti must always prefer Zahir al-Riwayah rulings over lower transmissions.

In the Hanafi school, legal issues are classified into grades, just as jurists are. This classification is essential for a mufti when narrations conflict: he must choose the ruling from the highest grade. This lesson introduces the first and most authoritative grade, known as 'masa'il al-usul' or 'Zahir al-Riwayah', and explains its sources and authority.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Need for Grading
Recognize that Hanafi masail are not all equal; they are divided into grades so that a mufti can resolve conflicts by preferring higher-grade narrations.
This is a foundational principle of ifta methodology.
2
Identify the First Grade and Its Authorities
The first grade is called 'masa'il al-usul' or 'Zahir al-Riwayah'. It consists of rulings transmitted from the three main imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani (and sometimes Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad).
These three are called 'al-thalatha' and are the primary authorities.
3
Recognize the Books of Zahir al-Riwayah
The rulings of this grade are compiled in the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir.
The passage lists five; the sixth is al-Siyar al-Kabir.
4
Apply the Rule of Priority
When two narrations conflict, the mufti must choose the one from the higher grade. Zahir al-Riwayah is the highest, so it takes precedence over lower grades like the Nawadir.
Exceptions may occur when later scholars prefer a lower-grade ruling due to changing custom.
