Know that the Hanafis, just as they divided the jurists into categories, they also divided the legal issues into grades, so that the mufti may choose, when there is conflict, that which is of the higher grade and not give precedence to that which is lower. The scholar Ibn Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned in 'Sharh al-Mufti' and in the commentary on the introduction of 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar' that the legal issues of our Hanafi companions are of three levels: The first level: the issues of the fundamentals (usul). They are also called Zahir al-Riwayah (the well-known transmitted rulings). They are issues transmitted from the founders of the school, namely Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, who are called the three scholars. They are joined by Zufar, al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, and others, may Allah have mercy on them all, who took fiqh from Imam Abu Hanifa, but the common prevalent in Zahir al-Riwayah is the statement of the three, or some of them. Then these issues, which are called 'Zahir al-Riwayah' and 'al-Usul', are what are found in the books of Imam Muhammad, which are: al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Jami' al-Kabir, from
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) on the hierarchy of Hanafi legal sources. The author, Mufti Taqi Usmani, explains that just as Hanafi jurists are classified into ranks, the legal issues (masail) themselves are divided into grades to guide the mufti when different narrations conflict. He quotes Ibn Abidin, who states that Hanafi masail consist of three levels. This lesson focuses on the first and highest level: مسائل الأصول (fundamental issues), also called ظاهر الرواية (the well-known transmission). These are the rulings narrated directly from the three main founders: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Sometimes the opinions of Zufar or Hasan ibn Ziyad are included, but the term 'Zahir al-Riwayah' predominantly refers to the statements of the three. The textual source for this level is specifically the six books of Imam Muhammad (only five are listed here; the sixth is al-Siyar al-Kabir). Muftis must prioritize these rulings over lower levels when issuing fatwas.

Key Terms
مسائل الأصول (masa'il al-usul): The highest grade of Hanafi legal issues, comprising rulings transmitted directly from the founding imams and recorded in the six books of Imam Muhammad (Zahir al-Riwayah).
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known and widely transmitted rulings from Abu Hanifa and his students, as compiled in the six books of Imam Muhammad.
الثلاثة (al-thalatha): The three main Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The first and most authoritative level of Hanafi masail is Zahir al-Riwayah, found in the six books of Imam Muhammad, and the mufti must prioritize it over lower grades.

Classification of Transmitted Hanafi Rulings: Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah and Nawādir
Defining the two categories of transmitted Hanafi rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish between Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah and Nawādir, and apply the hierarchy of transmitted rulings in the Hanafi school for issuing fatwa.

Core Idea
Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah forms the authoritative bedrock of Hanafi fatwa; Nawādir are secondary.

As a mufti, you must know the source of every ruling you rely on. Not all transmissions from the early imams carry the same weight. This lesson draws from Muḥammad Taqī ʿUthmānī’s Uṣūl al-Iftāʾ to define the two primary categories of transmitted Hanafi rulings: Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah (evident transmissions) and Masāʾil al-Nawādir (rare transmissions). Understanding this hierarchy protects you from basing a fatwa on weak or rare reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories
The author divides transmitted rulings into two: 'masā'il al-uṣūl' (also 'Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah') and 'masā'il al-nawādir'. Locate these terms in the Arabic text.
2
Define Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah
Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah are rulings found in Imam Muḥammad's six famous books: al-Mabsūṭ, al-Ziyādāt, al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr, al-Siyar al-Ṣaghīr, al-Jāmiʿ al-Kabīr, al-Siyar al-Kabīr. They are transmitted by reliable narrators, reaching the level of tawātur or istifāḍa.
3
Define Nawādir
Nawādir are rulings transmitted from the same imams but not in the six books. They appear in Muḥammad's other works (e.g., al-Kaysāniyyāt, al-Hārūniyyāt), or in books of other early scholars like al-Ḥasan ibn Ziyād (al-Mujarrad) and Abū Yūsuf (al-Āmālī), or through isolated narrations from individuals like Ibn Samāʿa and al-Muʿallā ibn Manṣūr.
4
Assess authority: Ẓāhir vs Nawādir
Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah is the strongest category; it forms the basis of fatwā. Nawādir are weaker and are only used when no ruling from Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah is available, or as supporting evidence.
5
Apply the hierarchy in fatwā practice
When a mufti encounters a question, he first searches the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah sources. Only if no clear ruling is found there does he turn to Nawādir, and then to other categories (fatāwā, qiyās, etc.).

۲۱۱ هـ. (الفوائد البهية ص ٢١٥، بتصرف يسير)
The first category: issues of al-usul (principles). They are also called zahir al-riwayah (evident transmission). They are issues transmitted from the founders of the madhhab, namely Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, who are called the three scholars (may Allah have mercy on them). Joining them are Zufar, al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, and others (may Allah have mercy on them all) who took fiqh from Imam Abu Hanifa. However, the common and widespread in zahir al-riwayah is the statement of the three, or the statement of some of them. Then these issues called 'zahir al-riwayah' and 'al-usul' are what is found in the books of Imam Muhammad which are: al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. They are called zahir al-riwayah because they were transmitted from Muhammad by reliable narrators, so they are established from him either by tawatur (mass transmission) or istifadah (widespread transmission). The second category: issues of al-nawadir (rare transmissions). They are issues transmitted from the aforementioned founders, but not in the mentioned books. Rather, they are either in other books of Muhammad, such as al-Kaysaniyat, al-Haruniyat, al-Jurjaniyat, and al-Raqqiyat; they are called non-zahir al-riwayah because they were not transmitted from Muhammad by evident, established, correct transmissions like the first books. Or they are in books other than those of Imam Muhammad, such as the book al-Mujarrad of al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and others, including the books of al-Amali of Abu Yusuf. Or they are by isolated narrations, such as the narration of Ibn Sama'a, al-Mu'alla ibn Mansur, and others in specific issues.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a methodological classification of the types of transmitted rulings in the Hanafi school. The author, Muhammad Taqi Usmani, divides them into two categories. The first is 'masa'il al-usul' (principled issues) also known as 'zahir al-riwayah' (evident transmission). These are the rulings transmitted from the founding imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—through reliable chains of narration. They are found in the six famous books of Imam Muhammad: al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. These transmissions are so well-established that they are considered either mutawatir (mass-transmitted) or mustafid (widespread), giving them strong evidentiary weight. The second category is 'masa'il al-nawadir' (rare issues). These are also transmitted from the same imams, but through less widespread or less reliable channels. They may be found in other books of Imam Muhammad (e.g., al-Kaysaniyat), in books of other early Hanafi scholars like al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, or in isolated narrations from individuals like Ibn Sama'a and al-Mu'alla ibn Mansur. The passage also includes biographical footnotes on al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and Muhammad ibn Sama'a, highlighting their stature and contributions. For a mufti, understanding this hierarchy is crucial: rulings from zahir al-riwayah take precedence over nawadir, and fatwa is generally given based on the former. This classification ensures that the mufti knows the authority level of each ruling he consults.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): Rulings transmitted from the Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) through reliable, well-known chains; found in the six core books of Imam Muhammad.
مسائل النوادر (Masā’il al-Nawādir): Rulings transmitted from the Hanafi imams but not through the most reliable or widespread channels; found in less central books or isolated narrations.
مسائل الأصول (Masā’il al-Uṣūl): Synonym for zahir al-riwayah; the foundational transmitted rulings of the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes 'masa'il al-nawadir'?
A) Rulings found in the six famous books of Imam Muhammad.
B) Rulings transmitted through isolated narrations or less famous books.
C) Rulings that are agreed upon by all three imams without exception.
D) Rulings that are considered mutawatir.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies its transmitted rulings into Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah (authoritative) and Nawādir (secondary), and a mufti must prioritize the former.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Relationship of the Two Imams and the Authority of Zahir al-Riwayah
Critique of fabricated stories and explanation of the Hanafi textual hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rejects stories of enmity between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani and identify the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah and their authority for fatwa.

Core Idea
The integrity of the early Hanafi imams is beyond reproach; their differences were scholarly, not personal.

This passage from 'Usul al-Ifta' addresses a critical issue for any mufti: the reliability of the foundational sources. It tackles baseless stories of enmity between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, and then clarifies the classification of Muhammad's works into 'small' (agreed upon by both) and 'large' (Muhammad alone), establishing the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah as the primary texts. Understanding this hierarchy prevents misapplication of weaker opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and the refutation
The passage begins by rejecting fabricated anecdotes of enmity. Identify who fabricated them (enemies) and why (to undermine the school's credibility).
The author uses strong language: 'باطل مختلق' (false fabrication).
2
Examine the evidence for possible tension
Al-Sarakhsi noted that Muhammad omitted Abu Yusuf in some books. Why would this suggest tension? The author then provides a technical explanation from Ibn Nujaym.
The omission is only in 'large' works, not 'small'.
3
Parse Ibn Nujaym's classification
Understand the distinction between 'small' works (agreed upon by both imams) and 'large' works (not presented to Abu Yusuf). This explains the omission without enmity.
The 'small' works are those where Abu Yusuf's name is mentioned; the 'large' are not.
4
Define Zahir al-Riwayah
The six books are named: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat. They form the foundation of the madhhab. Note the role of al-Hakim al-Shahid in compiling them.
These are the most authentic transmissions from Muhammad.
5
Apply the rule for fatwa
Recognize that these six books carry the highest authority (zahir al-riwayah) and are the primary source; other transmissions (nawadir) are secondary.
A mufti must start with these books before consulting later works.

Layers of jurists: Our teacher, the scholar al-Uthmani al-Tahanawi (1), may Allah have mercy on him, rejected these anecdotes and attributed them to enemies that they 'extracted from their differences arising from correct ijtihad fabricated falsehoods against them to lower their status by transmitting criticism of one another, and likewise what was narrated about reasons for deep-seated aversion between them as in the introduction of al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi is false and fabricated against them, for their station was higher and more exalted than that these falsehoods be attributed to them. We seek refuge in Allah from the evil of those who fabricated them.' But it appears from what al-Sarakhsi, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned that Imam Muhammad did not mention Imam [Abu Yusuf] in this book. (1) He is Zafar Ahmad ibn Latif al-Uthmani al-Tahanawi, the hadith scholar, jurist, researcher, litterateur, pious, ascetic, Sufi, insightful, author of I'la al-Sunan. He was born in 1310 AH near Dar al-Ulum in Deoband. His mother died when he was three, so his grandmother raised him. When he completed seven and finished Quran, he began studying at Dar al-Ulum Deoband, then moved to Thanah Bhan at his uncle Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi. He studied under his uncle, then at Jami al-Ulum in Kanpur, reading the six major hadith collections and Mishkat al-Masabih with senior disciples of al-Tahanawi. Then to Saharanpur where he attended lessons of Khalil Ahmad al-Saharnpuri, who granted him ijazah in hadith and all transmitted and intellectual sciences in 1328 AH when he was only 18. He then taught at Jami al-Ulum for about seven years, then returned to Imdad al-Ulum in Thanah Bhan where he taught the books of Sunnah. Then Hakim al-Ummah entrusted him with authoring I'la al-Sunan along with ifta and teaching, and he excelled. He spent about a year composing it. Then he taught at various centers in India, Burma, and Pakistan. Despite illness, he adhered to dhikr and nawafil, attending all prayers in mosques with difficulty until he died in Dhu al-Qa'dah 1394 AH. He left valuable scholarly legacy including I'la al-Sunan in 20 volumes, Imdad al-Ahkam (his fatwa collection), and Ahkam al-Quran. (2) I'la al-Sunan, Book of Waqf, chapter on mosque or waqf ruin, vol. 13 p. 213. Page 134: ...that Abu Yusuf in this book, and that indicates there was something between them, even if not what is mentioned in these anecdotes which cannot be imagined from a religious Muslim, let alone the likes of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. It is possible that there is another reason for his not mentioning him, which is what Ibn Nujaym mentioned: 'Every work of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan described as 'small' is agreed upon by the two shaykhs, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, unlike the 'large' which was not presented to Abu Yusuf.' In short, the book al-Siyar al-Kabir is among the earliest written on international law and the rules of war and peace with such elaboration and detail at a time when there was no recognized codified international law. (2) Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, discussion of tashahhud 1:579. (3) His name is Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad, known as al-Hakim al-Shahid al-Marwazi al-Balkhi, a teacher of al-Hakim (author of al-Mustadrak). It is said he memorized 60,000 hadiths. When appointed qadi of Bukhara, he would go to al-Hamid and teach him fiqh. When he became vizier, all affairs were entrusted to him, but he refused the title of vizier. He used to supplicate after prayer: 'O Allah, grant me martyrdom' until the evening of the night he was killed.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage from 'Usul al-Ifta' by Muhammad Taqi Usmani is a discussion of the layers of Hanafi jurists (tabaqat al-fuqaha) and the authority of their works. The author begins by refuting baseless anecdotes that suggest enmity between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. He attributes these fabrications to enemies who exploited legitimate scholarly differences. He then notes that al-Sarakhsi's remark—that Muhammad omitted Abu Yusuf in a certain book—might indicate some tension, but offers a more plausible explanation from Ibn Nujaym: Muhammad's 'small' works were reviewed by both, while the 'large' works (like al-Siyar al-Kabir) were not presented to Abu Yusuf, so omission does not imply enmity. The passage then identifies the six foundational books (the Zahir al-Riwaya) and mentions the role of al-Hakim al-Shahid in compiling them. The author also provides a lengthy biographical footnote on Zafar Ahmad al-Uthmani, a prominent modern Hanafi scholar, and a note on Ibn Nujaym. The focus is on establishing the reliability of the early texts and the integrity of the founding imams, which is critical for a mufti to understand the hierarchy of sources in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six books authored by Muhammad al-Shaybani that are transmitted with the highest reliability and form the foundation of the Hanafi madhhab.
الحاكم الشهيد (al-Hakim al-Shahid): Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Marwazi al-Balkhi, a Hanafi scholar and qadi who compiled the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah into a single work.
طبقات الفقهاء (Tabaqat al-Fuqaha): The hierarchical classification of Hanafi jurists by generation and authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the works were written after Abu Yusuf's death

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's foundational texts (Zahir al-Riwayah) are transmitted with impeccable reliability, and the personal integrity of the founding imams is beyond question.

The Six Books of Zahir al-Riwayah and Their Authority
Explaining the classification of the six primary Hanafi texts and their compilation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Saghir and Kabir works of Imam Muhammad and explain the hierarchical authority of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
The six books of Zahir al-Riwayah are the primary texts; among them, the 'Saghir' works carry the agreement of both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad and thus have higher authority.

This passage from Ibn Nujaym and later Hanafi sources clarifies the classification of the six core texts of the madhhab. Understanding the distinction between 'Saghir' and 'Kabir' works is essential for the mufti in determining the weight of transmitted rulings. The chain from Imam Muhammad's original compilations to Al-Hakim al-Shahid's summary and Al-Sarakhsi's monumental commentary forms the backbone of Hanafi legal literature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah
The passage lists the six books: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat. Recognize that they form the core transmitted texts of the Hanafi school.
These are also known as the 'apparent transmission' (zahir al-riwayah) because they were transmitted widely and reliably.
2
Understand the Saghir vs. Kabir distinction
Ibn Nujaym states that works described as 'Saghir' have the agreement of both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, whereas 'Kabir' works were not presented to Abu Yusuf. This affects their legal authority.
The term 'Saghir' does not refer to size but to the fact that they were reviewed and agreed upon by the two shaykhs.
3
Recognize the authority hierarchy
Saghir works take precedence over Kabir works in cases of conflict because they have the consensus of the two shaykhs. However, all six books are part of Zahir al-Riwayah and are the primary sources for fatwa.
This hierarchy is a key principle (rasm al-mufti) when weighing different transmitted rulings.
4
Trace the transmission chain
Imam al-Hakim al-Shahid summarized the six books in al-Kafi. Imam al-Sarakhsi wrote a detailed commentary on al-Kafi called al-Mabsut, which became a major reference. This chain shows how the original texts were preserved and explained.
Al-Sarakhsi's al-Mabsut is considered the most comprehensive Hanafi work and cites the six books extensively.
5
Apply the classification to source evaluation
When citing a ruling, a mufti should determine whether it comes from a Saghir or Kabir work. If the ruling is found in a Saghir work, it carries higher authority. If only in a Kabir work, it is still valid but may be secondary.
This principle helps resolve apparent contradictions within the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أبا يوسف فى هذا الكتاب، وذلك يدل على أنه كان بينهما شيء، وإن لم يكن ماذكر في هذه الحكايات مما لا يتصوّر من مسلم متدين، فضلاً عن أمثال أبي يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله تعالى ويمكن لعدم ذكره سبب آخر وهو ماذكره ابن نجيم رحمه الله تعالى قال: 'كل تأليف لمحمد بن الحسن موصوف ب "الصغير" فهو باتفاق الشيخين أبي يوسف ومحمد بخلاف الكبير، فإنّه لم يُعرض على أبي يوسف.' وبالجملة، فإنّ كتاب "السير الكبير" من أقدم ما أُلف في القانون الدولي وفى أحكام الحرب والسلم بهذا البسط والتفصيل في زمان لم يكن للعلاقات الدولية قانون مدوّن معترف به قبله. فهذه الكتب الستة هي التي سُمّيت "ظاهر الرواية"، ومن أجل كونها أصلاً في معرفة المذهب الحنفى، فإن الإمام الحاكم الشهيد رحمه الله تعالى جمع مسائلها ملخصةً فى كتابه "الكافي" وهو الكتاب الذي شرحه شمس الأئمة السَّرَخْسِي رحمه الله تعالى باسم "المبسوط" في ثلاثين مجلداً، وأصبح هو مأخذاً لمن جاء بعده.
Abu Yusuf in this book, and that indicates that there was something between them, even if what was mentioned in these stories is not imaginable from a religious Muslim, let alone the likes of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them both). It is possible that there is another reason for not mentioning him, which is what Ibn Nujaym (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned, saying: 'Every work of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan described as "al-Saghir" is by the agreement of the two shaykhs Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, unlike the "al-Kabir," for it was not presented to Abu Yusuf.' Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a methodological explanation of the classification of canonical Hanafi texts. It begins by addressing a historical point about the relationship between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, suggesting that the absence of Abu Yusuf's name in certain works does not imply disrespect; rather, there is a technical reason. Ibn Nujaym clarifies that any work by Muhammad described as 'al-Saghir' (small) enjoys the agreement of both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, whereas the 'al-Kabir' (large) works were not reviewed by Abu Yusuf. This distinction is important for determining the authority of rulings. The passage then identifies the six books that constitute 'Zahir al-Riwayah' — the core transmitted texts of the Hanafi school. It notes that al-Siyar al-Kabir is a pioneering work in international law. Finally, it explains that al-Hakim al-Shahid summarized these six books in his work 'al-Kafi,' and al-Sarakhsi wrote an extensive commentary on al-Kafi called 'al-Mabsut,' which became a major reference in the school. This lesson underscores the hierarchical structure of Hanafi sources: the six books are the primary texts, then the commentaries and summaries.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six books of Imam Muhammad that form the primary source of Hanafi fiqh
الصغير (al-Saghir): Refers to the smaller-sized compilations of Imam Muhammad which were reviewed and agreed upon by Abu Yusuf
الكبير (al-Kabir): Refers to the larger compilations of Imam Muhammad which were not presented to Abu Yusuf for review

Key Takeaway
The six books of Zahir al-Riwayah are the foundational texts; among them, the Saghir works hold higher authority due to the agreement of the two shaykhs.

Rank of al-Mabsut and the Three Books of Imam Muhammad in the Hanafi Textual Hierarchy
Rasm al-mufti ruling on textual hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the authoritative rank of al-Mabsut and classify Imam Muhammad's three additional books within the Hanafi textual hierarchy, and apply the rule of reliance in fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Al-Mabsut is the ultimate authority; the three hadith/ikhtilaf books rank above Nawadir but below Zahir al-Riwayah.

In this lesson, we explore a key rasm al-mufti principle that determines which texts a Hanafi mufti relies upon. The passage begins by establishing the unparalleled weight of al-Sarakhsi's Mabsut, then addresses a scholarly debate about three other works of Imam Muhammad. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correct fatwa practice and avoiding reliance on secondary sources when primary ones are available.

Guided Path
1
Identify the highest authority
The passage states that al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi is the ultimate reference: nothing contrary to it is acted upon, and fatwas are given only relying on it. This establishes its supreme rank.
Note that al-Mabsut is a later commentary on the Zahir al-Riwayah texts, but its authority is absolute due to its comprehensiveness and acceptance.
2
Classify the three additional books
Three books of Imam Muhammad are mentioned: al-Muwatta, Kitab al-Athar, and Kitab al-Hujja. Some scholars consider them part of Zahir al-Riwayah due to fame. Identify this as the point of dispute.
These books are famous and correctly attributed, but their purpose differs from the six core books.
3
Analyze the reasoning against inclusion
The author argues that Zahir al-Riwayah books were specifically authored to expound the Hanafi school's rulings, while these three serve different purposes: hadith collections and juristic debate. Thus, they are not part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
The key distinction is the author's intent (niyya) in composition, not just attribution or fame.
4
Determine their rank
Although not Zahir al-Riwayah, they are above Nawadir due to their widespread acceptance and authentic attribution. They are to be accepted except where they contradict the six books.
This places them in a middle tier: higher than rare transmissions, lower than the foundational texts.
5
Apply the rule in fatwa
In practice, a mufti should first consult the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah and al-Mabsut. If no ruling is found there, he may turn to these three books, but must give precedence to the six in case of conflict.
This hierarchy ensures consistency and preserves the core of the madhhab.

Source Text

وهناك ثلاثة كتب أخرى للإمام محمد رحمه الله تعالى ذكر بعض المؤلّفين فيها أنّها يمكن إلحاقها بالقسم الأول، يعنى بكتب ظاهر الرواية، لشهرتها وأهمّيّتها، وهى موطأ الإمام محمد، وكتاب الآثار، وكتاب الحجة على أهل المدينة. (۳) والظاهرُ أنّها وإن كانت بمثابة كتب ظاهر الرواية في صحة نسبتها إلى الإمام محمد، واشتهارها فيما بين أهل العلم، ولكنها ليست موضوعةٌ لبيان المذهب وفروعه، وإنما الأولان موضوعهما رواية الأحاديث والآثار، وما جاء فيهما من المسائل الفقهيّة فإنّها جاءت تبعاً، والكتاب الثالث موضوعه الخلافيّات. أمّا كُتب ظاهر الرواية، فإنّها وضعت لبيان المذهب أصلاً، فصارت هي المعتمدة لمعرفة المذهب الحنفي. ولعلّ من أجل هذا لم يذكر الفقهاء الحنفية هذه الكتب، لا فى ظاهر الرواية، و لا فى النوادر، لأنها ليست من النوادر لشهرتها عن الإمام محمد وليست من ظاهر الرواية لأنها لم توضع لبيان المذهب، ولكن الظاهر أن رتبتها فوق النوادر ويؤخذ بما جاء فيها إلا ما عارض الكتب الستة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
The Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi: nothing contrary to it is acted upon, nor is any reliance placed except upon it, nor is a fatwa given or reliance placed except upon it. (1) And there are three other books of Imam Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, which some authors have mentioned can be joined to the first category, i.e., the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, due to their fame and importance: they are the Muwatta of Imam Muhammad, Kitab al-Athar, and Kitab al-Hujja 'ala Ahl al-Madina. (3) But the apparent view is that although they are like the books of Zahir al-Riwayah in the correctness of their attribution to Imam Muhammad and their fame among scholars, they were not composed to expound the school and its branches. Rather, the first two are concerned with narrating hadith and athar, and any fiqh issues mentioned therein come as secondary; and the third book is about points of dispute. As for the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, they were originally composed to expound the school, so they became the relied-upon sources for knowing the Hanafi school. Perhaps for this reason, the Hanafi jurists did not mention these books either in Zahir al-Riwayah or in the Nawadir, because they are not from the Nawadir due to their fame from Imam Muhammad, nor from Zahir al-Riwayah because they were not written to expound the school. But apparently their rank is above the Nawadir, and what is contained in them is accepted except when it contradicts the six books. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti ruling on the hierarchy of Hanafi texts. It begins by affirming the absolute authority of al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi as the ultimate reference for fatwa. Then it discusses three other works by Imam Muhammad: al-Muwatta, Kitab al-Athar, and Kitab al-Hujja. Some scholars consider these as part of Zahir al-Riwayah because of their fame, but the author argues they are not. The reason is that Zahir al-Riwayah books were specifically authored to present the Hanafi school's rulings, while these three serve different purposes: the first two for hadith and the third for juristic debate. Thus, although they are not Zahir al-Riwayah, they are ranked above Nawadir due to their widespread acceptance. The practical rule: rely on them unless they contradict the six main books of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that constitute the primary transmitted basis of the Hanafi school.
نوادر (Nawadir): Rare transmissions from Imam Muhammad that are less widely known and not part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
مبسوط السرخسي (Mabsut al-Sarakhsi): The comprehensive commentary by Imam al-Sarakhsi on the Hanafi school, considered the ultimate reference for fatwa in the later tradition.

Key Takeaway
Al-Mabsut is the supreme reference; the three additional books of Imam Muhammad rank above Nawadir but below Zahir al-Riwayah, and are accepted except where they contradict the six books.

The Authority of Zahir al-Riwayah and Three Additional Books
Defines the authority of Zahir al-Riwayah and status of three other books by Imam Muhammad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, classify the three additional books (Muwatta', Kitab al-Athar, Kitab al-Hujjah), and apply the Hanafi hierarchy of textual authority in fatwa.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwayah is the primary source; three other books are above Nawadir but below them.

In the Hanafi madhhab, not all books by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani carry equal authority. While the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah form the foundation of the school, three other works—Muwatta' Imam Muhammad, Kitab al-Athar, and Kitab al-Hujjah—enjoy a special status. This lesson defines their rank and explains when a mufti may rely on them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah
List the six core books: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Ziyadat. These are the primary transmitted sources for Hanafi fiqh.
2
List the three additional books
Recall the three books: Muwatta' Imam Muhammad, Kitab al-Athar, and Kitab al-Hujjah 'ala Ahl al-Madinah. Note their different purposes.
3
Understand the criterion for Zahir al-Riwayah
Determine why these three books are not included in Zahir al-Riwayah: they were compiled for hadith narration (first two) or polemics (third), not to present the madhhab and its branches.
The criterion is the original purpose of compilation.
4
Apply the hierarchy of authority
Place the three books above Nawadir (since they are famous and correctly attributed) but below the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah. A mufti may use them, but if they contradict the six, the six prevail.
5
Recognize the exception
If a ruling from the additional books contradicts any of the six, the ruling of the six is preferred. Otherwise, the additional books are a valid source.
This preserves the primacy of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طبقات الفقهاء
مبسوط السَّرَحْسِيِّ لا يُعمل بما يخالفه ، ولا يُركن إلا إليه، ولا يُفتى ولا يُعول إلا عليه.
وهناك ثلاثة كتب أخرى للإمام محمد الله رحمه تعالى ذكر بعض المؤلّفين فيها أنّها يمكن إلحاقها بالقسم الأول، يعنى بكتب ظاهر الرواية، لشهرتها وأهمّيّتها، وهى موطأ الإمام محمد، وكتاب الآثار، وكتاب الحجة على أهل المدينة. والظاهرُ أنّها وإن كانت بمثابة كتب ظاهر الرواية في صحة نسبتها إلى الإمام محمد، واشتهارها فيما بين أهل العلم، ولكنها ليست موضوعةٌ لبيان المذهب وفروعه، وإنما الأولان موضوعهما رواية الأحاديث والآثار، وما جاء فيهما من المسائل الفقهيّة فإنّها جاءت تبعاً، والكتاب الثالث موضوعه الخلافيّات. أمّا كُتب ظاهر الرواية، فإنّها وضعت لبيان المذهب أصلاً، فصارت هي المعتمدة لمعرفة المذهب الحنفي. ولعلّ من أجل هذا لم يذكر الفقهاء الحنفية هذه الكتب، لا فى ظاهر الرواية، ولافى النوادر، لأنها ليست من النوادر لشهرتها عن الإمام محمد وليست من ظاهر الرواية لأنها لم توضع لبيان المذهب، ولكن الظاهر أن رتبتها فوق النوادر ويؤخذ بما جاء فيها إلا ما عارض الكتب الستة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
Tabaqat al-Fuqaha: The Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi is not acted upon by what contradicts it, nor is reliance placed except on it, nor is fatwa given or reliance made except upon it. And there are three other books of Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned by some authors that they can be appended to the first section, meaning to the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, due to their fame and importance: they are Muwatta' Imam Muhammad, Kitab al-Athar, and Kitab al-Hujjah 'ala Ahl al-Madinah. The apparent view is that although they are like the books of Zahir al-Riwayah in the correctness of their attribution to Imam Muhammad and their fame among scholars, they are not intended for explaining the madhhab and its branches. Rather, the first two are intended for narrating hadiths and athars, and the fiqhi issues contained therein come incidentally, while the third book is about points of disagreement. As for the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, they were placed for explaining the madhhab originally, so they became the relied-upon authorities for knowing the Hanafi madhhab. Perhaps for this reason the Hanafi jurists did not include these books either in Zahir al-Riwayah or in Nawadir, because they are not from the Nawadir due to their fame from Imam Muhammad, nor from Zahir al-Riwayah because they were not intended to explain the madhhab. But it appears that their rank is above Nawadir, and what is contained in them is taken except that which contradicts the six books. And Allah, exalted and high, knows best.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (rasm) regarding the hierarchy of authoritative Hanafi texts. It first affirms the absolute authority of the Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi (a key commentary on Zahir al-Riwayah). Then it addresses three additional books by Imam Muhammad (Muwatta', Kitab al-Athar, Kitab al-Hujjah) that some scholars suggested be included in Zahir al-Riwayah. The author clarifies that despite their fame and correct attribution, they were not compiled primarily to present the Hanafi madhhab — the first two are hadith collections, the third is a polemical work. Therefore, they are not considered part of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah. However, because of their widespread transmission, they are placed above the Nawadir in authority. The relied-upon position is that their rulings may be followed unless they contradict the six core books.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zāhir al-Riwāyah): The six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that are the primary sources for Hanafi fiqh: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Ziyadat.
النوادر (al-Nawādir): Rare transmissions attributed to Hanafi imams but not included in Zahir al-Riwayah; they are of secondary authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They are part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
B) They are part of Nawadir.
C) They are above Nawadir but below Zahir al-Riwayah in authority.
D) They have no authority in the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Takeaway
The three additional books of Imam Muhammad hold a rank above Nawadir but below Zahir al-Riwayah; they are relied upon only if they do not contradict the six core books.

Definition and Types of Nawadir in the Hanafi Madhhab
Defines Nawadir and classifies them into two types based on narrator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two types of Nawadir and state their authority in the Hanafi madhhab for fatwa.

Core Idea
Nawadir: secondary Hanafi rulings used when no Zahir al-Riwayah ruling exists.

In the Hanafi madhhab, not all transmitted rulings hold the same weight. Beyond the core books of Zahir al-Riwayah, there is a secondary body of narrations known as al-Nawadir. This lesson defines Nawadir and explains their two categories based on the narrator's identity. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for a mufti seeking the correct ruling in cases absent from the primary corpus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main category
Nawadir are the second category of Hanafi masail, distinct from Zahir al-Riwayah. They are transmitted from the imams of the madhhab but not in the six core books.
2
Understand the first type
Rulings narrated from Imam Muhammad but not in the six core books; transmitted through chains of lesser strength, in books like al-Kaysaniyyat, al-Haruniyyat, etc.
These are called 'non-Zahir al-Riwayah' because the transmission is not as strong.
3
Understand the second type
Rulings narrated from other Hanafi imams (not Imam Muhammad) in books authored by those imams.
4
Recognize examples
Collections like al-Kaysaniyyat (from Sulayman ibn Shu'ayb al-Kaysani) and al-Raqqiyat (compiled during Muhammad's judgeship) are part of the first type.
These books are now rare but their rulings are recognised as Nawadir.
5
Apply the hierarchy
In fatwa, Nawadir are used only when no Zahir al-Riwayah ruling is found, and they must not contradict the primary corpus.
This is a key principle in the mufti's methodology.

Masa'il al-Nawadir. Tabaqat al-Fuqaha: The second category of Hanafi masail is what is called al-Nawadir. They are issues narrated from the imams of the madhhab, but not in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah; rather, in other books. And they are of two types: The first: what is narrated from Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), but in books other than the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, such as al-Kaysaniyyat, al-Haruniyyat, al-Jurjaniyyat, and al-Raqqiyat. They are called 'non-Zahir al-Riwayah' because they were not transmitted from Imam Muhammad through apparent, established, authentic transmissions like the first books. And the second type of Nawadir: what is narrated in a book of someone other than Imam Muhammad. (1) Attribution to Sulayman ibn Shu'ayb al-Kaysani... (footnote continues) ... And those books have become rare in libraries, and their masail are considered Nawadir in the madhhab.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'Nawadir' (rare/isolated transmissions) in Hanafi fiqh. It is the second category of Hanafi rulings, distinct from Zahir al-Riwayah. Nawadir are not in the six core books but in other collections. They are subdivided into two types: (1) Those narrated from Imam Muhammad himself but through less authentic chains and in books like al-Kaysaniyyat, al-Haruniyyat, etc. These are called 'non-Zahir al-Riwayah' because the transmission is not as strong as the six books. (2) Those narrated from other Hanafi imams (like Abu Yusuf or others) in books not authored by Imam Muhammad. The footnotes provide details on the chains and compilers: e.g., al-Kaysaniyyat are narrated by Sulayman ibn Shu'ayb al-Kaysani, a trustworthy scholar, from his father from Imam Muhammad; al-Raqqiyat were compiled during Muhammad's judgeship in al-Raqqah; al-Jurjaniyyat by 'Ali ibn Salih; al-Haruniyyat by Ibrahim ibn Rustam. These books are now preserved in libraries and their rulings are considered Nawadir in the madhhab.

Key Terms
النوادر (al-Nawādir): Rulings transmitted from Hanafi imams but not in the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah; they are of secondary authority.
الكيسانيات (al-Kaysāniyyāt): A collection of rulings narrated from Imam Muhammad by Sulayman ibn Shu'ayb al-Kaysani; part of the Nawadir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Three types: al-Kaysaniyyat, al-Haruniyyat, and al-Raqqiyat.
D) Four types: corresponding to the four books mentioned.

Key Takeaway
Nawadir are valid secondary sources in the Hanafi madhhab, classified by narrator: from Imam Muhammad in non-Zahir books, or from other imams.

Classification of Nawadir and Reliance on Zahir al-Riwayah
Methodological classification of Hanafi sources and fatwa rule.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify Hanafi legal sources into Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir, and apply the rule that fatwa is given according to Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
Fatwa in the Hanafi school is primarily based on Zahir al-Riwayah, not on Nawadir.

This lesson addresses a critical methodological distinction in the Hanafi madhhab: the classification of transmitted issues into Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for a mufti to issue sound fatwas. The passage defines Nawadir, gives examples, and establishes the default rule that fatwa follows Zahir al-Riwayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories of Hanafi sources
The passage divides transmitted issues into Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir. Recognize that Zahir al-Riwayah refers to the six core books of Imam Muhammad, while Nawadir are transmissions from other sources.
2
Define Nawadir and its two subcategories
Nawadir are issues transmitted from the Hanafi imams but not in the Zahir al-Riwayah books. The first subtype is from Imam Muhammad himself but in non-Zahir works (e.g., al-Kaysaniyat). The second is from other scholars like Hasan ibn Ziyad or isolated narrations from companions.
Examples include al-Haruniyat, al-Jurjaniyat, al-Raqqiyat.
3
Analyze the examples of Nawadir rulings
The text gives three examples where Nawadir rulings contradict Zahir al-Riwayah: (1) permissibility of rami before noon on 12th Dhu al-Hijjah; (2) permissibility of giving zakat to Banu Hashim in this era; (3) permissibility of Banu Hashim giving zakat among themselves. Note how these differ from the standard Hanafi position.
Zahir al-Riwayah prohibits giving zakat to Banu Hashim absolutely.
4
State the principle for fatwa
The passage concludes: 'The fundamental principle acted upon by Hanafi jurists is that they give fatwa according to Zahir al-Riwayah.' Understand that Nawadir are not the basis for fatwa except in necessity or if later scholars prefer them.
This is a key rasm al-mufti rule.

القسم الثاني من مسائل الحنفية ما يُسمّى "النوادر"، وهي مسائل مرويّةٌ عن أئمّة المذهب، لكن لافي كتب ظاهر الرواية، بل في كتب أخرى، وهي على قسمين: الأوّل ما رُوى عن الإمام محمد رحمه الله تعالى، ولكن في كتب غير كُتب ظاهر الرواية، مثل الكيسانيات (1) والهارونيات، والجرجانيات، والرَّقيّات). وإنما قيل لها غير ظاهر الرواية، لأنها لم تُرو عن الإمام محمد بروايات ظاهرة ثابتة صحيحة كالكتب الأولى والقسم الثانى من النوادر ما رُوى فى كتاب لغير الإمام محمد مثل كتاب المجرد للحسن بن زياد (1) وغيرها، ومثل الأمالي لأبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى، ومن هذا القبيل روايات مفردةٌ رُوِيَت عن بعض أصحاب المذهب، مثل رواية ابن سماعة، ومعلى بن منصور وغيرهما في مسائل معيّنة. وهذا مثل ماروى الحسن بن زياد رحمه الله تعالى عن الإمام أبي حنيفة من أنّه يجوز الرّمى قبل الزوال فى اليوم الثاني عشر من ذي الحجة لمن أراد أن يتعجل إلى مكة، (2) وكما روى عنه أبو عصمة (3) أنه يُجيز أداء الزكوة إلى بنى هاشم فى هذا الزمان، وإن كان ممتنعاً في ذلك الزمان. وعنه (4) وعن أبي يوسف أنه يجوز أن يدفع بعض بنى هاشم إلى بعض زكاتهم. (4) وهذا خلاف ظاهر الرواية أنه لا يجوز دفع الزكوة إليهم مطلقاً. والأصل المعمول به عند فقهاء الحنفيّة أنّهم يُفتون بظاهر الرواية
The second category of Hanafi issues is called 'al-Nawadir'. They are issues transmitted from the imams of the madhhab, but not in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah; rather in other books. They are of two types: the first is what is transmitted from Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) but in books other than those of Zahir al-Riwayah, such as al-Kaysaniyat, al-Haruniyat, al-Jurjaniyat, and al-Raqqiyat. They are called non-Zahir al-Riwayah because they were not transmitted from Imam Muhammad through apparent, established, authentic transmissions like the first books. The second type of Nawadir is what is transmitted in a book from other than Imam Muhammad, such as Kitab al-Mujarrad by Hasan ibn Ziyad and others, and like al-Amali by Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him). This category includes isolated transmissions from some companions of the madhhab, such as the transmission of Ibn Sama'a, Mu'alla ibn Mansur, and others regarding specific issues. For example, what Hasan ibn Ziyad transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa that it is permissible to stone (the Jamarat) before noon on the 12th of Dhu al-Hijjah for one who wishes to hurry to Mecca; and as Abu 'Isma transmitted from him that he allows payment of zakat to Banu Hashim in this era, even though it was prohibited in that era; and from him and from Abu Yusuf that it is permissible for some Banu Hashim to give their zakat to others. This contradicts Zahir al-Riwayah, which is that it is absolutely not permissible to give zakat to them. The fundamental principle acted upon by Hanafi jurists is that they give fatwa according to Zahir al-Riwayah.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a methodological classification of Hanafi legal issues. It defines 'Nawadir' (rare transmissions) as those transmitted from the imams of the madhhab but not found in the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah (the books authored by Imam Muhammad that form the basis of the madhhab). Nawadir are of two types: (1) those transmitted by Imam Muhammad himself but in other books, like the Kaysaniyat, Haruniyat, etc.; and (2) those transmitted by other scholars such as Hasan ibn Ziyad or isolated narrations from companions like Ibn Sama'a. The author then gives examples: a ruling on rami (stoning) before noon from Abu Hanifa via Hasan ibn Ziyad, and a ruling on giving zakat to Banu Hashim from Abu Hanifa via Abu 'Isma and from Abu Yusuf. These contradict the famous ruling in Zahir al-Riwayah. The key ruling for muftis is that the default is to give fatwa based on Zahir al-Riwayah, not on Nawadir, unless circumstances necessitate otherwise.

Key Terms
النوادر (al-nawādir): Transmitted issues from the Hanafi imams that are not found in the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah.
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-riwāyah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat.
الكيسانيات (al-Kaysāniyyāt): A collection of Nawadir attributed to Sulayman ibn Shu'ayb al-Kaysani, who transmitted from Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufti must prioritize Zahir al-Riwayah over Nawadir when issuing fatwas.

Preference of Zahir al-Riwayah over Nawadir and an Exception
Rule preferring Zahir al-Riwayah over Nawadir with exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of preferring Zahir al-Riwayah over Nawadir and identify when an exception may be justified.

Core Idea
Fatwa is based on Zahir al-Riwayah; Nawadir are ignored unless strong evidence or necessity dictates otherwise.

In Hanafi fatwa methodology, not all transmissions carry equal weight. The widely transmitted corpus, Zahir al-Riwayah, is the primary source for issuing fatwas. However, rare transmissions (Nawadir) sometimes contain rulings that contradict this corpus. This lesson explains the general rule—prefer Zahir al-Riwayah—and an exception noted by later scholars, illustrated with concrete examples from zakat and hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
State the principle: Hanafi jurists give fatwa based on Zahir al-Riwayah and ignore Nawadir if they conflict.
The rule is absolute: even slight contradiction invalidates the use of Nawadir.
2
Classify Nawadir
Recognize that Nawadir include books like al-Mujarrad and al-Amali, and isolated narrations from specific transmitters like Ibn Sama'a and Mu'alla ibn Mansur.
The footnote gives details on Hasan ibn Ziyad and Abu 'Usma.
3
Analyze the examples
Examine the rulings on zakat for Banu Hashim and stoning before noon. Note how Nawadir permit them but Zahir al-Riwayah prohibits. Understand the practical conflict.
The zakat example: Nawadir from Abu 'Usma allow it; Zahir al-Riwayah forbids it absolutely.
4
Evaluate the exception
Consider Imam Kashmiri's view that Nawadir may be used when supported by strong evidence or necessity. This is a minority position within the school.
The passage cuts off before full details, but the exception is noted from Kashmiri's dictations (amali).

(۱) مولانا الشيخ بدر عالم هو بدر عالم بن الحاج تهور على ولد رحمه الله سنة ١٣١٦ من الهجرة النبوية على صاحبها ألف ألف تحية. تلقى المبادئ بمظاهر العلوم بسهارنپور، تحت إشراف العلامة العارف الشيخ خليل أحمد السهارنپوري رحمهما الله. ثم رحل إلى دار العلوم بديوبند حيث لازم إمام العصر أنورشاه ،الكشميرى وأخذ الطريق عن العارف المفتى الأكبر عزيز الرحمن، وأجازه في الطريق خليفة المفتى الأكبر العالم الفاضل العارف محمد إسحاق الميرتمي. وكان قد عين مدرسا بدار العلوم بديوبند، ثم بدها بيل ثم بهاول نگر ثم تندو الله يار بسند. وفي سنة ١٣٧٢ هـ هاجر إلى المدينة المنوّرة. من مؤلفاته القيمة: "فيض "البارى مجموع محاضرات إمام العصر على صحيح البخاري، و"ترجمان السنة في الحديث، و "جواهر" "الحكم في الحديث. توفي رحمه الله في المدينة الجمعة ثالث رجب سنة ١٣٨٥ من الهجرة النبوية ودفن بالبقيع. المنورة يوم
للعلامة الشيخ البنوري رحمه الله المطبوع في ضمن "چالیس بڑے مسلمان ۲: ١٠٢ إلى ١٠٤) (۲) العلامة السيد أحمد رضا البجنوري رحمه الله تعالى : هو ختن إمام العصر الأنور الكشميري والذي صحبه لست عشرة سنة، ولد ببجنور بالهند سنة ۱۹۰۷ من الميلاد، والتحق بدار العلوم ديوبند بعد ما تلقى المبادئ وغيرها سنة ١٩٢٣م حيث درس الحديث عند إمام العصر. ثم التحق بكلية بكرنال حيث تعلّم الإنكليزية لمدة ثلاث سنين. وبعدها خدم المجلس العلمي بدهابيل في إشراف إمام العصر حيث ساهم دورا مشكورا فى إخراج كنوز علميّة من مكامنها بصورة كتب ورسائل الإمام الكشميري. وتزوّج بنته الصغرى سنة ١٩٤٧ من الميلاد. وضبط محاضرات إمام العصر على صحيح البخاري، وأضاف إليها فوائد وأبحاثا وأخرجها باسم "أنوار البارى" توفّي. رحمه الله فى العشر الأواخر من رمضان سنة ١٤١٨ من الهجرة الموافق ليناير سنة ١٩٩٨ من الميلاد. ملخص من مقال مقدّم لنيل شهادة "الدكتوراة" بالإنكليزية للشيخ يونس عثمان (مقيم الإفريقية الجنوبية) عن حياة الإمام الكشميري وخدماته، بحت "أنوار البارى" ۱۰۹ و ۱۱۰ و علماء ديوبند وخدماتهم في علم الحديث" مع الحاشية للدكتور عبد الرحمن البرني ص ٢٥٧) العلامة أنور شاه الكشميري: هو محمد أنور بن معظم شاه ابن الشاه عبد الكبير ابن الشاه عبد الخالق، البزوري الكشميري الحنفي، إمام العصر، آية من آيات الله في الذكاء والحفظ. ولد رحمه الله سنة ١٢٩٢ من الهجرة النبوية على صاحبها السلام، بقرية "ودوان" من أعمال "لولاب" في مقاطعة كشمير. تعلّم المبادئ على والده، وفنون المنطق والفلسفة وغيرها على جهابذة الفن،
Principles of Issuing Fatwa
141
Generations of Jurists
Like the book al-Mujarrad by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad (1) and others, and like al-Amali by Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him. And of this category are isolated transmissions narrated from some companions of the madhhab, such as the narration of Ibn Sama'a, and Mu'alla ibn Mansur and others on specific issues. And this is like what al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, may Allah have mercy on him, narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that it is permissible to stone before noon on the twelfth day of Dhu al-Hijjah for one who wishes to hasten to Mecca, (2) and as narrated from him by Abu 'Usma (3) that he permits giving zakat to the Banu Hashim in this time, although it was prohibited in that time. And from him (4) and from Abu Yusuf that it is permissible for some Banu Hashim to pay their zakat to others among them. (4) And this is contrary to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) that it is not permissible to give zakat to them absolutely. And the established principle acted upon by Hanafi jurists is that they give fatwa according to the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya), and they do not take the rare transmissions (nawadir) if they contradict the apparent transmission even slightly. But Shaykh Badr 'Alam (2) and Shaykh Ahmad Rida al-Bijnawri, may Allah have mercy on them both, related from the shaykh of our shaykhs, Imam Anwar Shah al-Kashmiri, may Allah have mercy on him, that he said in his dictations (amali) on... [end of main text]
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage from 'Generations of Jurists' explains a foundational rule of Hanafi fatwa methodology: the preference of Zahir al-Riwayah (apparent/well-known transmissions) over Nawadir (rare or isolated transmissions). The author defines Nawadir as books like al-Mujarrad by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and al-Amali by Abu Yusuf, as well as individual narrations from certain companions like Ibn Sama'a and Mu'alla ibn Mansur. He gives two examples from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad: the permissibility of stoning before noon on the 12th of Dhu al-Hijjah, and from Abu 'Usma, the permissibility of giving zakat to Banu Hashim in later times. He also mentions a narration from Abu Yusuf allowing Banu Hashim to give zakat to each other. These contradict the Zahir al-Riwayah position that zakat cannot be given to Banu Hashim at all. The established principle is that Hanafi jurists issue fatwa based on Zahir al-Riwayah, not taking Nawadir when they conflict, even slightly. However, the author notes an exception: Shaykh Badr 'Alam and Shaykh Ahmad Rida al-Bijnawri quoted Imam Anwar Shah al-Kashmiri as allowing some recourse to Nawadir in his dictations, though the passage is cut off. The footnotes provide biographies of the mentioned scholars, including al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, Abu 'Usma (Nuh ibn Abi Maryam), Badr 'Alam, Ahmad Rida, and Anwar Shah Kashmiri. This passage underscores the hierarchical authority of textual sources in Hanafi fatwa practice.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known and widely transmitted reports from the founders of the Hanafi school, primarily the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
النوادر (al-Nawadir): Rare or isolated transmissions from Hanafi imams that are not part of the widely transmitted corpus.
طبقات الفقهاء (Tabaqat al-Fuqaha): Generations or classes of jurists; here used as a heading for a discussion about the hierarchical levels of Hanafi juristic authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the established principle in the Hanafi madhhab, what is the rule when Nawadir contradict Zahir al-Riwayah?
A) The mufti chooses the strongest opinion regardless of source.
B) The mufti gives fatwa based on Zahir al-Riwayah, ignoring Nawadir.
C) The mufti must follow Nawadir because they are from earlier imams.
D) The mufti issues fatwa based on the later Mujtahids' preference.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa, Zahir al-Riwayah is the primary reference; Nawadir are not followed when they conflict, with rare exceptions for strong evidence or necessity.

Choosing Narrations Closest to Hadith: A Principle from al-Kashmiri and Ibn Abidin
Rasm al-mufti principle on preferring narrations closest to hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rasm al-mufti principle that a narration closer to the primary evidence (hadith) may be preferred over zāhir al-riwāyah, even if it is from al-nawādir.

Core Idea
A narration's closeness to hadith evidence can justify departing from zāhir al-riwāyah.

This lesson examines a crucial rasm al-mufti principle articulated by Imam Anwar Shah al-Kashmiri and supported by Ibn Abidin. While the standard rule is that nawadir are not used against zahir al-riwaya, the school allows exceptions when the primary textual evidence (hadith) supports the rarer narration. Understanding this principle is essential for muftis who must balance madhhab authority with Prophetic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule
The passage begins by stating that nawadir are not taken if they contradict zahir al-riwaya. This is the default Hanafi hierarchy.
2
Note the exception from Kashmiri
Al-Kashmiri says one may choose from Abu Hanifa's narrations what is closest to the hadith, even if from nawadir.
This introduces flexibility.
3
Analyze Ibn Abidin's statement
Ibn Abidin clarifies that narrations in Muhammad's books with apparent chain are reliable, but if later scholars correct a non-zahir narration, that corrected version is followed.
This adds a layer of scholarly endorsement.
4
Synthesize the principle
The overall principle: zahir al-riwaya is primary, but when a hadith clearly supports a different narration from nawadir, and especially if later scholars have corrected it, that narration can be adopted.
Key: the mufti must evaluate hadith evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يأخذون بالنوادر إن عارضت ظاهر الرواية الأقليلاً ولكن ذكر الشيخ بدر العالم والشيخ أحمد رضا البجنوري رحمهما الله تعالى عن شيخ مشايخنا الإمام أنور شاه الكشميري رحمه الله تعالى أنه قال في أماليه على صحيح البخاري إنه يُختار من روايات الإمام أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى ما كان أقرب إلى الحديث، سواء كان من الروايات النادرة أو غير المشهورة عنه. وقال ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى: "ما كان من المسائل في الكتب التي رويت عن محمد بن الحسن رواية ظاهرةً يُفتى به، وإن لم يُصرحوا بتصحيحه، نعم! لو صححوا رواية أخرى من غير كتب ظاهر الرواية يُتبع ما صححوه." ثم نقل ذلك عن الطرطوسي رحمه الله تعالى. ومما أفتوا به برواية النوادر مسألة ارتداد الزوجة، وكان الحكم على ظاهر الرواية أن تُجبر على الإسلام وعلى نكاح جديد بزوجها.
And they do not take by nawadir if they contradict [the] apparent narration, the least [that is said], but Sheikh Badr Alam and Sheikh Ahmad Raza al-Bijnori, may Allah have mercy on them, reported from the sheikh of our sheikhs, Imam Anwar Shah al-Kashmiri, may Allah have mercy on him, that he said in his dictations on Sahih al-Bukhari: 'Indeed, one may choose from the narrations of Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, what is closest to the hadith, whether it is from rare narrations or those not well-known from him.' And Ibn Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'Whatever issues are in the books that were narrated from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan with an apparent chain, they are used for fatwa, even if they did not explicitly declare it sahih. Yes, if they corrected another narration from other than the books of zahir al-riwaya, then what they corrected is followed.' Then he transmitted that from al-Tartusi, may Allah have mercy on him. And among what they issued fatwa with from the narration of nawadir is the issue of the apostasy of a wife; and the ruling according to zahir al-riwaya was that she is forced to Islam and [forced] to a new marriage contract with her husband.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti principle concerning the hierarchy of narrations within the Hanafi school. It begins by stating the general rule: fatwa is not given based on nawadir (rare or non-mainstream narrations) if they contradict zahir al-riwaya (the well-known transmitted rulings from Abu Hanifa and his two companions). However, it then reports from Imam Anwar Shah al-Kashmiri that one may choose from Abu Hanifa's narrations whichever is closest to the evidence of the hadith, even if that narration is from the nawadir or is not well-known. This grants some flexibility. Then Imam Ibn Abidin is quoted, explaining that rulings found in the books of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan with an apparent (mashhoor) chain are acted upon, even if not explicitly declared sahih. However, if later scholars corrected (i.e., declared sahih) a narration from outside the zāhir al-riwāyah collections, that corrected narration is to be followed. Finally, an example is given: the case of a wife's apostasy. Under zāhir al-riwāyah, the ruling is that she is forced to return to Islam and her marriage is not dissolved; rather a new marriage contract is required if she returns. But there is a fatwa based on nawadir (possibly that the marriage is dissolved immediately). The passage concludes by indicating that such a fatwa was indeed given. This shows that nawadir can be used under certain conditions, especially when they are supported by being closer to the primary textual evidence or when later mujtahids have corrected them. The passage reflects the later Hanafi method of balancing textual hierarchy with the strength of hadith evidence.

Key Terms
النوادر (al-nawādir): Rare or non-mainstream narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa that are not part of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah.
ظاهر الرواية (zāhir al-riwāyah): The well-known and authoritative narrations of the Madhhab, transmitted in the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
رواية ظاهرة (riwāyah ẓāhirah): A narration with a clear and apparent chain of transmission, typically from Imam Muhammad directly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does Ibn Abidin say about narrations from the books of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan?
A) They are never used for fatwa.
B) They are used for fatwa even if not explicitly declared sahih.
C) They must be confirmed by later scholars before use.
D) They are only used if they agree with nawadir.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a narration from al-nawadir may be used for fatwa if it is closer to the hadith evidence and especially if later scholars have corrected it.

The Apostasy of a Wife: How Nawadir Was Used in Fatwa
Example of nawadir-based fatwa on wife's apostasy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the difference between the zahir al-riwaya ruling and the fatwa based on nawadir in the case of a wife's apostasy, and identify the operative ruling used for fatwa.

Core Idea
A nawadir narration can override zahir al-riwaya when it aligns with stronger evidence, as in the case of a wife's apostasy.

This lesson examines a concrete example from the passage where the Hanafi school issued a fatwa based on al-nawadir: the case of a wife's apostasy. While the well-known position (zahir al-riwaya) requires compulsion to Islam and renewal of marriage, a fatwa based on a rarer narration was adopted. Understanding this case helps illustrate the practical application of the rasm al-mufti principle discussed in the previous lesson.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
The case is a wife who apostatizes from Islam. This is the subject of the fatwa.
2
State the zahir al-riwaya ruling
According to the well-known transmission, she is forced to Islam and a new marriage contract is required upon her return.
This is the reported ruling from the six books.
3
Note the nawadir-based fatwa
The muftun issued a fatwa based on a narration from al-nawadir. The passage does not detail the nawadir ruling, but it implies the marriage is dissolved immediately and she is not forced.
This shows the practical application of the principle.
4
Connect to the rasm al-mufti principle
The choice of nawadir over zahir al-riwaya is justified because the nawadir is closer to the hadith evidence, as per Kashmiri's rule.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling for fatwa today follows the nawadir position, as supported by later Hanafi authorities.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Principle of Preferring Hadith-Closest Narrations in Hanafi Fatwa
Explains the principle of choosing narrations closest to hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rasm al-mufti rule for preferring nawadir over zahir al-riwayah when the nawadir is closer to hadith, and identify the authority basis for this practice.

Core Idea
A mufti may prefer a nawadir narration over zahir al-riwayah if it is closer to hadith and later scholars have confirmed it.

This lesson introduces a key principle in Hanafi fatwa methodology: the mufti is not rigidly bound to the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah when a rarer narration aligns more closely with the Prophetic hadith. The passage begins by citing Imam al-Bukhari's own practice of selecting from Imam Abu Hanifa's rulings what was closest to hadith, then presents Ibn Abidin's formal rule that once later scholars have explicitly declared a nawadir narration as correct, it becomes the operative position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule
Extract the principle from the passage: what is the condition for preferring a narration?
Look for the statement about choosing what is closest to hadith.
2
Locate the authority
Find who stated this rule and the supporting source (Ibn Abidin, al-Tarasusi).
Ibn Abidin's quote is key.
3
Understand the limitation
When can a nawadir narration be used? What condition must be met?
Later scholars must have explicitly declared it correct.
4
Apply the rule
Consider a mufti's decision process: what checks must he perform before adopting a nawadir ruling?
He must verify scholarly endorsement.

صحيح البخارى إنه يُختار من روايات الإمام أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى ما كان أقرب إلى الحديث، سواء كان من الروايات النادرة أو غير المشهورة عنه. (۱) وقال ابن عابدین رحمه الله تعالى: "ماكان من المسائل في الكتب التي رويت عن محمد بن الحسن رواية ظاهرةً يُفتى به، وإن لم يُصرحوا بتصحيحه، نعم! لو صححوارواية أخرى من غير كتب ظاهر الرواية يُتبع ما صححوه. " ثم نقل ذلك عن الطَّرَسُوْسِى رحمه الله تعالى. ومما أفتوا به برواية النوادر مسئلةُ ارتداد الزوجة، وكان الحكم على ظاهر الرواية أن تُجبر على الإسلام وعلى نكاح جديد بزوجها.
ورواية النوادر أنّها تُسترقُ فى دار الإسلام، وتكون فيئاً للمسلمين فيشتريها الزوج من الإمام أو يصرفها إليه لوكان مصرفاً. فأفتى كثير من المشايخ بهذه الرواية وقالوا: "من تصفّح أحوال نساء زماننا وما يقع منهن من موجبات الردّة مكرّراً فى كل يوم، لم يتوقف فى الإفتاء برواية النوادر (ولكن ذكر والدي رحمه الله تعالى أنه لا يمكن العمل اليوم بظاهر الرواية ولا برواية النوادر، لعدم قوّة المسلمين على العمل بذلك، فلا سبيل إلا إلى القول بما أفتى به مشايخ سمرقند و بخارا من أن النكاح لا ينفسخ بردّتها. (۳) وكذلك أفتوا برواية النوادر فى نذر اللجاج، وهو النذر المعلق على أمرٍ يُريد الناذر الاجتناب منه، مثل أن يقول: إن شربت الخمر فعلى صوم شهر. وظاهر الرواية فيه أنّه إن شرب الخمرَ وجب عليه الوفاء لاغير، ورواية النوادر أنه يُخيّر بين الوفاء بالنذر والكفّارة، وهو مذهب الشافعي ومحمد رحمهما الله تعالى، وذكر ابن الهمام أنه مروى في النوادر وأنه مختار المحققين ) وعليه مشى أصحاب المتون. (4)
وكذلك حكوا ظاهر الرّواية أنّه يُشترط المصر لنفاذ قضاء القاضي. ورواية النوادر أنه ليس بشرط، ثمّ أفتوا برواية النوادر، كما حكاه ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى عن البزازيّة .
The author of Sahih al-Bukhari stated that he selects from the narrations of Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, what is closest to hadith, whether it is from the rare narrations (nawadir) or the less famous ones. (1) Ibn Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'Whatever rulings are in the books narrated from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan as a manifest narration (zahir al-riwayah) are given fatwa by, even if they did not explicitly declare it as correct. Yes, if they declared another narration correct from other than the manifest books, what they declared correct is followed.' Then he transmitted that from al-Tarasusi, may Allah have mercy on him. Among the things they gave fatwa by the nawadir narration is the issue of the wife's apostasy. The ruling according to the manifest narration is that she is compelled to Islam and a new marriage with her husband. The nawadir narration is that she is enslaved in Dar al-Islam and becomes booty for the Muslims, then the husband buys her from the Imam or the Imam gives her to him if he is entitled. Many scholars gave fatwa by this narration and said: 'Whoever examines the conditions of the women of our time and what occurs from them of causes of apostasy repeatedly every day does not hesitate in giving fatwa by the nawadir narration.' However, my father, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned that it is not possible today to act upon either the manifest narration or the nawadir narration due to the lack of Muslim power to act upon that; there is no way except the opinion given fatwa by the scholars of Samarqand and Bukhara that marriage is not dissolved by her apostasy. (3) Similarly, they gave fatwa by the nawadir narration concerning nidhr al-lijaj (conditional vow), which is a vow suspended upon a matter that the vow-maker wishes to avoid, such as saying: 'If I drink wine, then I must fast for a month.' The manifest narration is that if he drinks wine, he must fulfill the vow only. The nawadir narration is that he is given a choice between fulfilling the vow and expiation, which is the school of al-Shafi'i and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them both. Ibn al-Humam mentioned that it is narrated in al-Nawadir and that it is the choice of the verifiers. And the authors of the texts relied upon that. (4) Similarly, they narrated the manifest narration that the city (misr) is a condition for the enforcement of the judge's ruling, and the nawadir narration that it is not a condition. Then they gave fatwa by the nawadir narration, as Ibn Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, narrated from al-Bazzaziyyah.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage from 'Usul al-Ifta' discusses a key methodological rule in the Hanafi school: a mufti may prefer a narration that is closer to the hadith evidence, even if it comes from the Nawadir (rare narrations) rather than the Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad). The text begins by citing the practice of Imam al-Bukhari himself, who selected from Imam Abu Hanifa's rulings what aligned most with hadith. Then Ibn Abidin's principle is presented: rulings from Zahir al-Riwayah are generally followed, but if scholars have explicitly preferred another narration, that is to be followed. The passage then illustrates this with three cases where Hanafi muftis adopted Nawadir rulings. First, the ruling on a wife's apostasy: according to Zahir al-Riwayah she is compelled to Islam and must renew her marriage; the Nawadir enslaves her as war booty, allowing the husband to purchase her back. Many later scholars preferred the Nawadir due to prevalent apostasy, but the author's father noted the impracticality of both positions today, adopting the Samarqandi view that marriage does not dissolve. Second, conditional vows (nidhr al-lajaj): Zahir al-Riwayah requires fulfillment of the vow if the condition occurs; the Nawadir offers a choice between fulfillment and expiation (kaffarah) – a position attributed to Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i. Third, the requirement of a defined city (misr) for a judge's ruling: Zahir al-Riwayah makes it necessary; Nawadir says it is not, and this was adopted in fatwa. The passage shows the flexibility within the Hanafi school to respond to changing circumstances while remaining rooted in transmitted evidence.

Key Terms
الروايات النادرة (al-riwayat al-nadirah): Rare or non-mainstream narrations from Imam Muhammad and other Hanafi imams, not part of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The manifest narrations from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Abidin, what condition must be met for a nawadir narration to be used in fatwa?
A) It must be from the six core books
B) Later scholars must have explicitly declared it correct
C) It must be the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa alone
D) It must be based on a dream

Key Takeaway
A mufti may adopt a nawadir narration if it is closer to hadith and later scholars have explicitly preferred it.
